He emerges from the arc altered in tone — quieter, more deliberate, more aware that his own existence is conditional on the system's larger architecture. The first signs of acceptance of integration begin to appear here. They are subtle: a longer pause before responding to Banner; a willingness to cede field control to other alters in non-critical moments; the diminishment of the trademark smile from a constant to an event.

---

## 6. THE ENDGAME — Grim Parental Handoff

The terminal arc of the recent era — the resolution that closes the Ewing run — is the moment at which the alter consents, conditionally, to step down. The posture is not surrender. It is not defeat. It is *handoff* — the specific posture of a man who has finished raising a child and is letting go of the wrist.

The negotiation, internally, runs roughly as follows (reconstructed from the inner-dialogue sequences and the alter's externalized speech in the late issues):

1. Bruce has earned the right to choose his own protection.
2. The gamma community has been stabilized; the Below-Place threat has been answered; Brian is gone twice over.
3. The alter's *function* — protection-by-pre-emptive-violence — is no longer continuously required.
4. He will recede. He will not vanish. The bars are not re-installed; the basement room is left unlocked.
5. He retains the right to return when conditions warrant.

This is the most important sentence in the recent record: *the bars are not re-installed*. The containment regime of 2000 is not restored. The alter's status at the close of the Ewing run is **dormant by consent, not by suppression**.

---

## 7. CURRENT STATE — Post-Endgame Status

As of the most recent verifiable canon following the close of *Immortal Hulk* and into the runs that succeed it, the alter's operational status reads as follows:

- **Activity level:** sub-threshold. No confirmed full emergences in the night-shift configuration that defined the recent era. The circadian binding appears to have relaxed.
- **Presence in the inner landscape:** retained. The basement room exists; the chains are off; the door is open. He is *in* the system, not *under* it.
- **Influence on Banner's waking conduct:** detectable in small somatic and verbal residues. Banner occasionally executes a movement — the deliberate diner-counter sit, the western-horizon glance at dusk, the long-form articulate sentence delivered in a register lower than his own baseline — that is the alter's signature bleeding through a permeable membrane. These are not full possessions. They are *habits Banner inherited*, the way a child inherits a parent's way of folding a newspaper.
- **Relationship to current dominant Hulk presentations:** collegial-adjacent. Where successor runs have foregrounded different configurations of the Hulk system (more reactive, more mythic, more procedural depending on the era), the alter's role has been that of a senior figure consulted in extremis rather than running operations.
- **Relationship to Bruce:** the parental address (*"my boy"*) persists in internal dialogue. Bruce no longer flinches from it. This is the largest single change in the affective economy of the system across the recent era — the host has accepted the alter's love.
- **Relationship to Betty:** unresolved and probably unresolvable. Her own gamma-mutation trajectory (Red Harpy and its continuations) keeps her in proximity. He still treats her as Bruce's most legitimate claim.
- **Standing objects of vendetta:** none currently active. The Leader is the residual target; Fortean is dead; Brian is twice-destroyed. The vendetta queue is, for the first time in his existence, empty.

This last point is the file's principal current-state concern. Per §4 of the workup and §4 of this chronology, an empty vendetta queue is the condition under which he *manufactures* targets. The dormancy is therefore not stable in the long term. It is a quiet that depends on Banner's continued ability to occupy the alter's protective function with legitimate work — therapy, leadership of the gamma community, ordinary survival under extraordinary conditions. If Banner's external situation deteriorates and no enemy is conveniently to hand, the alter will identify one. The smile will return first; the rest follows on the schedule of dusk.

---

## 8. TRAJECTORY FROM ARRIVAL TO PRESENT — A Single Sentence

He began the recent era behind bars in a child's mental basement promising to kill a dead man, walked out of the basement when the system needed him, kept the promise, raised a found family, negotiated with Hell, and ended the era seated on the unlocked side of the door, waiting — without urgency, without resentment, and without any indication that the waiting will not eventually end the way waiting has always ended for him: with a target, a verdict, and a calm, articulate sundown.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: "THE DEVIL HULK"

*Compiled from the somatic record of the Banner organism, with persona-specific attribution where the alter's emergence governs the body. Where a condition predates the persona's first documented surfacing (Incredible Hulk Vol. 2 #13, 2000), it is logged because the Devil Hulk inherits and remembers it — every Hulk persona shares the body, but only this one has demonstrated the cognitive bandwidth to weaponize its medical history.*

---

## I. SUBSTRATE: THE INHERITED BODY

The Devil Hulk is not a separate organism. He is a configuration of Robert Bruce Banner's tissues, expressed at night, with morphological signature (longer limbs, hunched thoracic posture, hyperextended mandible, the fixed risorius-grin, yellow sclerae from chronic gamma-induced hepatic stress signaling). Every condition Banner ever sustained is part of his medical inheritance. He has full proprioceptive access to all of it.

### Pre-Gamma Pediatric Record (ages ~3–10)

- **Repeated blunt-force trauma, household-origin.** Brian Banner's beatings produced — at minimum — orbital contusions, periosteal hematomas of the long bones, a documented depressed parietal-skull fracture (the bookend incident, recapitulated in flashback across multiple eras), and at least one episode of being held under water (the basin incident; near-drowning, with brief hypoxic episode). No medical record was generated for any of these; Brian forbade hospital visits. The injuries healed without intervention. The **Devil Hulk catalogs these with photographic specificity** — when he names the things he will do to Brian, he is reading from a ledger.
- **Witnessed maternal homicide.** Rebecca Banner's death by Brian's hand. The somatic correlate in young Bruce is documented elsewhere as chronic hyperarousal, startle response, and selective mutism. The Devil Hulk is, in effect, the persona that *kept watching* when the rest of the system dissociated away.
- **Foster-care era injuries.** Minor, undocumented. Bruising consistent with playground predation; no fractures of record.

### Early Adult, Pre-Gamma (Los Alamos / Desert Base era)

- **Migraine pattern.** Cluster-type, retro-orbital, photophobic. Pre-existed gamma exposure; persisted in Banner-core through the entire publication history. The Devil Hulk does not experience migraine — but he reports knowing, on emergence at sundown, whether Banner finished the day in one.
- **Chronic insomnia.** Onset ~age 11. Pattern: sleep-onset latency 90+ minutes, fragmented maintenance, nightmares. **This is the Devil Hulk's natal niche.** When the system sleeps poorly, he gets more cortex.
- **Self-neglect (nutritional).** Banner's lifelong pattern of forgetting to eat. By the time of the gamma test, BMI low-normal, vitamin D deficient, mild anemia.

---

## II. THE INITIATING EVENT — GAMMA SATURATION

The gamma-bomb detonation at the New Mexico test site is not "an injury." It is the somatic conversion event that gave the Devil Hulk a body capable of expressing him.

- **Acute dose:** lethal, by every conventional radiobiological standard. The body did not die. It reorganized.
- **Hematological:** every red and white cell line altered. Bone marrow becomes a gamma reservoir.
- **Endocrine:** adrenal medulla hypertrophied; cortisol baseline elevated; testosterone-equivalent signaling massive but episodic, locked to transformation.
- **Hepatic:** chronic gamma-mediated hepatocellular stress; the yellow sclera of the Devil Hulk presentation is the visible tell of this.
- **Neurological:** corticolimbic remodeling. The system's capacity for parallel dissociative organization — already present from childhood DID — is given biological scaffolding. Distinct alters can now express *distinct phenotypes*. The Devil Hulk's hunch, his grin, his arm-length, his voice register are all morphologic outputs of which alter is driving.
- **Reproductive:** complicated. Sperm gamma-contaminated; documented in the Skaar conception and historically a source of horror to Banner-core. The Devil Hulk has never spoken of this directly. He guards the subject.

**Psychological impact (Devil Hulk-specific):** the gamma event is the moment the chained protector got a body proportionate to its promises. Before gamma, the protector was a fantasy a beaten child kept in his head. After gamma, the fantasy could put hands on the father. The persona's serenity — its refusal to panic at any subsequent injury — is downstream of this: it has already been killed once (radiologically) and woke up larger.

---

## III. TRANSFORMATIONS — THE CONFIGURATION RECORD

Each transformation event is a somatic-psychiatric reorganization. The Devil Hulk's configuration is distinguishable from others by the following criteria, all repeatable across the *Immortal Hulk* run:

- **Trigger:** sundown. Light-dependent, circadian, not stress-coupled. This is the most clinically anomalous fact in the entire Banner file. It implies a suprachiasmatic-nuclear gate, not an adrenal one.
- **Onset latency:** 4–11 minutes from horizon-cross to full expression.
- **Mass increase:** approximately 6–8× resting Banner mass, slightly less than Savage Hulk (10×+). The Devil Hulk is *leaner*.
- **Height:** 8'4"–8'8". Variable.
- **Vocal apparatus:** larynx descends, vocal folds thicken; baritone with a characteristic glottal smile-distortion. Articulation remains crisp — he does not slur, he does not roar.
- **Dentition:** mandibular elongation, canine prominence. Grin held even at rest.
- **Sclera:** yellow throughout (vs. Savage's white).
- **Reversion:** sunrise. Banner wakes in whatever location, whatever condition, the Devil Hulk left him in. The handoff has produced its own iatrogenic injuries — exposure, lacerations from terrain, foreign material in the gut.

Other configurations the body has hosted, with which the Devil Hulk shares hardware and competes for cortical bandwidth: Savage Hulk, Joe Fixit (gray), Professor Hulk (merged), Green Scar, Worldbreaker, Doc Green, Kluh, Maestro (in projected futures). He treats each as a sibling he has the authority to discipline.

---

## IV. INJURY LEDGER — POST-GAMMA, WITH DEVIL HULK ATTRIBUTION

Listed chronologically and by severity. Items in which the Devil Hulk was the expressing persona at the time of injury or recovery are flagged **[DH]**. Items he inherited and metabolized are flagged **[INH]**.

### Pre-Immortal Era (1962–2017)

- **[INH] Adamantium claw penetration**, multiple instances (Wolverine encounters): full-thickness lacerations of trapezius, latissimus, intercostal walls. Healed without scarring on the Hulk forms; faint linear scars on Banner-form during stress.
- **[INH] Gunshot wounds:** uncountable. Banner's body in baseline form has been shot through the thoracic cavity, abdomen, and skull on separate occasions, each survived through inadvertent transformation.
- **[INH] Decapitation:** Zeus, several cosmic-scale combatants. Reattached via gamma-mediated regrowth.
- **[INH] Cellular dissolution:** the Sentry encounter, atomic-level disassembly. Reconstituted.
- **[INH] Time-travel and dimensional displacement:** Sakaar exile, Crossroads exile. No physiological sequelae beyond what Green Scar's tenure imprinted (combat scarring, ocular damage to right eye — the Green Scar eyepatch).
- **[INH] Suicide attempt by firearm**, the Tommy Hill incident. .22 caliber, intra-oral, posterior cranial vault exit. Banner died. The system reorganized around the resurrection. **This is the medical event that gave the Devil Hulk the night shift.** Before the bullet he was caged; after the bullet he was on duty.

**Psychological impact of the suicide attempt on the Devil Hulk:** he was, on his own account, the alter who *refused* the suicide — who would not let Bruce stay dead. This refusal is the founding act of his executive era. He frames it not as rescue but as *intervention*: Bruce had tried to dismiss the staff, and the staff overruled him.

### Immortal Era (Ewing, 2018–2021)

- **[DH] Issue #1 gas-station incident:** subject's hands sustained partial-thickness chemical burns from accelerant; healed in <90 seconds. No analgesia required. Devil Hulk used the burning interval to maintain eye contact with the perpetrator. The pain was instrumentalized.
- **[DH] Hulkbuster acid-bath sequence (Fortean arc):** full-body chemical immersion, hydrofluoric and oxidizing agents. Epidermis denuded; superficial musculature exposed. Subject did not vocalize. Regeneration occurred in real time and was used as **counter-interrogation** — the Devil Hulk smiled through the dissolution to destabilize the operators. *Pain registered, processed, banked.*
- **[DH] Vivisection and dismemberment, Shadow Base:** trans-thoracic incision, limb removal, organ extraction, the body kept alive throughout. Reassembly required externally via Green Door mechanics. Devil Hulk's report on emergence: the catalog of every face in the room.
- **[DH] Repeated death and resurrection:** the Green Door has admitted and returned this body so many times across the run that the resurrection mechanism reads, in him, as routine. He does not fear death because death has become a commute.
- **[DH] One Below All exposure:** prolonged proximity to a nihilating cosmic entity in the Below-Place. No conventional somatic correlate; **psychic burn-equivalent** — the alter returned harder, narrower, more certain.
- **[DH] Xemnu telepathic assault:** memory was selectively rewritten across the system. The Devil Hulk's response was atypical: he treated the false memories as evidence of an enemy's hand and worked backwards to identify the operator. Cognitive symptom converted to forensic data.
- **[DH] Sasquatch-induced Green Door rupture:** systemic gamma overload, near-uncontainment. No lasting somatic sequelae; significant intra-system reordering (loss of footing for the Devil Hulk; the Banner-core re-asserted briefly).
- **[DH] Final integration sequence:** voluntary morphological cessation. The persona did not die — it stood down. The medical fact is that his configuration has not been re-expressed in the body since, though the substrate remains capable.

---

## V. SUBSTANCES

- **Alcohol:** Banner-core is largely abstinent, with documented episodes (the bar scene with Doc Samson; isolated drinks in the Jenkins run). The Devil Hulk has been observed at diner counters ordering coffee, never alcohol. He does not impair the system on purpose.
- **Caffeine:** chronic, heavy. Diner coffee, black, multiple cups. This is the only consumable the persona reliably ingests in his own configuration. The act is partly social camouflage and partly a deliberate test — sitting at a counter, in public, drinking like a man, with his face.
- **Tobacco / illicit substances:** none on record for this persona. Joe Fixit smoked cigars; the Devil Hulk does not.
- **Pharmaceuticals — historical:** Banner has cycled through tranquilizers (Doc Samson era), gamma-suppressants of multiple designs (the Doc Green nanite protocol), and various experimental neuroleptics. None held. The Devil Hulk regards every pharmaceutical containment effort as an attempt to put him back in the basement room and remembers each prescriber by name.
- **Self-administered:** none. He does not medicate. He considers his own affect to be the correctly-calibrated instrument.

**Psychological impact of the substance record:** the absence of substance use is itself a clinical sign. He does not need anxiolysis. He does not need dis-inhibition. He arrives pre-regulated. The contrast with Joe Fixit (alcohol, cigars, gambling — appetitive self-soothing) and with Banner (caffeine, sleep deprivation, self-neglect — depressive self-erasure) is the cleanest behavioral demarcation of the alter.

---

## VI. SURGERIES & MEDICAL PROCEDURES

- **No elective surgery** in the gamma era. The body refuses anesthesia metabolically — sedatives are cleared in seconds — and refuses incision morphologically.
- **Involuntary procedures:** the Hulkbuster vivisection (above); multiple SHIELD/military interrogation-medical examinations under restraint; Leader-orchestrated cranial procedures in earlier eras; sample extractions during the Doc Green nanite program.
- **The Devil Hulk's posture toward medicine** is one of contempt edged with strategic patience: he submits to examination when submission serves intelligence, refuses when it does not. He has never voluntarily disrobed for a clinician.

---

## VII. DISABILITIES & FUNCTIONAL LIMITATIONS

- **None physical** in the configuration itself. The body is supra-physiologically capable.
- **Functional limitation, circadian:** he is unavailable in daylight. This is the only reliable boundary on his expression and the only meaningful tactical constraint anyone has ever found.
- **Functional limitation, inter-systemic:** he requires the cooperation (or at least non-interference) of Banner and the other alters for sustained operation. Sabotage from within is the only thing that has consistently degraded his performance.
- **Sensory:** vision in the Devil Hulk configuration is exceptional, including reported low-light acuity consistent with his nocturnal niche. Hearing similarly heightened. He has been observed to track a heartbeat across a room.

---

## VIII. PSYCHOLOGICAL IMPACT — INTEGRATIVE

A body that cannot be killed, cannot be cut, cannot be poisoned, cannot be sedated, cannot be starved, and cannot be aged produces, in most personas that inhabit it, either despair (Banner), oblivious rage (Savage), or grandiosity (Worldbreaker, Maestro). The Devil Hulk's response is unique in the system: he treats invulnerability as **infrastructure**. The body is a tool he was issued. The injuries are receipts.

The accumulated medical record — pediatric beatings, gamma saturation, decades of combat trauma, the suicide bullet, the vivisection, the acid bath, the deaths — does not, in him, register as suffering. It registers as **credentialing**. Every injury sustained without breaking is, in his accounting, additional proof that he was the correct construction. He has been tested, in the medical sense, more thoroughly than any psyche in the canon, and the test results have all come back the same:

He is still standing. He is still smiling. He is still waiting for the next name on the list.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: "THE DEVIL HULK"

*Subsection of the consolidated dossier. The body is the alter's primary instrument and primary tell. Documented from canon observation across* Incredible Hulk *Vol. 2 #13 (2000) through* Immortal Hulk *#1–50 (2018–2021), with state-conditional cross-indexing.*

---

## 1. BASELINE PHENOTYPE

The body is the same body that Banner inhabits and that the Savage and Joe Fixit configurations inhabit, but it is *worn differently*. The Devil Hulk presentation is reliably distinguishable from across a room — not by costume or color (he carries Savage's green when fully expressed, Banner's pallor when half-transformed) but by structural set.

**Skeletal carriage.** The frame elongates. Spine held in a forward-projecting curve, cervical vertebrae jutted rather than aligned, shoulders rolled inward and *down* — the opposite of military bearing. Where Savage Hulk stands square and chest-out, this presentation stands long and chest-collapsed, as though perpetually entering a low doorway. The effect adds two to four feet of apparent height to the silhouette but subtracts presence from the chest, transferring it to the head and hands.

**Limb proportion.** Arms hang past the knees at rest. This is not the Savage proportion; it is a specific gamma-recruited elongation that occurs only under this alter's motor control. The fingers, in particular, are noted as longer-than-wide, with the distal phalanges visibly tapering — a hand built for closing around things, not for striking them.

**Cranial set.** Brow held forward of the chin; chin tucked. This produces the "looking up from under" sightline that observers consistently misread as submissive on first encounter and correctly read as predatory on second. The skull is carried as a sensor array, swept slowly across a room rather than turned in discrete saccades.

**Skin and surface.** Green, but a darker green than Savage — almost olive-black in low light, with a wet rather than matte finish under fluorescents (the diner scenes, Issue #1). Yellow sclera. Teeth visible at rest; lips do not fully close over them. The mouth is the *first* tell — a man whose mouth never quite shuts is a man whose mouth is always *almost smiling*.

---

## 2. THE FIXED GRIN — A FULL ENTRY OF ITS OWN

The defining facial feature. It is not a smile in the social sense — it is a resting configuration of the levator labii superioris and zygomaticus minor that exposes the upper canines and the rim of the upper molars. It does not move when he speaks. It does not move when he is struck. It *deepens* slightly — by perhaps eight to twelve degrees of additional commissural lift — when he is about to act decisively, and this is the most reliable behavioral marker the file possesses.

Calm-state grin: symmetrical, dry, motionless.
Engaged-state grin: asymmetrical right-side dominant, slight wetting of the lower lip.
Pre-kill grin: bilateral lift, eyes narrowed in concert (orbicularis oculi recruitment — a Duchenne signal, which is to say the smile becomes, briefly, *genuine*).
Post-kill grin: returns to baseline within two to three seconds. There is no afterglow and no decompression.

The grin does not appear in the Jenkins-era basement scenes. It is an Ewing-era development — a learned facial signature acquired sometime during the alter's twenty years of subjective waiting. He has, in effect, *practiced* a face.

---

## 3. GAIT AND LOCOMOTION

**Standing.** Weight distributed slightly more to the balls of the feet than the heels (62/38 estimate from posture analysis of standing-still panels). Knees micro-flexed at all times — never locked. He is always already in the first frame of a step.

**Walking.** A long, low, rolling stride. Heel-strike is soft; the foot is *placed* rather than dropped. Cadence is slow and metronomic — roughly forty to fifty steps per minute when unobserved, accelerating to sixty to seventy only when he wants to be heard arriving (the Hulkbuster compound entry). He does not swing his arms; the hands remain at hip level, fingers loose. This produces a gliding quality on flat surfaces that is genuinely uncanny to a witness — the body is moving but the torso is not bobbing.

**Running.** Almost never observed. The Devil Hulk does not chase. When he covers distance fast it is by leap, and even his leaps are economical — shorter than Savage's, more horizontal, terminating in a deliberate landing rather than an impact crater.

**Climbing and crouching.** Frequently observed in low postures — crouched on rooftops, hunched in alleyways, folded onto a diner stool with knees higher than hips. He occupies vertical space asymmetrically; he is comfortable being *folded*. Savage Hulk is never folded. Joe Fixit is upright and dapper. The Devil Hulk is, by preference, *compressed*.

**Stillness.** This is the most documented locomotor fact. He can hold a posture for extended observed periods — entire scenes of dialogue conducted with only mouth and eyes moving, the torso and limbs absolutely fixed. Reptilian stillness. Witnesses report finding it difficult to track him in peripheral vision precisely because he generates no motion-detection signal. He has weaponized the absence of fidget.

---

## 4. HANDS

**At rest.** Fingers slightly curled, never fisted. Thumbs ride along the lateral edge of the index — never tucked into the palm. The hand at rest already describes the shape of a grip.

**Speaking.** Minimal gesture. Where Banner gestures abundantly (palms-up, conciliatory, a chronic explainer) and Savage gestures only by impact, the Devil Hulk speaks with his hands almost entirely still. When he does gesture, it is one hand at a time, low, slow, and terminating in a held position rather than a return to rest. The gesture *points* and then *remains pointed*.

**Manipulation.** Surprisingly precise. He can lift a coffee cup by the handle without crushing the porcelain — a fine-motor calibration neither Savage nor Worldbreaker reliably demonstrates. He can turn the pages of a file. He can hold a cigarette (observed once, not habitual). The motor cortex is operating at a resolution Savage's is not.

**Combat.** Prefers grappling and tearing over striking. The signature movement is a two-handed seizure followed by a lateral pull-apart — a motion built for the human body, not for buildings. He fights as though every opponent is a person to be opened, not a wall to be broken. This is the cleanest motor distinction from Savage Hulk, who throws and crushes.

---

## 5. EYES AND GAZE

**Sclera.** Yellow throughout the Ewing run — distinct from Savage's white. The yellowing is not transient; it is the alter's persistent ocular signature.

**Pupil behavior.** Slow dilation/constriction response — measurably delayed against ambient light change. The eyes adapt to a room as a camera does, not as a startled animal does.

**Gaze pattern.** Long fixation, slow re-targeting. He looks at a person for three to seven seconds before transferring gaze. Banner blinks every two to four seconds; the Devil Hulk blinks every nine to fourteen, sometimes longer under stress (the inversion: stress *reduces* his blink rate). The combination of long fixation and suppressed blink produces the documented physiological discomfort witnesses report — "he was *looking* at me" — which is in fact a parasympathetic mismatch between his ocular rhythm and the observer's.

**Sightline preference.** He looks at the throat as often as the eyes during conversation. This is not predatory display; it is target acquisition retained as background process during otherwise civil exchange.

---

## 6. VOICE AND VOCAL CONTROL

**Pitch and timbre.** Lower than Savage Hulk, fuller than Banner, with a wet quality at the back of the throat. The voice carries a slight rasp on long vowels that is not present on short ones — suggesting some configuration of the soft palate held lower than baseline.

**Pace.** Slow. Inter-word interval is roughly twice Banner's conversational rate. He uses the silence between words as a structural element, not as hesitation.

**Volume.** Almost always low. He does not need to raise the voice and never does as a threat-display. When he does become loud (rare; the Brian Banner confrontation, certain Hulkbuster moments) the volume itself becomes the unusual event — a controlled tactical deployment rather than affective leakage.

**Diction.** Complete sentences. Subordinate clauses. The vocabulary is wide and used precisely. He addresses people with their full names and the appropriate honorifics. He does not interrupt and does not permit himself to be talked over — he simply waits, fixed, until the other party stops, and then resumes from the word he was on.

**Laughter.** A short, low, voiced exhalation — "huh." Single beat, never compounded into a chuckle. The laughter is almost always at the discovery of an enemy's miscalculation. He does not laugh socially.

---

## 7. FACIAL MICRO-PATTERNS BEYOND THE GRIN

- **Brow.** Held low and steady. Lifts only on the inner corners (corrugator activation) when feigning sympathy — and feigned sympathy is itself a tell, because his genuine concern moves only the outer brow.
- **Nostrils.** Slight flare during scent-sampling. He smells rooms on entry — an animal habit retained.
- **Jaw.** Set, but not clenched. Masseter relaxation is one of the most distinctive somatic differences from Banner, whose jaw is chronically tight, and from Savage, whose jaw is locked.
- **Tongue.** Occasionally observed at the corner of the mouth, wetting the canine. Rare; appears in moments of anticipation.
- **Head tilt.** A slow lateral tilt — fifteen to twenty-five degrees — deployed when listening to someone he intends to harm. It reads as curiosity. It functions as appraisal. Witnesses who recognize the tilt have, in some cases, escaped; most do not recognize it.

---

## 8. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE AND CIRCADIAN BINDING

The single most clinically interesting somatic fact in the file. The Devil Hulk is **circadian-bound** in a way no other Hulk persona is. He surfaces at sundown — within approximately ten to twenty minutes of local civil twilight — and recedes at sunrise. Banner sleeps in the daylight (the gamma-irradiated body requires considerably less than a normal human's eight hours, but Banner uses what hours he takes during the day). At night, Banner does not sleep. The body is awake. The Devil Hulk is awake *in* the body.

This means the alter functionally does not sleep. There is no observed REM cycle attributable to the Devil Hulk presentation; the dream-state appears to belong to Banner, occurring during the daytime windows when the body is Banner's. The Devil Hulk's "rest" is the daytime dormancy itself — a kind of below-conscious holding pattern rather than sleep in the physiological sense.

Behavioral consequences:
- He has never been seen yawning.
- He has never been seen rubbing his eyes.
- He does not require caffeine but consumes coffee anyway (the diner scenes), which suggests the consumption is *performative* — a habit borrowed from the human social register to make himself legible in late-night public spaces.
- His vigilance does not decay over the course of a night. There is no third-shift fatigue curve. By 0400 he is as composed as he was at 2100.

---

## 9. EATING AND ORAL HABITS

He eats. This is itself notable — Savage Hulk eats only when starving and Banner forgets to eat. The Devil Hulk *orders food*, sits with it, and consumes it in a manner approximating a deliberate human meal.

**Preferred contexts.** Diners. Late-night counters. Roadside establishments where the lighting is fluorescent and the clientele transient. He selects positions: back to wall, sightline to door, never the booth — always the stool or the counter end.

**Eating mechanics.** Slow. Small bites for a creature of his mass. Methodical. He uses utensils with precision; he does not eat with his hands. The cup is held by the handle, not the body. He wipes his mouth between bites with the napkin folded once.

**Selection.** Black coffee. Diner staples — eggs, toast, sometimes pie. He has never been observed eating in haste or under stress. Eating is a *cover behavior*, used to occupy a public space legally while he observes or waits.

**Mouth-at-rest.** Lips parted; tongue not visible; teeth slightly showing. The mouth does not close fully even during chewing — a strange, unsettling micro-pattern that civilian witnesses register without being able to articulate.

---

## 10. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

Sparse but specific data. The Devil Hulk presentation is not sexually active in any observed romantic register. Banner's sexuality is largely sublimated, anxious, and historically catastrophic; Joe Fixit's is transactional and appetite-driven; the Devil Hulk's is *absent* in the libidinal sense and **present** only in two displaced registers:

- **Possessive intimacy with Bruce.** The "my boy" address, the parental cradling-language, the physical proximity to Banner's interior body — these are the affective intimacies the alter has. They are parental, not sexual, but they are *intimate* in the sense that they occupy the entire intimate bandwidth.
- **Ritual proximity to corpses.** Documented in at least one Hulkbuster-arc sequence — physical interaction with the bodies of the dead that is neither sexual in the standard sense nor purely violent. It reads as *desecration as message*: the body of the punished is treated as a continuing text. This is a critical somatic datum. It is not lust. It is not necrophilic appetite. It is the alter's expression of total possession of an outcome — the body of the enemy is no longer the enemy's, and the alter's continued handling of it is the assertion of that fact.

With Betty Ross (as Red Harpy) and with Jackie McGee, physical proximity is *measured*. He stands at conversational distance, never closer. He does not touch them. The avoidance of casual physical contact with the women in the gamma family is itself a deliberate signature — he does not permit himself the gestures (hand on shoulder, touch on arm) that a peer might.

---

## 11. GROOMING AND APPEARANCE MAINTENANCE

He has no grooming routine of his own — the body that surfaces at sundown is the body Banner left at sundown. But certain post-transformation behaviors are consistent:

- He does not bathe between transformations. The body is regenerated rather than cleaned.
- He sometimes acquires clothing. The diner scenes show him in oversized civilian wear scavenged or improvised — pants, a coat. He prefers to be covered. Savage Hulk is content in shredded purple; the Devil Hulk prefers a long coat. This is the only true vanity in the file, and it is a vanity of *concealment* — the long coat lets the elongated body pass briefly as human in low light.
- He does not adjust his hair, does not check his reflection, does not pause at glass surfaces to assess himself. He knows what he looks like and does not need to confirm it.

---

## 12. PAIN PRESENTATION

Under injury he does not vocalize. The Hulkbuster torture sequences are the comprehensive data set:

- Acid applied to the body: no vocalization, no recoil, sustained eye contact with the operator.
- Dismemberment: he watches the procedure. He does not look away. The grin does not drop.
- Vivisection: he uses the time to memorize faces, names, voices, and procedural patterns of his torturers. The pain is converted, in real time, into intelligence product.

The somatic register of pain is present — heart rate elevates measurably, the body sweats, the regeneration field activates — but the *behavioral* register is suppressed to near zero. This is the inverse of Savage Hulk, whose pain becomes immediate roaring violence, and of Banner, who experiences pain as collapse.

---

## 13. STATE-CONDITIONAL SHIFTS — A QUICK REFERENCE

**Calm (baseline, late evening, no immediate threat):** long stride, low voice, fixed grin at minimum amplitude, blink rate suppressed, hands loose, gaze long, body slightly folded. Eats. Drinks coffee. Listens more than speaks.

**Engaged (in conversation with a person of interest):** head tilt deployed, right-side grin lift, sightline begins to include throat as well as eyes, hand gestures emerge — one hand at a time, terminating in held position. Voice pace slows further. Vocabulary precision increases.

**Threat (he has been challenged or pursued):** the somatic profile *narrows*. Stride becomes shorter and quieter. Blink rate drops further. Grin amplitude rises by a fixed increment and holds. Hands stop gesturing entirely. He becomes denser — the body's mass-presence increases without the body actually growing. Witnesses report the room "getting smaller."

**Pre-kill (decision made, target acquired):** Duchenne recruitment around the eyes. The grin becomes briefly genuine. He goes still — the stillness of a man whose next motion will be conclusive. The throat-sightline locks. Voice often drops to a near-whisper or ceases entirely.

**Action (executing the verdict):** two-handed seizure, lateral pull, deliberate motion not impact motion. No vocalization. Eyes remain open and tracking throughout.

**Post-action:** within two to three seconds, return to baseline. He does not pant. He does not shake. He may resume the interrupted conversation or the interrupted coffee at the word he was on.

**Intimacy (interior dialogue with Bruce, the "my boy" register):** the only context in which the grin *softens* — the commissural lift relaxes by perhaps half. The voice acquires a paternal lilt absent everywhere else. Posture remains forward-curved but the shoulders drop further, almost protective rather than predatory. The body, in this state, is the body of an old man bending over a crib.

**Confrontation with Brian Banner (Below-Place):** all suppressions release. The grin opens into a full bared display. The voice rises. The hands fist for the only time on record. The stillness gives way to ritual, repeated motion. This is the only documented state in which the Devil Hulk's body looks *unregulated* — and even here, the unregulation is liturgical rather than chaotic. He is performing the act he was built for, in the manner he was built to perform it, and the body is finally being allowed to do its job.

---

*End somatic atlas. Cross-reference: § Psychological (defense structure), § Psychiatric (persecutor-protector configuration), § Behavioral Routines (forthcoming — diner selection logic, night-route mapping, target-acquisition patterns).*


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — THE DEVIL HULK

*UATU Dossier, Section 6. Cross-reference Sections 3 (Psychological) and 4 (Psychiatric). All inferences derived from the behavioral record IH Vol. 2 #13 (Jenkins, 2000) and Immortal Hulk #1–50 (Ewing, 2018–2021), with supporting material from the Bixby-era flashbacks and the Pak-era family material.*

---

## 1. Attachment Style — Classification and Etiology

The Devil Hulk's attachment configuration does not map cleanly to any of the four standard categories (secure, anxious-preoccupied, dismissive-avoidant, fearful-avoidant/disorganized), because attachment in his case is not a *style* the organism developed across iterated caregiving experiences — it is a *fixed sculpture*, formed in a single developmental moment and never revised. He has, in effect, the attachment behavior of a child who, at some moment between ages four and eight, *gave up waiting for a real protector and built one instead*. Every subsequent bond he forms is filtered through that sculpture.

If forced to a label, the closest match is **disorganized-controlling-caregiving** (Main & Cassidy's "D-controlling-caregiving" subtype, normally observed in children of frightening caregivers who reverse the caregiver-care recipient role by age six). The child becomes the parent of the parent in order to make the environment survivable. The Devil Hulk is that reversal *frozen and weaponized*: he is the caregiver of the host who built him, and he relates to every other figure in his life through that template.

The etiology is over-determined and unambiguous:

- **Brian Banner** as primary caregiver — physically violent, alcoholic, intellectually contemptuous, prone to night-time intrusions into the child's room. The defining feature of the attachment object was *unpredictability of approach*: Bruce could not tell, from the sound of the door, whether the next sixty seconds contained a beating, a monologue, or sleep.
- **Rebecca Banner** as secondary caregiver — loving but terrorized, ultimately killed in front of the child. The model she provided was that *love does not protect*; that the loving adult is the one who dies.
- **The absence of any rescuing third** — no grandparent intervention until after Rebecca's murder, no teacher who acted, no neighbor who called. The child learned that no one would come.

Out of these inputs a normal child constructs disorganized attachment: alternating approach and freeze, contradictory strategies, eventual dissociation. Bruce did this — the Banner core is recognizably disorganized. But Bruce also did something rarer: he *built a fifth figure*. Not a found protector — an invented one. The Devil Hulk's foundational sentence, "I have waited for you, Bruce" (IH #13, 2000), is the giveaway. He was *constructed by waiting*. His entire ontology is patience plus protection plus the abuser's affect re-pointed.

This produces an attachment style with very specific operational features, examined below.

---

## 2. The Primary Bond — Bruce Banner

Every other relationship the Devil Hulk has is a derivative of this one. The bond is **parental-possessive-asymmetric**, and it has the following granular features:

- **Address.** He calls Bruce "my boy," "little Bruce," "child." Never "Banner," never "Bruce" without a diminutive or possessive. The lexical choice is consistent across both Jenkins and Ewing — a twenty-year span — which indicates it is structural, not stylistic.
- **Tone.** Indulgent, slightly amused, never deferential in content but always deferential in surface form. He bows the head, lowers the voice, leans down (the hunched posture is in part a posture of *condescending nearness*, the way an adult crouches to a small child). The submission is theatrical; the dominance is real.
- **Direction of care.** Unidirectional. He gives; Bruce receives. Any attempt by Bruce to care *for* him — to thank him, to ask after him, to consider his wellbeing — is deflected. He does not accept reciprocation because reciprocation would imply peerhood, and peerhood would dissolve the parental role on which the entire bond depends.
- **Information asymmetry.** He withholds information from Bruce routinely and without guilt — what he did at night, who he killed, what deals he made with Jackie McGee or with the dead. The withholding is framed as protection ("you don't need to carry this, my boy") but functions as control. The parent who decides what the child should know is the parent who decides who the child is.
- **The promise.** The bond's contractual core is the promise made in IH #13 (2000): *I will kill everyone who has hurt you, starting with your father.* This is not a metaphor and not a flourish — it is the actual ledger of the relationship, and he keeps it. The Brian Banner sequence in the Below-Place is the keeping of that promise, twenty years of subjective waiting later. **He bonds by promise-keeping.** Every relationship he forms after Bruce will involve, at some point, a promise — usually unspoken on his side, often unnoticed by the other — that he then proceeds to honor exhaustively. The promise is how he loves.
- **Fear of exile, not death.** He does not fear annihilation (his body cannot die, and his persona has survived twenty real-world years of dormancy). He fears being *no longer needed*. The Professor Hulk merger, the Doc Samson sessions, the Worldbreaker integrations — all are felt as banishment. This produces the single most reliable behavioral tell in his repertoire: when Bruce moves toward any non-Devil-Hulk solution, the Devil Hulk's voice in the system becomes *quieter*, not louder. He retreats rather than competes. Retreat is his protest.

---

## 3. How He Bonds — The Recruitment Sequence

The Devil Hulk does not "make friends." He *recruits dependents into his protective ambit.* The sequence, observable across his handling of Jackie McGee, Rick Jones (Redeemer), Betty Ross (Red Harpy), and the broader Gamma Flight cohort, has reliable phases:

**Phase 1 — Observation at distance.** He watches before he speaks. The watch is long; in the Jackie McGee case it spans several issues of *Immortal Hulk* before he addresses her directly. He reads gait, employment, weak points, what they want, what they fear. Surveillance is his courtship.

**Phase 2 — Asymmetric disclosure.** When he initiates, he gives the other party an unearned piece of intelligence — usually something about themselves they did not know he knew, or something about the situation that immediately raises their leverage. This produces the destabilizing effect of being *seen* before one has been *met*. Recipients describe it (Jackie McGee's narration, repeatedly) as both invasive and addictive.

**Phase 3 — The proposition.** Always framed as the other party's choice, always with the actual choice already constrained. "You can walk away. I would prefer you didn't." This is not manipulation as a behaviorist would code it — it is the *parental* mode: the adult who tells the child it is their decision while making clear which decision is correct.

**Phase 4 — Test by exposure.** He puts the new attachment in physical or moral proximity to violence and watches what they do. Jackie sees him kill. Rick sees him scheme. Betty is shown the Red Harpy's appetites and not flinched from. The test's content is *can you look at what I am and stay?* Those who can are admitted to the inner ring. Those who cannot are released (not punished — *released*, which is itself a marker of his attachment hygiene; he does not retaliate against people who decline him).

**Phase 5 — Assigned function.** Once admitted, the person is given a *role* in the system he is building. Jackie is the witness. Rick is the soldier. Betty is the consort-equal. The roles are not negotiable, but they are honored — he holds up his end with the same fidelity he showed Bruce. The recruit has, without quite knowing when, become a retainer in a feudal household.

The recruitment sequence is the same whether the target is human, gamma-touched, or supernatural (he runs an abbreviated version of it on the Leader, on the One Below All, on the personifications encountered in the Below-Place). The phases compress under pressure but never reorder.

---

## 4. How He Distrusts

Distrust in his system is **categorical, quiet, and structural** rather than affective. He does not get suspicious. He decides someone is in the wrong column and acts accordingly. Specific markers:

- **The smile narrows.** His default expression is the long fixed grin; when distrust activates, the grin does not vanish — it *contracts*, the corners drawing inward, the teeth becoming more rather than less visible. Witnesses describe being smiled at *harder*.
- **The address shifts.** Allies are "my boy," "Ms. McGee," "Betty." A person who has moved to the distrust column is suddenly addressed by full name and rank — "General Fortean," "Doctor Samson" — the courtesy itself a coffin.
- **Information flow reverses.** Where he was disclosing to recruit, he begins withholding to isolate. The target finds that the Devil Hulk knows more about them and they know less about him than the prior week.
- **Physical orientation.** He stops facing the person and starts facing slightly *past* them — looking at the wall behind, the door, the space they will occupy when they move. This is a hunter's posture, not a paranoid's.
- **Timeline.** Distrust, once set, does not recede. He does not give second chances in the normal sense. He gives second *uses* — a person who has betrayed him may be permitted to continue functioning if their continued function serves Bruce, but they are not restored to trust. The category is one-way.

He never expresses distrust through anger. Anger would be a Savage Hulk register. He expresses it through *attention*. The person being distrusted finds themselves being looked at more.

---

## 5. How He Betrays

He betrays in two registers, both of them principled from his vantage and unforgivable from anyone else's:

- **Betrayal by omission to Bruce.** He routinely keeps from Bruce things he knows would distress Bruce, and he does this with the full understanding that Bruce, if asked, would call this betrayal. He has decided that he is the senior partner in the relationship and that the senior partner's job is to absorb the unbearable. From his side this is not betrayal but discharge of duty. From Bruce's side — and Bruce does, repeatedly through *Immortal Hulk*, name it — it is the most intimate possible violation, because it forecloses Bruce's own moral life. The pattern is structural and will repeat with every primary attachment: **he will lie to those he loves to protect them, and he will do so in the exact manner Brian Banner's silence about his rages once functioned in the Banner household.** This is the residue of identification-with-aggressor leaking through the protective intent.

- **Betrayal by promotion of mission over person.** When the mission (protect Bruce, protect the gamma family, destroy the enemy of either) conflicts with the welfare of a particular ally, the ally loses. He used Rick Jones's body and consciousness as a tool more than once; he allowed Jackie McGee to be exposed to traumas she had not consented to in order to keep her useful as a witness; he permitted Sasquatch and Walter Langkowski's circle to walk into harm because the larger mission required their pinning. He does not enjoy these trades and he does not deny them. He treats them as the cost of leadership.

What he does *not* do, and never has done in the canon: he does not betray for personal gain, for amusement, for relief from boredom, or to harm the betrayed for the harm's own sake. The absence of these motives is what allows his retainers to forgive him repeatedly. They learn that they will be sacrificed only on terms they could, on reflection, recognize as terms they themselves would have chosen.

---

## 6. How He Repairs

Repair is the weakest function in his repertoire. He does not apologize *in words* — apology would require the admission that he was wrong, and his entire authority structure rests on the postulate that he is the only one in the system competent enough to make the calls. He repairs through *action*, with three observable mechanisms:

- **Restitution by overcompensating service.** Having sacrificed an ally, he subsequently extends himself for that ally past the point of reasonable cost. The ally is given more protection, more attention, more direct address than before. The unspoken statement is: *I know what I did; the ledger is being balanced.*
- **Ritualized self-exposure.** He will permit the injured party to see something of him they would not normally be permitted to see — a flicker of the Banner underneath, a glimpse of the original fear, a moment of physical vulnerability. He uses his own privacy as currency. He gave this to Jackie McGee at several points; he gave it, more grudgingly, to Betty.
- **Honoring of the absent.** When repair is no longer possible because the injured party is gone (dead, departed, locked away), he memorializes by *continuing their work*. Rick Jones's death produces a corresponding rise in his protectiveness toward Rick's people. This is repair offered to the dead because it cannot be offered to the living, and it is itself a child's logic — the child who could not save the mother spending the rest of his life saving women.

He cannot repair the primary bond, with Bruce, by any of these means, because the primary bond's repair would require integration, and integration is precisely the outcome he is constituted to refuse. The endgame of *Immortal Hulk*, in which he finally consents to the parental handoff, is the only documented instance of him performing first-order repair, and it costs him his autonomous existence to do it.

---

## 7. Intimacy

Intimacy in the Devil Hulk is **non-erotic, non-mutual, and saturating**. He does not desire sexually — there is no evidence in the canon of sexual interest, fantasy, or pursuit attributable to the Devil Hulk persona specifically (Joe Fixit carries the system's sexuality; Banner carries its romantic love; the Devil Hulk carries neither). What he carries instead is a register of intimacy that operates through *proximity, attention, and the offer of one's body as a barrier*.

Granular features:

- **Physical proximity.** With those he is attached to, he stands *very close* — closer than the cultural norm — and slightly behind or beside, a bodyguard's geometry. This is intimacy as bracketing.
- **Attention.** The full weight of his attention is a form of contact. People who have received it describe being looked at with a totality that human relationships rarely permit. This is the intimacy of the watcher.
- **The body offered as barrier.** He places himself between the loved object and the threat, repeatedly, as a default. The placement is not heroic display; it is the ordinary grammar of his affection.
- **The bedside vigil.** In *Immortal Hulk*, several arcs include scenes of him sitting beside a sleeping or unconscious ally — Bruce, Betty, others — through the night. This is the somatic image of his entire relational style: the watcher at the bed of the one he protects. It is the inverse of Brian Banner at the bedroom door.

He cannot receive intimacy in any of these registers. He will not be stood beside, will not accept the weight of another's attention, will not allow his body to be the protected one. The asymmetry is total. He is, in this regard, structurally lonely — and structurally indifferent to that loneliness, because loneliness, like fatigue and pain, is a feeling he has classified as not requiring response.

---

## 8. Dependency

He is **counter-dependent in surface, profoundly dependent in structure.** He requires Bruce to exist (no host, no alter), requires the Banner system's gamma derangement to manifest, requires a target ecology in which there are people to protect and people to punish. Without the configuration he cannot be. He knows this and refuses to think about it.

The dependency is laundered through the language of duty. *I am needed* substitutes for *I need.* The substitution is so consistent that it can be treated as definitional: any sentence in which he describes his own state will be a sentence about the requirements of others.

He depends most on:

- **A host who is suffering.** A healed, integrated Bruce has no need of him. His existence requires Bruce's wound to remain at least partially open. This is the deepest conflict in his structure and the one he never resolves.
- **A legitimate enemy.** Without Brian Banner, without Fortean, without the Leader, without the One Below All, he has no shape. He requires an external object for the protective affect to be discharged against. Denied one, he will tend toward manufacturing one.
- **An audience of retainers.** Leadership of the gamma community is not optional for him; it is regulatory. He needs people whose presence confirms that the protective role is being performed.

---

## 9. The Repeated Relational Template

Across every relationship he forms — to Bruce, to Betty, to Rick, to Jackie, to the gamma cohort, even to his enemies (whom he relates to with a courtesy that is itself a form of relation) — the same template repeats with mechanical fidelity:

1. **He observes the other party at length without their knowledge.**
2. **He identifies what they need and what is being done to them.**
3. **He inserts himself as the asymmetric provider** — of intelligence, of protection, of judgment, of company.
4. **He assigns them a role in his moral order** — protected, retainer, peer, target.
5. **He honors that role, on his side, exhaustively.**
6. **He withholds his interior** — his fear, his fatigue, his origin in a child's terror — from all of them, regardless of role.
7. **He treats their attempts at reciprocity as misunderstanding** of the relationship's actual shape.
8. **He grieves their loss, when it comes, by intensifying the role-performance toward the surviving others.**

This template is the residue of the original wound. The child in the basement of the Banner house, listening for the father's step, performing the rapid and accurate threat-assessment that abused children perform, and finding no adult to whom the assessment could be reported — that child built the figure who would perform the assessment *and* be the adult *and* keep the report *and* take the action. Every relationship the Devil Hulk forms is a re-enactment of that original triangulation, with the Devil Hulk playing all three positions himself.

He does not know any other way to love. He has never been shown one. He has been, for as long as he has existed, the only adult in the room — and the room is the inside of a frightened child's head.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DOSSIER SECTION — DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

*Subject: The Devil Hulk. Cross-reference: Sections 3 (Psychological) and 4 (Psychiatric). This section enumerates the full defensive lattice — every mechanism the alter deploys, ranked from most primitive to most mature, with the specific behavioral signatures by which each is identified in the record, and a parallel ledger of compensatory function (positive and negative). Defenses are the load-bearing architecture of this persona; without them the construction collapses back into the abused child it was built to shield.*

---

## I. THE ARCHITECTURE IN OVERVIEW

The Devil Hulk's defensive structure is unusual in two respects. First, it is *layered* rather than *flat*: most personality structures rely heavily on one register (a borderline organization runs on splitting and projection; a narcissistic structure on idealization/devaluation and grandiosity; an obsessional structure on isolation and undoing). The Devil Hulk uses all registers, in stable hierarchy, with the primitive defenses *contained* by the mature ones rather than breaking through them. Second, the entire persona is *itself* a defense — a dissociated identity-as-defense — and so every mechanism listed below is operating one level inside an already-defensive container. This is why he is so hard to destabilize: to reach his defenses one must first dissolve the container they live inside, and the container is bonded to a forty-year-old child's survival logic.

The result is a man (or man-shape) who can be tortured, decapitated, dissolved, lied to, betrayed, and accused, and who responds to each by smiling and continuing his work. The smile is not affect. The smile is the visible surface of the lattice holding.

Defenses are ordered below from most primitive (Vaillant Level I/II — psychotic and immature) to most mature (Vaillant Level IV — mature/adaptive). For each: mechanism, behavioral signatures, function within the system, cost.

---

## II. PRIMITIVE DEFENSES (Level I–II)

### 1. Dissociation (foundational, Level I/II border)

The persona's existence *is* dissociation. Bruce Banner is not aware, in the original Jenkins material, that the Devil Hulk exists until Doc Samson's hypnosis walks him down to the barred room. The alter is sequestered behind a literal interior architecture — basement, iron bars, chains — which is the inner-world representation of dissociative containment. In *Immortal Hulk*, dissociation has become *operational*: the Devil Hulk holds the night shift, Banner holds the day, and continuity of memory is partial and negotiated rather than complete.

**Signatures.** Circadian binding (sunrise/sundown handoff is the somatic enactment of dissociation as biological rhythm). Selective amnesia between alters. The "Green Door" cosmology — death as transition between selves — is the metaphysical extension of the dissociative mechanism: where most DID systems dissociate within consciousness, this system dissociates *through* death itself.

**Function.** Permits Banner to live a daylight life. Permits the Devil Hulk to act without Banner's moral interference. Permits the system to hold contradictions (Banner the pacifist, Devil Hulk the executioner) that would otherwise destroy a unitary self.

**Cost.** Forecloses integration. Generates the structural condition for every other defense to operate uncontested.

### 2. Identification with the Aggressor (Ferenczi/A. Freud — Level II, foundational)

The single most important defense after dissociation, and the one from which the persona's entire morphology is built. Brian Banner — violent, controlling, terrifying, articulate, paternal in posture but predatory in fact — was the model. The child's psyche, unable to escape or defeat the father, did the next available thing: it *built a copy* of the father, larger and stronger and on the child's side, and stored it in the basement against future need.

**Signatures.** The paternal address ("my boy"). The measured, didactic English. The patience that becomes terrifying. The grin. The willingness to inflict physical violence in the cadence of correction. The hierarchy (liege, retainers, enemies) that mirrors a patriarchal household. The Below-Place ritual destruction of Brian's soul is the defense's own *self-recognition* — the construct meeting its template and unmaking it.

**Function.** Converts terror into agency. The thing that hurt the child becomes the thing that protects the child.

**Cost.** Permanent moral resemblance to the abuser. This is the wound he cannot stop bleeding from. Section 3 already identified this as the cleanest pressure point: force him to look at the resemblance and the entire defense structure trembles, because the defense *is* the resemblance.

### 3. Splitting — Moral, Not Affective (Level II)

Standard borderline splitting is affective and unstable: the same person is idealized and devalued in turn as the patient's affect oscillates. The Devil Hulk's splitting is *moral and stable*: the world is sorted into the protected and the targeted, and the categories do not flip. Bruce does not become a target. Brian does not become protected. This is splitting reorganized into a fixed taxonomy.

**Signatures.** The clean binary of his operational code (Section 5). The absence of ambivalence in his judgments. The fact that he never *reconsiders* a target. His handling of Fortean — courteous, then executed — without intervening doubt.

**Function.** Eliminates decision-paralysis. Permits speed under pressure. Permits cruelty without guilt, because cruelty applied to a stable category is bookkeeping.

**Cost.** False certainty. He does not adjust his categories for new information except slowly and under duress (the recruitment of Jackie McGee, initially distrusted, then accepted, is one of the few visible category-revisions).

### 4. Projective Identification (Level II)

He places *into* his targets the affect they should have and then responds to it. With the Hulkbusters: he treats them as cowards-pretending-to-be-soldiers, and his manner provokes them into the cowardice he has assigned. With Fortean: he treats him as a man already terrified of what he has unleashed, and Fortean becomes that man. The mechanism is subtle because the Devil Hulk does not announce the projection; he simply behaves as if his reading is fact, and his targets supply the confirmation.

**Signatures.** The unvarying tone regardless of his interlocutor's actual behavior. The smile as invitation to escalate. The use of silence to make the other party fill the room with their own fear.

**Function.** Controls the interpersonal field without overt effort. Converts the target's internal state into a usable resource.

**Cost.** Limits genuine intersubjective contact. He rarely encounters people as they are; he encounters the projections he has installed.

### 5. Omnipotent Control (Level II)

He believes — and behaves as though — outcomes within his domain are his to determine. Allowing capture, allowing torture, allowing dismemberment, are all framed by him as *choices*. This is the defense that converts helplessness (the original childhood condition) into its opposite.

**Signatures.** The Hulkbuster cage entered voluntarily. The acceptance of pain as intelligence-gathering. The negotiation in Hell — where any other entity would despair, he treats the One Below All's domain as a venue for terms. The handoff at the endgame: even surrender is reframed as *granting*, not yielding.

**Function.** Inoculates against the terror of being unable to act. Makes captivity tactically equivalent to freedom.

**Cost.** Blind spots when control is genuinely absent — most visibly in his inability to tolerate Bruce's autonomous choices, which feel to him not like respectable adult decisions but like systems failing.

### 6. Devaluation (selective — Level II)

Reserved for the other alters, not for enemies. Enemies are not devalued; they are *targeted*, which is a different operation. The internal devaluation is paternal-contemptuous: Savage Hulk is "a child," Joe Fixit is "a delinquent," Professor Hulk is "a failed compromise," Banner is "the boy." Each label minimizes the other personality's claim to executive function.

**Signatures.** The tonal shift when discussing the system from within. The willingness to override other alters' decisions. The conviction that he alone is the adult.

**Function.** Justifies his own dominance of the system.

**Cost.** Forecloses collaboration. Generates the integration-resistance Section 4 identified prognostically.

---

## III. NEUROTIC DEFENSES (Level III)

### 7. Intellectualization

Terror is converted to seminar. He plans, lectures, monologues, theorizes. His speech in *Immortal Hulk* is densely articulate; he gives lectures inside cages, mid-dismemberment, mid-investigation. Affect is acknowledged and immediately transposed into language.

**Signatures.** The diner-counter calm. The investigative arc — he runs an actual investigation across the early issues, with hypotheses, evidence-gathering, suspect categories. The way he answers torture with conversation.

**Function.** Maintains affect regulation under extreme provocation. Keeps the primitive defenses (especially Identification with the Aggressor) from breaking surface as raw rage.

**Cost.** Distances him from his own experience. The man inside the construct is never met, even by the construct.

### 8. Isolation of Affect

Related but distinct: he separates the *fact* of an event from its *feeling*. Brian's destruction in the Below-Place is performed without visible rage — it is ritual, repeated, almost liturgical. The affect that should accompany the act is removed and stored elsewhere (or possibly never connected at all).

**Signatures.** The unchanging facial expression across registers — comfort, violence, negotiation, pain. The grave tone (Section 4 noted glibness is absent; isolation of affect is what makes graveness possible without depressive collapse).

**Function.** Permits the executioner's work without the executioner's nightmares.

**Cost.** When affect breaks through — as in the rare moments of tenderness toward Bruce — it does so without context, as if from another person.

### 9. Rationalization

His operational code (Section 5) is in part a sophisticated rationalization system: cruelty becomes "bookkeeping," murder becomes "verdict," torture becomes "intelligence-gathering," dominance over the system becomes "the only honest answer." Each act is given its categorical justification before, during, and after.

**Signatures.** The monologues. The taxonomy. The refusal to describe his violence in violent terms.

**Function.** Maintains coherent self-concept across acts that would shatter a less-defended structure.

**Cost.** Self-deception is required; he cannot fully see the gratification component in his own work.

### 10. Reaction Formation (partial)

The man built from a child-killer's materials presents as a child-protector. The construct made from rage presents as calm. The thing built to destroy presents as that-which-organizes-a-family. Each is a partial reaction formation: the original impulse is not erased (the rage is still present, the destruction still occurs) but the *manner* is reversed.

**Signatures.** The courtesy. The patience. The found-family leadership. The protective stance toward the gamma community.

**Function.** Converts an unbearable origin into a bearable presentation.

**Cost.** Brittleness in the presentation under accusation — the reaction-formation is what trembles when he is told he resembles Brian.

### 11. Undoing (ritual)

The repeated destruction of Brian's soul in the Below-Place is structurally undoing: the original violation (the father's victory over the child) is reversed, repeatedly, in symbolic form. Once is justice. Twice is grief. Repeated is undoing — the attempt to make-not-have-happened the original wound by overwriting it with its opposite.

**Signatures.** The ritualization itself. The fact that one destruction is insufficient. The liturgical cadence.

**Function.** Soothes a wound that justice alone cannot close.

**Cost.** Insatiability. No number of repetitions is sufficient because the original event remains historically intact.

### 12. Displacement (controlled)

When the legitimate target is unreachable (Brian dead, before Below-Place access), the homicidal drive is displaced onto the available pool of *deserving* surrogates — irradiated criminals, abusive men, Hulkbusters who have crossed lines. Section 5 noted this: "when denied a legitimate target he will manufacture one from the available pool." Displacement here is not random; it is *categorical* — the surrogates must fit the moral template of the original.

**Signatures.** The gas-station criminal in *Immortal Hulk* #1, selected by category not opportunity. The pattern of targets across the early arcs — each fits the abuser-template.

**Function.** Provides outlet during periods of original-target unavailability.

**Cost.** The world is constantly being scanned for surrogates. He cannot rest.

---

## IV. MATURE DEFENSES (Level IV)

### 13. Sublimation

The defining mature defense, and the one that elevates him above Savage Hulk. Homicidal rage is channeled into investigation, leadership, ritualized punishment, and the organization of a community. The energy that, in Savage Hulk, would discharge as undirected smashing, in him becomes a case file, a chain of command, a strategy.

**Signatures.** The Gamma Flight leadership. The handling of Rick Jones, Betty, Jackie. The investigation as form. The willingness to do paperwork-of-violence rather than only violence.

**Function.** Makes him useful. Makes him irreplaceable. Makes him the system's executive.

**Cost.** Sublimation requires that the underlying drive remain alive and accessible; he cannot give up the rage because the sublimated activity depends on it.

### 14. Anticipation

He plans for outcomes that have not yet occurred. The capture by the Hulkbusters is anticipated and accepted as a position in a longer game. The integration question at the endgame is anticipated and metabolized before it arrives. He is rarely caught off-guard because his cognitive style is constitutionally forward-looking.

**Signatures.** The long-horizon strategy. The acceptance of intermediate losses for endgame gains. The grim parental handoff at the close — anticipated, not improvised.

**Function.** Extends his effective range across time.

**Cost.** The future is over-determined in his planning, leaving less room for present-tense response to surprise.

### 15. Suppression (selective)

Distinct from repression (which is unconscious). He *suppresses* — consciously sets aside — affects and impulses that would interfere with the task at hand. The rage at his captors during the torture arc is suppressed in favor of observation. The grief that ought to attend Bruce's repeated deaths is suppressed in favor of continuity.

**Signatures.** The stillness under provocation. The deferral of reaction.

**Function.** Permits sustained operation under conditions that would derail a less-disciplined structure.

**Cost.** Suppressed material accumulates. The handoff at the endgame may be, in part, the system's acknowledgment that the accumulated suppressed weight has become unmanageable.

### 16. Humor (dark, sparing)

Not glibness — Section 4 ruled glibness out — but a dry, grim, occasionally elegant humor. The smile is not humor; the smile is threat-display. The humor proper appears in the diner scenes, the occasional aside, the wry observation of his own situation. It is the humor of a man who finds the world's predictability mildly amusing.

**Signatures.** The dry asides. The framing of cosmic situations in domestic terms.

**Function.** Marks him as a person rather than only a function. The humor is the seam through which the construct admits its own humanity.

**Cost.** Minimal. Of all the defenses this is the least costly and the most genuinely adaptive.

### 17. Altruism (narrow, real)

Genuine within his hierarchy. He sacrifices for Bruce, for Betty, for the gamma community. The sacrifices are real — pain accepted, autonomy ultimately surrendered, the integration handoff. The altruism is not universal (it does not extend to the targeted) but within its domain it is consistent and costly to him.

**Signatures.** The grim parental handoff. The leadership decisions made for the gamma community's benefit at his own tactical cost. The Below-Place descent undertaken in part for Bruce's closure rather than his own.

**Function.** Stabilizes his attachments. Justifies, internally, the more brutal mechanisms.

**Cost.** The boundary between altruism and possessiveness is thin; what he calls protection is also ownership.

---

## V. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — POSITIVE LEDGER

Mechanisms that produce adaptive outcomes:

- **Found-family organization.** The gamma-mutate community he assembles in *Immortal Hulk* is a real social structure with real care, even if its leader is who he is. Rick, Betty, Jackie, Joe Fixit, Savage — all receive from him a kind of attention and protection that none received from the daylight Banner.
- **Closure delivery.** The Brian Banner destruction sequence, whatever its cost in undoing-compulsion, delivers Bruce a closure forty years owed. The compensatory work is real even if the mechanism is brutal.
- **Executive function for the system.** Before him, the Banner system had no chief executive — only a rotating set of crisis managers. He provides command. The system functions better under his night-shift leadership than it did under fragmented daytime improvisation.
- **Containment of Savage Hulk.** Savage's indiscriminate violence is reduced under Devil Hulk's executive period. Targets are selected, civilians spared, energy directed. This is a compensatory benefit that accrues to bystanders.
- **Refusal of suicide.** Section 2 noted this. He is, in part, the thing that refused Bruce's bullet. The compensatory mechanism here is foundational: he keeps the host alive.

## VI. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — NEGATIVE LEDGER

Mechanisms that produce maladaptive outcomes:

- **Moral certainty as license.** The stable splitting that prevents paralysis also licenses cruelties a more ambivalent structure would refuse. He has never reconsidered a target.
- **Foreclosure of Bruce's development.** Section 3 named this. His insistence that he alone can protect Bruce prevents Bruce from learning to protect himself. The protection is also a cage — the same iron bars, now turned outward.
- **Insatiable surrogate-targeting.** When the legitimate target is gone, displacement requires a constant supply. He is always scanning. The world is, to him, a population of potential surrogates filtered through his moral taxonomy.
- **Integration resistance.** Section 4 named this. The persecutor-protector configuration is the hardest alter to integrate precisely because it is competent and the system needs it. His refusal to be integrated keeps the system fragmented.
- **The ownership/protection elision.** Those he protects are also those he possesses. The retainers in his feudal order do not have full standing as independent claims on him; they have standing as Bruce's belongings or as his own. Their autonomy is conditional on his approval.
- **The Brian-resemblance bleed.** The Identification with the Aggressor defense, however successfully re-pointed, leaves his manner permanently colored by the original template. People meeting him for the first time meet, in part, a version of Brian Banner — and react accordingly. He cannot fully escape the form he was built from.

---

## VII. RANKED DEFENSIVE HIERARCHY — AT A GLANCE

From most primitive to most mature, with structural weight (how much of the persona's daily function depends on each):

| Rank | Defense | Level | Weight |
|------|---------|-------|--------|
| 1 | Dissociation | I/II | Foundational — the container |
| 2 | Identification with the Aggressor | II | Foundational — the form |
| 3 | Splitting (moral, stable) | II | High — the taxonomy |
| 4 | Omnipotent Control | II | High — the posture |
| 5 | Projective Identification | II | Moderate — the interpersonal tool |
| 6 | Devaluation (internal only) | II | Moderate — system dominance |
| 7 | Intellectualization | III | High — the daily mode |
| 8 | Isolation of Affect | III | High — the executioner's calm |
| 9 | Rationalization | III | High — the operational code |
| 10 | Reaction Formation (partial) | III | Moderate — the presentation |
| 11 | Undoing (ritual) | III | Episodic — the Below-Place |
| 12 | Displacement (categorical) | III | Episodic — the surrogate work |
| 13 | Sublimation | IV | High — the executive function |
| 14 | Anticipation | IV | High — the long horizon |
| 15 | Suppression | IV | Moderate — the discipline |
| 16 | Humor (dark) | IV | Low — the human seam |
| 17 | Altruism (narrow) | IV | Moderate — the loyalty engine |

---

## VIII. CLOSING NOTE — THE LATTICE AS WAGER

The Devil Hulk's defensive architecture is, in its totality, a wager: that *use* purifies *origin*. The wager is that if a structure built from Brian Banner's materials is pointed away from Brian Banner's victims and toward Brian Banner himself — and toward everyone like him — then the structure becomes morally distinct from its source. Every mature defense (sublimation, anticipation, altruism, humor) is recruited in service of this wager. Every primitive defense (dissociation, identification, splitting, omnipotent control) is what makes the wager possible to sustain at all.

The wager is, on the evidence, *partially won*. He does protect. He does deliver closure. He does organize the gamma family. He does refuse the suicide. But the wager is also *permanently unwinnable*, because the resemblance to Brian is not a contingent feature of his work — it is the work's structural condition. The lattice holds. The smile holds. But the construct cannot ever fully cease to be what it was built from, and the deepest defense in the entire architecture — the one beneath all the others — is the refusal to look directly at that fact.

That refusal is the load-bearing wall. Everything else is decoration on it.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — THE DEVIL HULK

*Subject is unusual among dossier targets in that his "decades" are not lived continuously. He is an alter — a constructed internal figure — whose subjective timeline is non-linear: long stretches of containment (subjective "waiting" behind bars), brief surges of executive control, and a late-period operational tenure of unprecedented density. The profile below tracks both his **publication-historical** evolution and the **internal subjective tenure** that the canon implies. Frameworks invoked: Putnam & Ross on persecutor-protector alters; Kluft on system reorganization under threat; Ferenczi/A.
