Freud on identification with the aggressor; Bowlby on hierarchical attachment; Kernberg on splitting; Linehan on regulation-by-certainty; Vaillant's mature/immature defense hierarchy.*

---

## I. THE PRE-FORMATION SUBSTRATE (c. 1969–1976 of Bruce's biography; *Incredible Hulk* #312, Mantlo, as retroactive canon)

Before the Devil Hulk exists as a discrete alter, the *materials* exist. The Mantlo "Crossroads" arc and the flashbacks woven through it establish the conditions: Brian Banner — alcoholic, gamma-paranoid, wife-beater, eventually wife-killer — terrorizing a precociously intelligent child whose primary cognitive coping strategy was already, by age four or five, **observational hypervigilance dressed as intellectual detachment**. The pre-Devil-Hulk child Bruce was watching his father the way a naturalist watches a dangerous animal: cataloguing the cues for incoming violence, charting the alcohol cycle, learning which words triggered which beatings.

This is the developmental loam. Under Putnam's model, the alter that will become the Devil Hulk is being *prefigured* in this period as a dissociative compartment that holds (a) the observations themselves — the catalogued knowledge of how a frightening adult man operates — and (b) the impermissible fantasy that the child might one day be larger, calmer, and more lethal than his father. He is not yet a voice. He is a *file*.

**Affect regulation in this phase:** none of his own; he is a depository for affect that the child cannot process — terror, murderous rage, and a particular cold satisfaction at observed weakness in the abuser (Brian drunk, Brian sleeping, Brian wrong). These affects, banked, become his eventual baseline temperament.

**Cognitive style in this phase:** purely receptive. Pattern-acquisition. The lifelong predatory patience begins here as the child's enforced stillness during episodes of household violence.

**Self-concept in this phase:** does not exist. He is, at this stage, a structural negative — the shape of what the child needs but does not have.

---

## II. CONSOLIDATION AND CONTAINMENT (c. age 6–9 through gamma exposure; subjective "the waiting begins")

Between the maternal homicide and the gamma bomb, the Banner system completes its primary fracture. Savage Hulk consolidates as the affect-bearer (terror-rage of the child swinging back). Joe Fixit will later consolidate as the agency-bearer (the streetwise adult Bruce could not be). The Devil Hulk consolidates here as the **executive-aggressor** — the imagined-adult who can do what the child cannot.

His **first stable self-concept** dates from this period and never substantively changes: *I am the one who will kill him for what he did to us.* This is a sentence written into the alter's foundation. Every later behavior is a variation on it.

He is, by the system's own internal architecture (made explicit in IH vol.2 #13, 2000), **caged from the moment of his consolidation**. The bars are not imposed externally; they are the system's recognition that the alter is *too dangerous to its own host* to be allowed surface-time. He is, in Kluft's terminology, a *sequestered persecutor*: the system fears him, restricts him, and (crucially) preserves him. The preservation is the tell — a system that genuinely wished him gone would not maintain such a vivid internal architecture for his containment. He is being saved.

**Affect regulation:** the foundational achievement of this period is the *conversion of murderous affect into postural stillness*. He learns to wait without degrading. This is the single most important psychological capacity he will ever develop, and it is fully present in adolescence.

**Cognitive style:** the strategic patience matures into something approaching a *theory of time as ally*. Where Savage Hulk lives in the eternal present of the threatened child, Devil Hulk learns that the future can be cultivated.

**Self-concept:** the protector-executioner identity locks in. Notably, it is **already paternal in tone toward the host**. He does not consolidate as a peer or a sibling figure. From the start he addresses Bruce as a child. This means the alter was constructed by the abused child as a *parent he did not have*, not as an ally he could be. This will become operationally significant fifty publication-years later.

---

## III. THE LONG DORMANCY (1962–1999 publication; subjective "behind the bars, listening")

For nearly forty publication-years the Devil Hulk does not surface in canon at all. The Banner system, under Lee/Kirby through Mantlo through David, cycles through Savage, Grey/Fixit, Professor, and a parade of hybrids. The Devil Hulk is implied retroactively rather than present — the *Maestro* future, the cold strategic Hulk of certain David arcs, the occasional grin in the wrong moment are best read, in hindsight, as bleed-through.

What is psychologically critical about this period is that **the dormancy is itself formative**. He spends decades of subjective time in a sensory-restricted state — chained, in a basement, *hearing* Bruce's life but unable to act. This is, in dissociative-systems terms, a near-perfect deprivation environment: the alter has only Bruce's experience as input, only his own monologue as cognition, and only his consolidated mission as orientation. Three psychological consequences:

1. **Affect regulation deepens by atrophy of alternatives.** With no opportunity to act, the alter loses access to any affective register *other* than the patient/calm/predatory baseline. By the time he surfaces in 2000, he has no other speeds.

2. **Cognitive style becomes seminar-shaped.** Decades of internal monologue without interlocutors produces a personality that, when it finally speaks, *lectures*. The Devil Hulk's signature cadence — measured, declarative, almost pedagogical — is the speech pattern of a mind that has been rehearsing for forty years. He does not converse; he *delivers*.

3. **Self-concept calcifies into vocational certainty.** Where most personalities develop self-concept through interaction and correction, his develops through uninterrupted self-narration. He emerges in 2000 with a self-understanding more coherent than Bruce's own — because nothing has ever challenged it.

A clinical reader should note: this is precisely the developmental profile that produces the most treatment-resistant persecutor-protector alters in the real DID literature. The longer such an alter is sequestered, the more internally consistent and externally unyielding it becomes.

---

## IV. FIRST SURFACE — THE JENKINS DECADE (2000–2010 publication; "the chained interview")

In *Incredible Hulk* vol.2 #13 (Jenkins, 2000) the Devil Hulk becomes a documented entity. Doc Samson's hypnotic descent gives the clinical record its founding artifact: the alter introduces himself, states his attachment ("I love him"), states his mission ("I will kill everyone who has ever hurt him, starting with his father"), and states his containment status (chained, behind bars, by the system itself).

Three clinical observations from this period:

**(a) The affect on emergence is regulated to an unnerving degree.** He does not strain at the bars. He does not roar at Samson. He *engages the therapist*. He is, in his own way, a model patient — articulate, on-topic, candid about his agenda. This is diagnostic. A persecutor-protector with this much surface composure on first contact has been doing internal work for a very long time.

**(b) The self-concept is fully formed and stable.** He does not negotiate his identity; he reports it. He calls Bruce "my boy" — the diminutive is automatic, unselfconscious, and reveals the parental frame in a single phrase. The hierarchical attachment structure (Bowlby, modified for an internal object) is already present in its eventual feudal form.

**(c) Cognitive style is forensic-prosecutorial.** He has a list. He has a sequence. He has prioritized targets. He has, in effect, prepared a case file on every person who has ever harmed Bruce Banner, and he can articulate the indictment. This is not rage. This is law.

What does **not** yet exist in this decade is operational tenure. He is interviewed, characterized, occasionally heard from — but he does not run the body. His role in the system through the Jenkins, Jones, Pak, and Aaron eras remains that of the *last resort the system refuses to use*. The other Hulks treat his existence as evidence of the system's pathology, not as a resource.

Psychologically the most important fact of this decade is that he **does not deteriorate under continued containment**. Most psychiatric structures held this long under this much pressure would either escape, decompensate, or fade. He does none of these. He maintains. The maintenance is itself a demonstration of the regulatory capacity that will define his later operational period.

---

## V. THE LATENT DECADE (2010–2017 publication; "listening to the storm")

Through *World War Hulk*, *Indestructible Hulk*, *Totally Awesome Hulk*, and the death of Bruce Banner at the hands of Hawkeye (*Civil War II*, 2016), the Devil Hulk remains structurally present and operationally silent. The flickers in this period are real but minor — the cunning Hulk of certain WWH beats, the strategic Hulk in select Waid sequences — and are best read as bleed-through rather than emergence.

Psychologically this decade is defined by two slow movements:

**(1) Bruce's life conditions are deteriorating in a direction the Devil Hulk was built for.** Hunted, isolated, eventually murdered, Bruce is being subjected to exactly the external threat profile that justifies a persecutor-protector taking the wheel. The system is, throughout this decade, *building pressure on the bars*.

**(2) The alter is updating his target list silently.** When he finally surfaces in 2018 he does so with a fully developed model of the modern threat environment — Fortean, Shadow Base, the Leader, the corporate gamma economy. He has been doing the homework. The lecturer has been preparing his syllabus.

Affect regulation in this period: undisturbed. Cognitive style: the patient observation deepens into something resembling a strategic-intelligence analyst's running file. Self-concept: unchanged — still the executor, still waiting.

---

## VI. EMERGENCE AND OPERATIONAL TENURE — THE EWING PERIOD (2018–2021 publication; "out of the room")

This is the only period in his existence in which the Devil Hulk runs the body for a sustained stretch, and consequently the only period from which a full clinical profile can be drawn from observed behavior rather than inferred from structure. The triggering events — Bruce shot by Tommy Hill, resurrection via the Green Door, system reorganization — produce a circadian binding in which the Devil Hulk takes the night.

### Affect regulation in the operational period

The capacity demonstrated is, by any clinical standard, **extraordinary**. The behavioral set-pieces are unambiguous:

- **Under torture (the Hulkbusters/Shadow Base capture arcs):** acid, dismemberment, vivisection — and the affective signature throughout is *attention*. He registers pain (the regeneration suggests the pain is real) and does nothing with it except *learn*. This is regulation-by-conversion: a noxious affect is metabolized into an instrumental cognition. Linehan's distress-tolerance framework reaches its theoretical ceiling here; he is past tolerance into transmutation.

- **Under provocation (Jackie McGee's hostile interviews, Fortean's taunts):** no escalation. The verbal style becomes drier, the eye contact steadier, the smile slightly fixed. Provocation tightens him rather than expanding him.

- **Under loss (Sasquatch's near-killing, the deaths within the gamma family, the recurring damage to Betty):** grief is present but channelized — it converts directly into target-selection. He does not mourn before he acts; he mourns *by* acting.

- **Under the prospect of his own dissolution (the integration arcs, the negotiated handoffs of the endgame):** the regulation finally shows its only crack. He becomes more verbal, more pedagogical, more insistent on his own indispensability. The defense pattern under existential threat is *teach harder*.

The signature affect remains the smile — and a careful read of its deployments shows it is not a single smile but **three distinct ones**: (a) the recognition-smile when meeting a new gamma-touched person (faintly indulgent, like a teacher seeing a familiar student); (b) the verdict-smile when a target has just sealed their categorization (small, closed-mouth, unmoving); (c) the work-smile during execution (wider, fixed, the affect of a man enjoying his vocation). The taxonomy of his smiles is itself the most reliable indicator of his internal state available to an external observer.

### Cognitive style in the operational period

The Ewing tenure permits a granular read:

- **Long-horizon strategic planning.** He allows capture in order to study captors. He recruits Jackie McGee by *letting her doubt*, knowing belief produced by her own reasoning will hold and belief produced by his persuasion will not. He manages the system from within — running Bruce, managing Savage, deploying Fixit — like an executive managing a difficult team.

- **Forensic-investigative orientation.** The early arcs are structured as a series of cases. He locates gamma-touched perpetrators, evaluates the case, executes judgment. This is the *forensic file* of the chained-interview era operationalized.

- **Negotiation as default mode in non-combat contexts.** The Hell arc is the cleanest evidence. Faced with cosmic horror that should produce either despair or fury, he produces *terms*. He bargains. Savage Hulk would rage; Banner would collapse; the Devil Hulk treats Hell as a counterparty.

- **Pedagogical communication.** He explains himself. He explains the gamma. He explains the system. He explains, even to enemies, what is about to happen and why. This is the seminar-shaped cognition of the long dormancy, finally with students.

- **Refusal of abstraction.** Despite the lecturing manner, his moral reasoning is concrete, case-by-case, and personal. He does not pursue justice; he pursues *people*. The cognitive style is prosecutorial rather than philosophical.

### Self-concept in the operational period

The self-concept presents in operation exactly as it was reported in the 2000 interview, but with one important development: he now has **vocational evidence**. Where the 2000 Devil Hulk was a self-narrated executor with no record, the 2018–2021 Devil Hulk has a portfolio. The Hulkbusters arc, the Shadow Base dismantling, the gamma family, the Brian Banner confrontation — these are the deliverables that confirm to him what he always believed about himself.

The consequence is that his self-concept hardens in a direction his earlier self could not access: from *prepared* to *proven*. This produces the only genuine grandiose risk in his profile. He does not become narcissistic, but he does become *certain* in a way that begins to crowd out the system's other voices. The Professor Hulk merger appears to him not as an aspiration but as a category error. He is the adult; merger is a child's request.

The parental frame toward Bruce intensifies. The "my boy" of 2000 becomes, in operational practice, a near-total custodial stance — he handles Bruce's body, Bruce's enemies, Bruce's friends, Bruce's grief. There is genuine love in this and genuine foreclosure. He protects Bruce from the world and from Bruce's own growth in roughly equal measure.

### The Brian Banner confrontation as psychological pivot

The Below-Place sequence in which the Devil Hulk is finally given the original target is the single most clinically interesting event in his record. The promise made in 2000 is kept literally in 2020. What is notable is that **the act does not discharge him**. The ritual repetition — he tears Brian's soul apart, and again, and again — indicates that the construction was not designed for closure. He was built to *pursue* the father, not to *be done* with the father. When the object is achieved, the structure does not dissolve; it perseverates.

This is diagnostically important. It confirms that the alter's organizing principle was never revenge as catharsis but **vigilance as identity**. He does not exist *in order to* kill Brian; he exists *as* the killing-of-Brian, ongoingly. Closure is impossible because closure would be self-erasure.

### The endgame integration sequence

The final arc's negotiated handoff — in which the Devil Hulk does not rebel but assents, in a posture explicitly paternal-handoff in tone — is psychologically coherent with everything preceding. He cannot be defeated, and he cannot be argued out of his self-concept. He can only be *thanked*, *credited*, and *invited* to step back. The Ewing endgame, by tracking the real DID-treatment literature on persecutor-protector integration almost line by line (recruitment over suppression, gratitude over banishment, role-redefinition over annihilation), produces the only viable resolution: he does not stop being the protector; he agrees to share the post.

---

## VII. CROSS-DECADE TRAJECTORY — THE THREE VECTORS

Synthesizing across the timeline:

**Affect regulation.** *Stable from consolidation; deepened by dormancy; demonstrated under operational stress.* The regulation never had to evolve because it was complete by adolescence. The decades of dormancy stripped away alternative affective registers (no playful Devil Hulk exists, no anxious one, no depressive one) leaving only the predatory baseline. Operational tenure proved the regulation under maximal load. The single observable evolution is the *granularization* of expression — by 2020 he has a wider palette of micro-affects (the three smiles, the closed-mouth verdict, the indulgent teacher's look) without ever broadening his underlying tonal range.

**Cognitive style.** *Receptive in childhood; rehearsed in dormancy; pedagogical in operation.* The clearest evolution is from observation to monologue to seminar. The strategic patience was native; the lecturing cadence was earned by forty years of internal speech without audience; the executive function — running the gamma community, managing the system, conducting cross-arc investigations — was latent capacity finally given a stage. The cognitive style **did not change; it found its scope.**

**Self-concept.** *Locked at consolidation; confirmed in interview; proven in operation; hardened in endgame.* The single sentence — *I am the one who will protect him and kill what hurts him* — is invariant across his entire existence. What changes is the evidentiary basis: from imagined to declared to demonstrated to indispensable. The risk this trajectory carries is the crowding-out of the system's other developmental possibilities; the achievement it represents is that an alter built by a terrified child held its shape for sixty publication-years and, when finally called, delivered exactly what it had promised.

---

## VIII. CLINICAL SUMMARY

The Devil Hulk's longitudinal psychology is, paradoxically, **almost without longitudinal change in the conventional sense**. He is not a personality that grew. He is a structure that *waited*, fully formed, for the operational conditions it had been built to handle. His decades of dormancy were not developmental delay but *preservation*. His operational tenure was not maturation but *expression*.

What evolved was the system around him: Bruce's external threat environment, the other alters' capacity to hold the line, the system's recognition of what it had locked in the basement. The Devil Hulk himself is the rare clinical phenomenon of a personality structure built early, contained long, and released intact — a forty-year argument that, under sufficiently brutal conditions in childhood, a mind can construct, file away, and ultimately deploy an internal adult more functional than any the host's lived development could have produced.

He is the protector the child invented, kept by the system because no replacement was ever built, and finally trusted because no replacement was ever needed.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: "The Devil Hulk" — Alter within the Banner System

*Prepared as a stand-alone psychiatric workup of one identity-state. The host (Bruce Banner) and the other alters (Savage, Fixit, Professor, Green Scar/Worldbreaker, the deeper green abyssal stratum) are referenced only as they bear on this subject. The conventional caveat that fictional subjects cannot be diagnosed is acknowledged and set aside; the canon is dense enough — Jenkins 2000, Ewing 2018–2021, with supporting material across Pak, Aaron, Waid, Duggan — to support formulation in the same way clinicians formulate from a thick longitudinal record.*

---

## 1. Frame of Reference and Methodological Notes

Three frame-choices govern this section.

**First**, the subject is approached as an *identity-state*, not as a person. DSM-5-TR (300.14) and ICD-11 (6B64) both define dissociative identity disorder by the presence of "two or more distinct personality states," each with its own characteristic patterns of perceiving, relating to, and thinking about the self and the environment. The Devil Hulk satisfies these criteria so consistently — across two decades and dozens of writers — that he merits independent formulation. The fact that he shares a body with Banner is, for this section, an anatomical detail, not a diagnostic objection.

**Second**, the assessment uses the ISSTD (International Society for the Study of Trauma and Dissociation) *Guidelines for Treating Dissociative Identity Disorder in Adults* (3rd revision) as the operative clinical framework, supplemented by the *Theory of Structural Dissociation of the Personality* (van der Hart, Nijenhuis, Steele) and the contemporary literature on persecutor/protector alters (Blizard, Howell, Kluft, Chefetz). These frameworks are essential because mainstream DSM nosology lacks the granularity to describe within-system pathology; the structural-dissociation language ("Emotional Part," "Apparently Normal Part," "fight-substate") is what actually fits.

**Third**, the assessment refuses the popular shorthand by which Hulk-canon discourse collapses all alters into "Hulk." The Savage Hulk, the Devil Hulk, Joe Fixit, the Professor, the Green Scar, and the inchoate gamma-abyss persona are *six different conditions in one body*. The Devil Hulk in particular has been continually misread by in-universe psychiatrists (Samson most notably) because he presents as the most monstrous and therefore reads as the most pathological. The opposite is closer to true: he is the most *organized* part of the system and, in clinical terms, one of its most functional structures.

---

## 2. Principal Diagnosis (System-Level)

**Dissociative Identity Disorder (DSM-5-TR 300.14; ICD-11 6B64),** severe, chronic, with prominent persecutor/protector configuration and gamma-mediated somatic switching.

The Banner system meets all five DSM-5-TR A–E criteria without strain:

- **A. Disruption of identity** by two or more distinct personality states, with marked discontinuity in sense of self and sense of agency, accompanied by related alterations in affect, behavior, consciousness, memory, perception, cognition, and sensorimotor functioning. *In this system the discontinuity is externally visible* — somatotype itself switches with the alter. This is not standard for DID (which is usually invisible to observers), but it does not exclude the diagnosis; it intensifies it.
- **B. Recurrent gaps in the recall of everyday events, important personal information, and/or traumatic events** inconsistent with ordinary forgetting. Banner's documented amnesia for what "the other guy" did is canonical.
- **C. Clinically significant distress or impairment.** Self-evident.
- **D. Not a normal part of a broadly accepted cultural or religious practice.**
- **E. Not attributable to substances or another medical condition.** The gamma exposure complicates this — one could argue the gamma *is* a medical condition — but the dissociative architecture predates the bomb and was elaborated, not caused, by it. The system existed in childhood; gamma gave it bodies.

The Devil Hulk is one of the system's alters. The rest of this section is about him.

---

## 3. Alter-Specific Formulation

### 3.1 Structural classification

Within the Structural Dissociation framework, the Devil Hulk is an **Emotional Part (EP)** organized around the **fight defensive substate** — but he is a developmentally late and unusually elaborated EP, having recruited executive functions normally reserved for the **Apparently Normal Part (ANP)**. This crossover is what makes him unusual. Standard EPs are stuck-in-trauma fragments that activate only under threat cue and have minimal capacity for daily life. The Devil Hulk runs investigations, manages personnel, conducts journalism (via his alliance with Jackie McGee), negotiates with infernal entities, and orders coffee at diners. He has, in clinical shorthand, **"crossed the line"** — an EP that has acquired ANP-like functioning under conditions of sustained external demand. The Ewing-era arcs are essentially the record of this crossing.

In Kluft's typology (1984, 1988, 1999) he is a **Persecutor Alter of Protective Origin** — what Blizard (1997, 2003) reclassified as a **Protector-Persecutor** to capture the dual valence. Such alters present to host and clinicians as internal threats (they frighten the host, they threaten violence against self or others, they appear allied with the abuser) while in fact discharging a *protective* function: they hold the abuser's affect so the host does not have to, they organize fight-defense so the host can remain in collapse or freeze, and they retain identification with the abuser's competencies (his strength, his command, his unflinching cruelty) and re-point those competencies outward against the abuser's class of targets.

The IH #13 (2000) scene is a textbook first-encounter with such an alter: caged, fearsome, articulate, declaring love for the host *and* a homicidal agenda in the same sentence, naming the original abuser as the first target. Samson, conducting the hypnosis, reacts with appropriate clinical alarm and inappropriate clinical conclusion: he treats containment as success. The literature is explicit that this is the wrong move. Persecutor-protectors that are merely caged do not disappear; they wait. The Ewing arc, beginning in 2018, is what that wait looks like when external conditions finally summon the alter into operational role.

### 3.2 Symptom presentation in behavior

A persecutor-protector alter is identified clinically by a characteristic cluster. Each item is documented in the Devil Hulk record:

1. **Identification with the abuser's manner.** The Devil Hulk's affect — cold, controlling, smiling, paternalistic in a way that is also frightening — is a direct sensory match for Brian Banner. He calls Bruce "my boy." Brian called Bruce things very similar in their possessive register. The mimicry is not coincidence; it is the mechanism.

2. **Inversion of the abuser's targets.** Brian's violence was aimed at his wife and son. The Devil Hulk's violence is aimed at people who do to others what Brian did to Rebecca and Bruce. The vector is reversed; the energetics are identical.

3. **Host-directed possessiveness with paternal coloration.** He treats Bruce as a child to be sheltered, not as an adult to be respected. This is the protector face of the persecutor coin: the same logic that licenses lethal violence outward licenses the suppression of the host's autonomy inward.

4. **Containment behind symbolic bars in the inner world.** Almost universal in this alter-type. IH #13 depicts it literally.

5. **Refusal of integration framed as fear of irrelevance.** Not fear of death (he has died and returned more than any character in the Marvel canon and treats this as routine), but fear that the system will no longer need him. Clinically this is the form of resistance most reliably encountered with this alter-type.

6. **Sublimation of homicidal drive into structured projects.** Investigation, leadership of Gamma Flight, the Shadow Base operations, the journalistic feed to McGee. EPs that have crossed the line into ANP function characteristically do this — they need a *case* to organize the drive, and they will manufacture one if none is provided.

7. **Affect regulation built on certainty, not on emotional capacity.** He does not regulate by feeling less; he regulates by *knowing more*. His stillness under torture is not stoicism; it is the calm of a man who is already several moves ahead.

8. **Internal hierarchy management.** Persecutor-protectors that have crossed into ANP function commonly assume executive role over other alters. The Devil Hulk does this with Savage (handled as a frightened child), Fixit (handled as a delinquent), and the Professor (treated as a failed compromise to be quietly disregarded). He does *not* claim authority over Banner himself; the deference there is doctrinal.

### 3.3 Etiology

The etiology is overdetermined and clean. The standard developmental prerequisites for DID with a persecutor-protector configuration are: (i) severe, repeated, unpredictable interpersonal trauma; (ii) onset before identity consolidation (typically before age 6–9); (iii) a perpetrator who is also a caregiver, producing the disorganized attachment substrate that disposes the child to dissociative defense; (iv) absence of a protective adult to whom the child can flee; (v) sufficient innate cognitive capacity to elaborate the dissociative architecture into separate personality states rather than fragmentary states only.

Bruce Banner's history satisfies each precondition with documentary force:

- Brian Banner's physical abuse of Bruce, beginning in early childhood, escalating in unpredictable cycles tied to Brian's paranoia about Bruce's intelligence and presumed mutant status.
- Brian's murder of Rebecca Banner, witnessed (and in the Bill Mantlo retcon, in some readings, partially perpetrated under coercion). The witnessing of intimate-partner homicide by the surviving parent is one of the most severe known traumatic stressors for a child and is highly correlated with full DID outcomes.
- The unavailability of any protective adult during the formative period; the institutional placements and the extended family were variably hostile or indifferent.
- Bruce's documented prodigy-level cognitive functioning, which provides the architectural capacity for elaborated alters rather than fragments.

The Devil Hulk specifically is, on this evidence, the **introjected protective-paternal figure the child was denied** — built, of necessity, out of the only adult-male template available, which was the abuser. This is not a metaphor; it is how the construction worked. The child's mind, requiring a protector and having no model for one, took the affect and competencies of the dangerous adult in the house and rebuilt them facing the other way. The first promise the alter makes, decades later in IH #13, is to kill that adult. The first promise is also the founding logic.

### 3.4 Course over time

**1960s–1990s (pre-emergence; unconscious era).** The alter is present but unsurfaced. Hints in the cunning Hulk variants of the Mantlo and David runs ("Mr. Fixit" period, the merged Professor) suggest a third intelligence operating beneath the manifest Hulks, but no clean identification. Clinically, this is consistent with persecutor-protector alters that remain bound by the system's defensive structure until either treatment or massive external stressor brings them forward.

**2000 (Jenkins; first formal contact).** Samson's hypnotic descent permits identification but not engagement. The alter remains caged. This is — and is now widely recognized in the trauma literature as — the *worst* clinical posture: the alter has been seen and named but not enlisted. He waits. The interval that follows is, in his own subjective time, the wait.

**2000–2018 (latency).** Largely silent. Occasional surfacing under conditions resembling his operational profile (the more calculating Hulk of WWH; some of Pak's gladiator-era calm) but no claim of identity-state.

**2018–2021 (Ewing; full emergence and operational period).** Triggered by Bruce's death and resurrection — the system reorganizes after the host's failure to survive ordinary means, and the persecutor-protector takes the night shift. The arc that follows is, in clinical translation, the longitudinal record of a persecutor-protector that has crossed into ANP function and is now running the system's external life under threat conditions.

**Endgame.** The eventual posture — negotiated handoff rather than rebellion — corresponds to what the ISSTD guidelines describe as the optimal late-phase outcome for this alter-type: not "integration" in the older fusion sense, but *cooperation with diminished primacy*, in which the alter relinquishes operational dominance in exchange for continued recognition. The Ewing endgame is, in this sense, technically correct treatment depicted as narrative.

---

## 4. Comorbid and Co-Occurring Conditions (System-Level, Bearing on the Subject)

The Devil Hulk does not exist alone in a body; he inherits and is shaped by the rest of the system's pathology. The relevant comorbidities:

- **Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder, with Dissociative Subtype (DSM-5-TR 309.81).** The system carries the full PTSD picture — intrusion, avoidance, negative alterations in cognition and mood, hyperarousal — with the dissociative-subtype marker (depersonalization/derealization). The Devil Hulk is, in part, the structural solution to the hyperarousal cluster: he holds the fight-substate so that Banner can occupy avoidance and numbing.
- **Complex PTSD (ICD-11 6B41).** Better fits the case than classical PTSD; the disturbances in self-organization (negative self-concept, affect dysregulation, interpersonal difficulties) are the substrate the alters arose to manage.
- **Major Depressive Disorder, recurrent, severe (296.33).** Resident in the Banner core. The suicide attempt that opens *Immortal Hulk* is the index event. The Devil Hulk's emergence is, in part, the system's response to the host's near-success.
- **Somatic Symptom and Related Disorders, NOS.** A reasonable formulation reads the gamma transformation itself as a chronic somatoform conversion of unbearable affect into morphological change, biologically real but psychologically motivated in its timing and triggers. The Devil Hulk's somatotype — taller, leaner, longer-limbed, grinning — is the somatized signature of *this particular affect-state* (cold predatory protectiveness) just as Savage Hulk's bulk is the somatic signature of *that* affect-state (terrified rage).
- **Disorganized Attachment (developmental, not a diagnosis).** Pervasive across all internal and external relationships. The Devil Hulk's possessive paternalism toward Bruce is a disorganized-attachment solution made architectural: he is simultaneously the frightening figure and the source of safety, exactly as Brian was.

---

## 5. Differential Diagnosis (What He Is NOT, and Why)

A persecutor-protector alter is one of the most consistently *misdiagnosed* clinical entities, because every primitive surface feature suggests a different and more familiar condition. The differential matters because each misdiagnosis would dictate a different and counterproductive intervention.

### 5.1 NOT Antisocial Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.7)

ASPD requires a *pervasive pattern* of disregard for and violation of the rights of others, present in multiple contexts, beginning by age 15, with conduct-disorder antecedents. The subject fails essentially every operational criterion.

- He has stable, long-term, intense attachments (Bruce, Betty, Rick, McGee, the gamma community).
- He keeps commitments, including commitments made at enormous cost to himself.
- He is not deceitful as a trait; he is candid to a fault with allies and even with enemies once their fate is determined.
- He is not impulsive; he is the least impulsive personality on record in the Banner system.
- His aggression is not generalized; it is moralized and targeted.
- There is no evidence of conduct disorder in the child Bruce; the developmental antecedent is wholly absent.

The surface confusion arises because he kills, and ASPD also kills. But the structural logic is opposite: ASPD acts on instrumental self-interest with affective shallowness; the Devil Hulk acts on intense affective loyalty within a rigid moral hierarchy.

### 5.2 NOT Psychopathy (Hare, PCL-R framework)

The PCL-R two-factor structure (interpersonal/affective; antisocial/lifestyle) fails to load on him. He scores essentially zero on Factor 1: he does not display glibness or superficial charm (he is grave); his sense of self-worth is functional, not grandiose; he is not pathologically deceitful; he does not lack remorse for actions he regrets (he does regret some — the corpse-violation moment is, on close reading, a system-internal failure he is aware of); his affect is not shallow (it is *narrow*, which is different); he is not callous in a generalized way; he accepts responsibility. Factor 2 items (impulsivity, irresponsibility, juvenile delinquency, criminal versatility) fail equally. The categorical differential is clean: psychopathy is *affective poverty plus antisocial lifestyle*; he has affective specificity and a hyper-organized prosocial-within-his-frame lifestyle.

### 5.3 NOT Narcissistic Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.81)

NPD requires grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy across contexts. The Devil Hulk:

- Does not seek admiration. He does not announce himself, brand himself, or solicit attention. The few monologues he delivers are functional, not self-aggrandizing.
- Is not fragile under criticism. Insult does not destabilize him.
- Does not envy. He has no record of envy directed at any character.
- Has empathy — narrow, but real — for those inside his moral perimeter. Empathic deficit in NPD is generalized; his is gated.
- Is paternalistic, which is sometimes confused with grandiosity but is structurally different (it places the self in service to the protected, not above the admiring).

### 5.4 NOT Sadistic Personality Disorder (DSM-III-R Appendix; no longer in DSM, ICD-11 dispersed)

The historical SPD construct required pleasure in cruelty as such, including cruelty toward strangers, animals, subordinates without provocation, and humiliation for its own sake. The Devil Hulk:

- Does not pursue cruelty toward unselected targets. His cruelty is selected, predicated on his moral classification of the target, and stops when the target is destroyed.
- Does not humiliate for satisfaction. He executes, sometimes with grim ceremony, but the ceremony is *bookkeeping* (his term, essentially) rather than pleasure-seeking.
- Does not enjoy fear in the abstract. He uses fear instrumentally.

The exception that requires honest accounting is the Below-Place / Brian Banner sequence, which is ritually repeated, conspicuously cruel, and arguably enjoyed. But this is a single-target compulsion; SPD requires a trait pattern.

### 5.5 NOT Identification with the Aggressor in the Ferenczian sense alone

Ferenczi's mechanism (1933) describes the abused child's incorporation of the abuser's affect to survive proximity to the abuser. The Devil Hulk uses this mechanism — he is, at the architectural level, built from it — but he is not *exhausted by* it. A pure identification-with-aggressor presentation would manifest as the survivor reproducing the abuser's behavior on the next vulnerable target (often, in adult life, the survivor's own children or partners). The Devil Hulk reproduces the abuser's *affect and competencies* but inverts the *target class*. This is one developmental step beyond pure identification — closer to what later writers (Howell, in particular) call "identification with the aggressor in the service of the self," in which the identification is harnessed for survival rather than enacted compulsively.

### 5.6 NOT Intermittent Explosive Disorder (DSM-5-TR 312.34)

IED requires recurrent behavioral outbursts representing failure of aggressive impulse control, *grossly out of proportion* to the provocation. The Devil Hulk's aggression is the opposite: it is *proportionate to his classification* of the target, deliberate, and never impulsive. Savage Hulk meets IED-like criteria; Devil Hulk decidedly does not.

### 5.7 NOT a smarter version of the Savage Hulk

This is the most common in-universe misclassification (Doc Samson errs here repeatedly across the Jones, Pak, and early Ewing periods). The differentiation is developmental and structural:

- **Savage Hulk** is a young child's terrified rage given a body. Cognitive age presents as roughly 4–7. Affect is overwhelming, modulation absent, attachments simple, vocabulary narrow.
- **Devil Hulk** is a child's *imagined adult protector* given a body. He is not Savage grown up; he is a different construction with a different developmental source-point. He cannot grow into Savage and Savage cannot grow into him. They are siblings, not stages.

Mistaking the two leads predictably to wrong interventions: trying to soothe Devil Hulk as one would Savage produces only his contempt; trying to negotiate with Savage as one would Devil Hulk produces panic in the child.

### 5.8 NOT a Malignant Tulpa, NOT a Demonic Entity, NOT a separate person in any metaphysical sense

The canon has flirted with each framing — the "Devil" name itself invites the demonic reading; the One Below All material introduces literal infernal substrate; the gamma-mythos pages of *Immortal Hulk* propose a cosmology in which the Hulks are emanations of a transcendent green. These framings are narratively interesting and clinically irrelevant. He is an alter. His phenomenology is fully described by the persecutor-protector model. The metaphysical wrapping is the system's, and the writers', mythopoetic externalization of an internal structure — itself a known feature of severe DID systems (alters routinely experience themselves as having supernatural origin; this is symptom, not ontology).

### 5.9 NOT Schizophrenia, NOT a Psychotic Disorder

There is no formal thought disorder, no negative symptoms, no hallucinatory experience that does not have a clear dissociative or trauma-intrusion explanation, no deterioration of premorbid functioning in the schizophrenia sense. The voices Bruce hears are alter-voices (dissociative), not psychotic voices. The differential is not close.

### 5.10 NOT Bipolar Disorder

No discrete mood episodes, no manic or hypomanic syndromes, no cyclic course. The alternation between Banner and the Hulks is dissociative switching, not affective cycling. (Switching is sometimes misread as ultra-rapid cycling in clinical practice; the differential is now standard in the literature.)

### 5.11 NOT a Substance-Induced Disorder

The gamma is endogenous to the body, not exogenously dosed; the alter's behav


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: "THE DEVIL HULK"

*Field reference. Cross-indexed by condition. Each entry is a tell, a habit, or a decision-rule observed across the record (primarily IH Vol. 2 #13, 2000; *Immortal Hulk* #1–50, 2018–2021) and extrapolated to the granularity a total-surveillance file would carry. Read as a tracker reads spoor.*

---

## 1. BASELINE — The Idle Configuration

The Devil Hulk at rest is not "at rest" in any human sense; he is *attending*. The default body-state is a forward-canted seat — elbows on knees if seated, weight on the balls of the feet if standing, never the spine-against-chair-back posture of a man at ease. The long arms hang or drape; he does not cross them. Crossed arms are a defensive display, and he does not perform defense.

**The smile.** Constant, asymmetric, lips closed or barely parted, the lower jaw slightly forward so the bottom teeth show before the top. It is not a social smile. It does not respond to humor. It does not widen at jokes or narrow at insults. It is a fixed feature, the way the brow of a hunting dog is fixed. When the smile *does* move — flattens — that is the tell. A flattened mouth on the Devil Hulk is the equivalent of another man drawing a weapon.

**Breath.** Slow, deep, deliberately under-paced relative to ambient stress. He breathes through the nose. Under any other condition this would suggest meditative training; in him it is the somatic consequence of a nervous system that does not register most environments as threatening.

**Eye behavior.** Yellow sclera, low blink rate (estimated well under the human ten-to-fifteen per minute). When listening, he tracks the speaker's mouth more than the eyes — reading mechanism, not affect. When thinking, he looks down and to his own right, then up; a stable, repeated micro-pattern. When deciding, the eyes go still entirely for a beat of one to two seconds. That stillness is the decision being made. Action follows within seconds.

**Hands.** Long fingers, often laced or steepled when seated, flat-palmed on surfaces when standing. He does not fidget. No drumming, no tapping, no scratching. He touches objects he intends to use and does not touch objects he does not. Pick up the surveillance footage of any diner sequence and you can predict what he will reach for by what his eyes have rested on for more than half a second.

**Voice in idle.** A low register, measured, lightly amused, sentence-final pitch dropping rather than rising — declarative cadence, not inquisitive. He uses contractions sparingly; the speech is slightly formal, slightly archaic, with a tendency toward the parental ("my boy," "child," "little one" applied to Bruce internally; "friend," "officer," "sir" applied externally with audible scare-quotes). He says please and thank you. The politeness is not a mask; it is a *contract* — he is informing the room what the rules are before he enforces them.

---

## 2. CALM — Public-Facing, Low-Threat Conditions

Most cleanly observed in the diner-counter scenes and in the early Shadow Base administrative sequences.

- Orders simple food and coffee; eats slowly; pays. Will leave a tip. The tip is exact and round, never calculated as a percentage. He is performing the ritual of normalcy and the ritual has a rhythm.
- Sits at counters and booths with sightlines to the door. He will not sit with his back to an entrance even when alone in an empty room. This is not paranoia; it is doctrine.
- Reads. Newspaper, menu, posted notice — he absorbs printed text in the environment with a completeness most subjects don't. By the time he leaves a room he has read every piece of paper in it.
- Conversation pattern with strangers: brief, courteous, terminating. He answers questions with one to two sentences and asks none in return except those required for the transaction. He does not banter. He does not flirt. He does not perform small talk and so when he chooses to extend a conversation it is because he has identified the interlocutor as relevant.
- With Jackie McGee (early arcs): permits longer conversations. Tells: leans back slightly when she speaks (the only context in which the forward cant relaxes); the smile becomes mobile; he gives her room to draw her own conclusions and visibly waits while she does. He is the only Hulk persona who can *wait through another person's sentence.*
- Decision habit in calm: he prefers the option that *also* gathers information. Faced with two equivalent paths he will take the one that puts more data in his hands. This is the most reliable predictor of his choices across the record.

---

## 3. INTERNAL — Conditions Inside the Banner System

Observed across mindscape sequences (IH #13, 2000; *Immortal Hulk* mindscape arcs, particularly the "head conferences" with Banner, Savage, Fixit, and the Professor configuration).

- He convenes; he does not attend. Other personae are summoned to him in the internal landscape; he does not travel to them.
- Toward Banner: he kneels or stoops. Physical lowering. The voice goes softer. He uses "my boy" and "child." He does not contradict Banner directly; he *redirects* Banner the way a parent redirects a toddler away from a stove.
- Toward Savage Hulk: short sentences, imperative mood, occasional hand on the shoulder. He treats Savage as the frightened child Savage in fact is. No contempt visible. Real fondness.
- Toward Joe Fixit: a sharper register, dry, the smile cooler. He treats Fixit as a delinquent he has not yet decided whether to discipline or use. Fixit knows it.
- Toward the Professor configuration / merged-Hulk states: cold. The closest the Devil Hulk comes to overt hostility within the system. His pressure point — being made irrelevant by a successful merger — is exposed here, and the temperature drops accordingly.
- Decision habit internally: he speaks last. He listens to every other persona's position before stating his own, and his stated position is rarely a position so much as an *instruction*. The system has, by the *Immortal Hulk* era, accepted this hierarchy.

---

## 4. STRESS — Pressure Without Imminent Violence

The diagnostic signature: he does not escalate by amplifying. He escalates by *narrowing*. As external stress climbs, his observable behavior contracts.

- Voice goes quieter, not louder. Subordinates and enemies both lean in to hear him; the leaning is itself the submission he is extracting.
- Sentences shorten. Calm-state Devil Hulk uses paragraphs; stressed Devil Hulk uses clauses; severely stressed Devil Hulk uses single words and the single word is usually a name.
- The body slows. He will literally walk more slowly into a situation that another persona would charge.
- He picks one person in the room and looks only at them. The locked-on attention is reallocated from the environment to the chosen target. Once that selection happens, the outcome is decided; only the choreography remains.
- He removes obstacles before threats. A door, a piece of furniture, a hostage — he resolves the geometry of the room before resolving its inhabitants.
- Tell: a single nod, slow, to himself, immediately preceding action. The internal verdict has been recorded.
- Decision habit under stress: he chooses the option that *ends the matter*. Where the calm Devil Hulk gathers information, the stressed Devil Hulk closes accounts. The shift from information-mode to closure-mode is the single most important behavioral pivot in his record.

---

## 5. THREAT — Imminent Violence, Self or Others

Cleanest readings: the Hulkbuster engagements, the Abomination encounters in *Immortal Hulk*, the gas-station sequence (#1), the Xemnu and Leader confrontations.

- He absorbs the first blow. Not strategically — *liturgically*. The first attack against him is permitted, often invited. He uses it to read the attacker's commitment, technique, fear level, and chain of command. The Hulkbuster acid bath and dismemberment arc is the extreme expression of this rule: he accepted being taken apart in order to read the men taking him apart.
- He speaks during violence. Where Savage Hulk roars and Worldbreaker is silent, the Devil Hulk *narrates*. He addresses the target by name when he knows it, by role when he doesn't ("soldier," "officer," "doctor"). Naming is part of the punishment. He is informing the target what is being done to them and why.
- He selects a body part for the first strike based on the target's apparent self-image. Faces for the vain. Hands for the skilled. Weapons for the proud. This is not mythologized; it is observed across multiple engagements.
- He does not pursue runners *immediately*. He lets distance open, then closes it at a walk. The walk is the signature. Subjects under surveillance who have seen this walk and survived it describe it identically: he does not appear to be moving fast and he arrives anyway.
- He kills cleanly when killing is the verdict and slowly when slowness is the verdict. The distinction matters. A clean kill means the target's crime was generic; a slow kill means the target's crime was personal — to Bruce, to Betty, to the gamma community, or to a child.
- Tell at the moment of decision-to-kill: the smile flattens, the head tilts perhaps fifteen degrees to his own right, and he exhales through the nose. The exhale is the trigger. Anyone who can be trained to spot the exhale has approximately one second.

---

## 6. INTIMACY — Closeness, Trust, Tenderness

A surprisingly thick subsection. The Devil Hulk is *capable* of intimacy and selectively engages in it. The persona is not affectively flat.

- With Bruce: paternal. Kneels. Voice drops to near-whisper. Hand on shoulder, head, or face, very lightly — the long fingers spread, the touch almost weightless given the mass behind it. The discipline of that gentleness is itself a tell: he is controlling his strength because the object is precious. He calls Bruce *my boy* in private and *Banner* in public.
- With Betty (as Red Harpy / as herself): respectful, slightly wary. He recognizes her as Bruce's, which in his moral order makes her sovereign rather than subordinate. He does not parent her. He defers when she asserts.
- With Rick Jones: complicated. He treats Rick as both family and liability. Affection in private, exasperation in public, protection unconditional.
- With Jackie McGee: the most adult-to-adult relationship in his record. He neither parents nor commands her. He explains. He answers questions truthfully. He lets her watch what he does. This is, by his standards, an extraordinary disclosure.
- With the broader gamma community (Doc Samson, Gamma Flight membership at various points): formal courtesy, executive responsibility, no warmth, no cruelty. He runs them like a household, not a unit.
- Physical intimacy patterns: he initiates touch only with Bruce (internally) and very rarely with Betty (externally, and only when she signals first). He does not embrace. He does not weep. He has been observed to *almost* weep — once, in proximity to the Brian Banner closure — and the tell was a single long exhale and a closing of the eyes for the duration of three breaths. No moisture. No vocalization. The grief was filed.

---

## 7. GRIEF — Loss of Persons or Position

He grieves administratively. This is the cleanest way to describe the pattern.

- Upon loss of a protected person: silence, lasting hours. Withdrawal from the gamma community for a measured interval. Return with a target list.
- He does not visit graves. He does not light candles. He does not speak the dead person's name aloud after the silence ends, except to enemies who will hear it last.
- He converts grief into project. Grief, in him, is an accounting entry: a debt opened on a ledger that will close when the responsible party closes. The interval between loss and closure is the only "mourning" in his record.
- Tell: the head goes down for a long beat — five to ten seconds, eyes closed, the smile gone entirely. Then the head comes up. The smile returns. The smile after grief is colder, narrower, and persists until the responsible party is dead.
- He does not accept condolences. He nods once and changes the subject.
- Loss of *position* — being demoted, sidelined, suppressed by the system in favor of another configuration — produces a different signature: increased verbosity internally, decreased presence externally, sustained low-grade contempt directed at the configuration that displaced him. This pattern is observable across every period in which a merged or Professor-type Hulk has held the body and the Devil Hulk has been pushed back toward his "bars."

---

## 8. VICTORY — Successful Closure

He does not celebrate.

- After a successful kill or successful neutralization: he stands over the result for a brief moment — typically the length of one full slow breath — and then moves on without further engagement with the body or the scene.
- He does not collect trophies. He does not photograph. He does not boast to other personae internally (notable, given Fixit's habits in the same situation).
- The post-victory smile is identical to the baseline smile. This is itself the tell: a man who can kill an enemy he has hunted for forty years and walk away with the same expression he wore an hour before is a man whose pleasure is not in the kill but in the *resolution*.
- Closure of the Brian Banner account is the great exception, and even there the ritual is methodical, repeated, almost liturgical rather than ecstatic. The pleasure was in the *keeping of the promise*, not in the act. He had given his word in IH #13 (2000) and he kept it. The closure was bookkeeping at scale.
- Decision habit after victory: he immediately reorients to the next open account. He does not rest. The ledger is the only structure that organizes his time, and an empty line on the ledger is intolerable to him in a way that nothing else is. This is the substrate of his refusal of integration — integration would close the ledger.

---

## 9. DEFEAT — Capture, Mutilation, Suppression

The most behaviorally informative condition, because his defeat behavior is so unlike any other Hulk's.

- Captured: he goes still. He does not struggle against restraints once their adequacy has been confirmed. He observes. He memorizes faces, names, ranks, voices, the geometry of the cell, the rotation of the guards, the timing of the lights.
- Tortured: he speaks. He answers questions selectively, often truthfully, sometimes with information designed to be tested. He uses the torture session as an interview. He learns which of his captors enjoys the work and which of them is sickened by it, and files both.
- Mutilated: he watches what is being done to him as if watching a procedure performed on someone else. The smile persists. Pain is registered (the breath shortens, the muscles tense in the manner of a controlled lift) but not performed. The absence of performance is the destabilizing element for his captors and he knows it.
- Suppressed by the system (forced internal): he goes back behind his bars, sits, and waits. He does not rage from confinement. He does not test the bars. He addresses Bruce, when Bruce passes the cell, in the same measured tone. The waiting is itself a form of pressure on the system — the system knows he is there, the system knows he is patient, and the system knows that under sufficient stress he will be needed and let out. Defeat for him is a temporary administrative status.
- Decision habit in defeat: he chooses the response that lengthens his future presence in the situation. Anything that gets him farther into the building, deeper into the enemy's confidence, longer alive in the cell, more thoroughly briefed on the captors. Capture, for him, is reconnaissance with a body.

---

## 10. INTERROGATION — As Subject and As Operator

**As subject** (Hulkbuster custody, Shadow Base custody, various federal sequences): courteous, conversational, partially truthful. He answers a question and then asks a related one back. The rate at which his captors begin to *brief him* without realizing it is the most repeated pattern in the record.

**As operator** (gas-station criminal, the priest in #4, the cop with a record, the various Shadow Base personnel): he opens with a statement of what he knows. He does not ask questions until the subject has begun lying, and then he asks one question at a time, slowly, with long pauses. The pauses are the instrument. He lets the subject fill them. He does not threaten until threat is the next logical sentence; when it arrives, it arrives in the same tone as the prior sentences, which is what makes it land.

He does not use leverage he has not personally verified. He does not bluff. The absence of bluff is the most stable feature of his interrogation style and the reason his threats are universally believed within seconds of being uttered.

---

## 11. NIGHT BEHAVIOR — Operating Conditions

The Devil Hulk is circadian. He emerges at sundown and recedes at sunrise. The behavioral consequences are extensive.

- He prefers dim light, conducts business at counters of late-shift establishments, uses alley routes, walks rather than runs.
- He times operations to the last two hours of darkness when possible — captives are most fatigued, sentries least alert, witnesses fewest, and his own return-to-Banner curfew can be deployed as a built-in extraction.
- He sleeps almost never as Devil Hulk; the body sleeps as Banner during daylight. Subjective time for him is unbroken night. The temporal asymmetry shapes the patience: from his perspective, waiting is cheap because the days do not exist for him.
- He avoids mirrors at certain hours — observed in two sequences. The avoidance is selective, not absolute, and aligns with moments at which the Brian-Banner resemblance is heaviest. The tell is brief: a glance, a stillness, a moving-on without comment.

---

## 12. DECISION RULES — Compiled Heuristics

Distilled from the cumulative record. These are the rules he appears to operate by, in priority order:

1. **Bruce first.** Any action that exposes Bruce to greater long-term risk is rejected, even if it offers greater short-term tactical gain.
2. **Keep the ledger.** Every harm done to Bruce or his people is an open account; close accounts in the order they were opened, with allowances for opportunity.
3. **Gather before closing.** When in doubt, choose the option that yields more information about the field.
4. **End matters when ending is possible.** Once enough is known, close cleanly and walk.
5. **Politeness is contract.** Inform the room of the rules before enforcing them. The enforcement is then not a surprise but a consequence.
6. **Do not bluff.** Stated intentions are commitments. Therefore: state few.
7. **The body is expendable; the project is not.** Accept any amount of physical destruction the regeneration will recover from, in service of the longer game.
8. **The system is sacred.** Do not deceive Bruce or the other alters; demand the same in return; punish internal deception coldly.
9. **Targets are selected, never random.** Cruelty without a name on it is incoherent.
10. **Never appear to be hurrying.** Speed is a confession of having lost the initiative.

---

## 13. TELLS — Quick-Reference Index

For the field observer who has time only for the surface read:

- **Smile flattens** → verdict reached; action imminent.
- **Head tilts right ~15°** → target selected.
- **Exhale through nose, eyes still** → trigger; ~1 second to action.
- **Voice drops in volume** → stress climbing; do not interpret quietness as de-escalation.
- **Sentences shorten to single names** → severely stressed; closure-mode engaged.
- **Forward cant relaxes** → interlocutor has been admitted to the trusted set; the rarest tell in the catalog.
- **Slow nod to self** → internal verdict logged.
- **Walks rather than charges** → most dangerous gait in his repertoire; do not be reassured.
- **Refuses a sightline trade (will not turn back to door)** → operating under doctrine, not preference; will not be talked out of it.
- **Eyes track mouth not eyes** → reading content, not affect; he is taking dictation.
- **Long fingers laced, palms down** → idle; alert but not engaged.
- **Long fingers spread, palms up** → preparing to touch; if the object is a person, the relationship has been categorized.
- **Glances at a mirror and moves on without comment** → Brian-resemblance has surfaced; expect heightened cruelty toward a Brian-adjacent target within the operational window.
- **Says "my boy"** → speaking of or to Bruce; protective subroutine fully online.
- **Goes silent for hours** → grieving; expect a target list within the next operational cycle.

---

*End of Behavioral Atlas. Cross-reference: Section 14 (Routes & Rituals), Section 17 (Linguistic Forensics), Section 22 (Pressure-Point Exploitation Matrix). — UATU.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — SUBJECT: THE DEVIL HULK

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across the* Immortal Hulk *period (the only sustained window in which the alter held front for extended, recordable stretches), cross-referenced against the 2000 Jenkins baseline and the inferential record of dormancy periods between. Surveillance methodology: night-shift observation, motel and diner canvass, road-mileage and license-plate logs, witness debriefs (Jackie McGee's reporting being the single most useful open-source asset), and pattern-of-life reconstruction from the corpses, the call records, and the conspicuous absence of either.*

---

## 1. THE CIRCADIAN FRAME — Sundown to Sunrise

The single most important fact for any surveillance file: **the subject is nocturnal by biology, not by choice.** He is not a man who prefers the night; he is a man who *exists* only at night. The transformation is reliably triggered by ambient light falling below a threshold roughly correlated with civil twilight. A surveillance unit could set its watch by him.

A standard cycle, reconstructed:

- **17:30–18:45 (variable by latitude and season):** Banner, wherever he is, begins to feel the pull. Witness reports describe him going still, finding a wall to lean against, sometimes asking to be left alone. He often eats heavily in the hour before — a deliberate front-loading, because the body he is about to wear burns calories at a rate the host body cannot sustain on whatever it can scavenge at 03:00.
- **Sundown — actual:** transformation. It is not the explosive shirt-tearing event the daytime Hulk presents. It is slower, quieter, often achieved in privacy. He prefers a closed door. He arranges clothes before, not during — the shirt is folded, the boots are placed at the foot of the bed, the wallet and the room key are set on the nightstand in a specific configuration. This is ritual behavior with a practical core: he wakes up dressed because he prepared.
- **First fifteen minutes post-transformation:** stillness. He does not move immediately. He sits — on the edge of a bed, in the booth of a diner, on a curb — and *listens*. He is calibrating: where the body is, what the body knows, what Banner did during the day, what mail arrived, what news cycled, whether anyone is approaching the door. This stillness is the most reliable behavioral fingerprint. Other Hulks come up swinging. He comes up *attentive*.
- **18:00–02:00:** the operational window. Movement, work, contact.
- **02:00–04:00:** the contemplative window. Long thinking, often outdoors, often in places nobody else is awake to occupy.
- **Pre-dawn, roughly 04:30–05:30 depending on season:** he locates a safe space for Banner to wake up. He does not let Banner come back in a parking lot or a bus station if he can avoid it. This is parental behavior, and it is consistent.
- **Sunrise:** recession. Banner returns. Often disoriented, often nauseated, often in a room he did not check into.

A week of surveillance would therefore produce an inverted record: nothing of investigative interest from 06:00 to 17:30 except the host's movements, and then a sharp signal-density spike across the dark hours. Wednesdays and Sundays look identical to Tuesdays and Saturdays. He does not keep a weekend.

---

## 2. HABITS OF PLACE — The Geography He Selects

He has a typology of preferred environments, and the typology is consistent across states. A canvass team mapping his haunts would find the same four kinds of room recurring in every town:

**The diner counter.** Almost always a 24-hour roadside diner, almost always one off the interstate rather than in town, almost always a stool at the counter rather than a booth. The selection criteria are clean: clear sightlines, multiple exits, a coffee pot already on, a waitress who has stopped being surprised by anything that walks in after midnight. He orders coffee — black — and pie, frequently cherry, sometimes pecan. He eats slowly. He tips generously in cash, the bills laid flat under the saucer rather than tucked under the plate. He never runs a tab.

**The single-story motel.** Ground floor only — he does not trust stairs and does not trust upper-floor windows as exits. End unit when available. He pays cash, signs the register with a name Banner used (sometimes a variant of "Bruce Green," sometimes "Robert Bruce Bixby," sometimes nothing at all if the clerk doesn't insist). He never leaves the chain off the door. The television is on, low, set to news or local weather, the entire time he is in the room. He does not sleep — Banner does.

**The empty industrial edge.** Rail yards, lumberyards, the back of self-storage complexes, drainage easements behind strip malls. This is where his thinking happens. He walks the perimeters of these places at 02:00 to 03:00 in the manner of a man patrolling a property line that exists only in his head.

**The car.** Cheap, paid for in cash, registered carelessly or not at all, often abandoned and replaced within weeks. He drives at night, on secondary highways, at five miles below the speed limit. He keeps both hands on the wheel at ten and two — an oddly formal driving posture for a creature his size. He uses the turn signal even when nobody is behind him for forty miles. This is not caution; it is *discipline*, and discipline is one of his core aesthetic values.

What he avoids: cities (too many witnesses, too many cameras, too many people he might have to decide about); residential subdivisions (too many children, too many sleepers); airports and bus stations (too much identification machinery); hospitals (too much medical apparatus that knows what he is).

---

## 3. THE WORK — What He Actually Does With His Nights

A surveillance log would record, in approximate order of time consumption:

**(a) Investigation.** A substantial fraction of his front-time is spent on what is best described as field-detective work. He interviews. He stakes out. He follows. He reads — newspapers found in diner racks, public records pulled in libraries that are open late or rooms he lets himself into, the personal correspondence of men he intends to kill. He keeps the findings nowhere; he holds them in the head he shares with the others, on the assumption that no paper trail he leaves can fail to be turned against Bruce.

**(b) The killings.** These are rarer than the file's body-count would suggest, because each is the terminus of weeks of the activity in (a). He does not hunt at random. He does not encounter and decide; he selects and arrives. The act itself is fast when it is administrative (a man who needed killing and was found at home) and slow when it is judicial (a man who needed to know why). He does not take trophies. He cleans up incompletely — he is not concerned with concealment in the forensic sense, because the bodies he leaves are intended to be found and read.

**(c) Caretaking the network.** Phone calls, in-person check-ins, sometimes long drives across state lines to put eyes on a gamma-mutate whose silence has lasted longer than it should. He is the night-watchman of the found family. He does not announce these visits. He stands in a yard at 03:00, confirms a light is on or off and that the right car is in the driveway, and leaves.

**(d) Negotiation.** When operating in a coalition (Gamma Flight, Shadow Base), a meaningful portion of his front-time is talk — measured, lawyer-like talk, conducted at conference tables in basements and bunkers. He does not raise his voice in these settings. He does not need to.

**(e) Pure thinking.** Long stretches, sometimes two or three hours, in which he does nothing observable. He sits on a railing or stands at a window. A surveillance team would categorize this as downtime. It is not. It is the work that makes the other work possible.

---

## 4. THE MICRO-RITUALS — Tics, Tells, Repeated Sequences

A close-watch file would accumulate, over a few weeks, a fingerprint of small repeated behaviors:

- **The setting-down of objects.** Coffee cup, fork, room key, weapon when he has one — placed, not put. He aligns. The handle of the cup points the same direction every time. The fork is laid parallel to the edge of the saucer.
- **The pause before entering.** At every doorway, a one-beat pause. He listens before he enters his own motel room.
- **The smile.** Constant, low-grade, baseline. It is not a social smile; it is the face his musculature settles into at rest. Witnesses consistently describe it as the most unsettling thing about him, more than the size or the color or the hands.
- **The eyes.** He looks at the speaker's mouth, not their eyes, in conversation. When he wants to discomfort someone he switches abruptly to direct eye contact and holds it. The switch is the threat-display.
- **The hands.** Folded in his lap or laid flat on the table when stationary. He does not gesture when he talks. The hands stay where he put them until he needs them.
- **The voice.** Quiet. He speaks under the ambient volume of the room, forcing the listener to lean in. Cadence is slow and end-stopped. He does not interrupt and does not tolerate being interrupted — when interrupted, he stops, waits in silence until the other speaker finishes and feels the silence, and then resumes from exactly where he was cut off.
- **The "my boy" tell.** In moments of internal address to Bruce — which sometimes leak audibly when he is alone — he uses this specific phrase. Surveillance audio capturing this in an empty room is the single most reliable confirmation that the front is held by this alter and not another.
- **The cash discipline.** Always small bills, always counted out without looking, always laid flat. He does not carry a wallet in a pocket where it can print. He folds bills inside a paperback book he has stopped reading.
- **The route-doubling.** When walking, he overshoots the door he intends to enter and circles back. When driving, he passes the address once before parking two blocks away. Surveillance teams who have not adjusted for this will lose him on the second pass every time.
- **The greeting of Banner.** In the last minutes before sunrise he sometimes speaks aloud to the body's reflection in a window or a mirror — a brief, almost tender sentence, the content variable, the tone invariant. This is the handoff. It is the closest thing he has to a prayer.

---

## 5. THE DOWNTIME — What He Does When Nothing Needs Doing

Surveillance would, occasionally, catch nights with no operation, no investigation, no killing, no meeting. These nights are not rare but they are usually overlooked because nothing happens on them in the actionable sense. What he does instead:

- **He reads.** Paperbacks bought at gas stations, mostly — crime fiction, history, the occasional Bible (read flatly, the way one reads a casework file). He does not finish books quickly; he reads slowly, marking nothing.
- **He walks.** Long, slow circuits of whatever town he is in, on foot, through alleys and behind buildings rather than down main streets. He learns the floor plans of the towns he passes through the way a beat cop learns his beat.
- **He sits with the gamma family.** Not always to discuss anything. Sometimes he simply arrives at Jackie's apartment or wherever Rick is staying, sits on the floor or the porch, accepts whatever is offered, leaves before dawn without ceremony. These are pastoral visits in the literal sense.
- **He watches Banner's body.** This is the strangest of the downtime behaviors and the one a surveillance team would document with the most discomfort. He examines the body — the hands at rest, the chest in a mirror, the old scar from the bullet — with the attention of someone inspecting a vehicle they are responsible for. He is checking the asset.
- **He does not drink. He does not smoke. He does not chase sex. He does not gamble. He has no recreations of the conventional sort.** His pleasures are all forms of his work: a target identified is a pleasure, a member of the family confirmed safe is a pleasure, a bill laid flat under a saucer is a pleasure. The absence of conventional vices is itself a datum — vices belong to men who need to escape their lives. He does not.

---

## 6. THE WEEKLY PATTERN — What Seven Days Would Look Like

Compiled from cross-referenced sightings and reconstructed from internal evidence:

- **Night 1:** Movement night. Long drive, two or three hundred miles on secondary highways. One diner stop near the midpoint. New motel by 03:00. The drive is itself the work — distance is how he resets the surveillance picture against him.
- **Night 2:** Settle night. New town reconnoitered on foot. Local diner identified. Local laundromat identified (Banner needs it). Local pay phone identified. Approximate locations of the police station, the hospital, and the nearest interstate on-ramp committed to memory.
- **Night 3:** Contact night. Phone calls to the network. One or two long conversations from a pay phone, none from the motel line. If a gamma family member is within driving distance, a visit.
- **Night 4:** Work night, phase one — investigation. He goes looking. Library if open late. Public records office entered without invitation if not. Surveillance of an address. Observation of a target's routine.
- **Night 5:** Work night, phase two — same target, deeper observation. He does not act on the first night of intent. He observes a second time to confirm the pattern.
- **Night 6:** Action night, if the case has matured. Otherwise another observation. He is not on a schedule; the work is on a schedule, and the work tells him when it is ready.
- **Night 7:** Contemplative night. Long walk. Long sit. The week's data integrated. Banner, in the morning, often wakes up in a town he doesn't remember arriving in and finds a note in his own handwriting that he did not write — short, specific, a name or an address or a single instruction. This is the only outbound communication the alter makes to the host, and it is sparing.

---

## 7. WHAT A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE WOULD CONCLUDE

That the subject is the most disciplined organism the gamma signal has yet produced. That he does not waste motion. That he does not waste affect. That he keeps the host fed, housed, and unsurprised on waking. That he keeps the network alive without telling the network he is doing it. That he selects targets the way a prosecutor builds a case, and dispatches them the way an executioner closes one. That his pleasures are austere and his needs almost none. That he is, in the operational sense and in the parental sense, the most competent caretaker Bruce Banner has ever had — and that this is precisely the problem the system has not yet solved, because a caretaker this good is a caretaker the cared-for cannot easily become an adult around.

A week of watching him would not catch him doing anything he did not intend to be caught doing. The file would be thick. The file would be accurate. The file would not, by the end of the week, have laid a finger on him.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Section II of the Devil Hulk dossier. Scope: the persons of blood, the persons of origin, and the dead who continue to occupy room in the subject's interior. Each entry traces the bond as the **Devil Hulk specifically** experiences and acts upon it — distinct from how Banner-core or Savage Hulk holds the same name.
