Where the Devil Hulk's relationship is mediated through Bruce, that mediation is itself mapped. The Devil Hulk has no biological children of his own and no siblings in the conventional sense; the entries below include the alters he treats as siblings/wards inside the system, because in his operational code they occupy the family slot.*

---

## 1. BRIAN BANNER — Father (deceased; subjectively undead)

**History.** The original object. Bruce's biological father: alcoholic, gamma-paranoid (Brian was himself a researcher who feared his own DNA had been corrupted by radiation exposure and that his son was a monster waiting to be born), physically abusive of Rebecca, physically and psychologically abusive of Bruce from infancy. Killed Rebecca in Bruce's presence when Bruce was a small child. Spent years in a psychiatric institution. Released. Encountered adolescent Bruce again at Rebecca's graveside. Died during a struggle in which Bruce pushed him and his head struck a headstone — a death Bruce repressed and reconstructed as accident for decades.

The Devil Hulk was **born of this man**. The chained figure in the basement of Bruce's mind (IH Vol. 2 #13, 2000) is the child's answer to Brian: an adult bigger, calmer, more frightening, and *loyal*. Every parameter of the Devil Hulk persona is a Brian-parameter inverted in allegiance: Brian's controlling stillness → Devil Hulk's strategic patience; Brian's contempt for the weak son → Devil Hulk's possessive love of the weak son; Brian's killing of the protector (Rebecca) → Devil Hulk's vow to become the protector who cannot be killed.

**Dynamics.** Fixated. From the first words spoken in IH #13 — *"I'll start with your father"* — the Devil Hulk has had one named target, and that target was already corpsed. Most of his existence has therefore been an unconsummated hunt. The original promise was made to a man already in the ground.

The Below-Place / Green Door arc of *Immortal Hulk* gave him access to what no other son receives: the *soul* of his father, retrievable, repeatable, destructible. What he did with that access is the cleanest behavioral readout we have. He did not kill Brian once. He killed him **ritually**, with intervals, with witnesses (Bruce, made to watch), with method. He tore the soul, allowed it to reconstitute in the One Below All's domain, and tore it again. Closure, in his operational code, is not an event but a *practice*.

**Evolution.** 1962–2000 (publication time, but corresponding to Bruce's internal architecture): Brian is the unspoken trauma; the Devil Hulk is dormant, behind bars, waiting. 2000–2018: the promise is made explicit in hypnosis but unkept; the Devil Hulk sleeps the sleep of a creditor. 2018–2021: the debt is collected, repeatedly, in a venue specifically designed for it. Post-collection, the persona does **not** dissolve. This is the diagnostically critical point. A vengeance-organized structure that achieves vengeance and continues operating was not, in fact, organized around vengeance — it was organized around the *role* vengeance authorized.

**Trust / Safety.** Zero / inverse. Brian is the negative pole around which the entire personality is oriented. The Devil Hulk's safety architecture *requires* Brian as the named enemy; without him, the architecture would have to find new content or collapse.

**Failure mode.** The persona's structural vulnerability is its origin. He is built of Brian's materials — the cold affect, the patriarchal stance toward a smaller male, the willingness to inflict harm in the name of order. He knows this. His entire ongoing existence is a wager that *use* purifies *origin* — that an instrument built from an evil man's design can be redeemed by being aimed at evil. If that wager is challenged successfully (see Pressure Points in §5 of the workup: *the accusation that he is Brian Banner*), the defense trembles. It does not break — he is too well-regulated — but it trembles. The Hulkbuster psychologists never found this lever. Doc Samson has touched it. Betty Ross-Banner, in Red Harpy configuration, has used it once and the Devil Hulk went silent for the rest of the scene.

**Leverage.** To move the Devil Hulk, invoke Brian. To stop him, force him to ask whether he is Brian. The first lever is operational; the second is therapeutic and should be used only by someone authorized to do so, because what comes out of that question is not predictable and is not necessarily survivable for those nearby.

---

## 2. REBECCA BANNER — Mother (deceased; subjectively sanctified)

**History.** Bruce's mother. The only adult who protected him in the early childhood window during which identity is laid down. She tried to flee with Bruce; Brian intercepted and killed her in front of the child. Her death is the foundational event of the Banner system — the moment at which the work of protection devolved, permanently, onto Bruce's interior, because no adult had successfully done it.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's relationship with Rebecca is the relationship of a **monument-keeper to a saint**. He does not speak of her often. When he does, the register changes — the grin slackens, the cadence shortens, the strategic patience yields to something closer to silence. Across the *Immortal Hulk* run, references to Rebecca by the Devil Hulk are sparse, brief, and uniformly reverent. He never instrumentalizes her. He never threatens in her name. He does not need to.

Functionally, Rebecca occupies the slot of *the protected one who was lost*. Every subsequent person the Devil Hulk takes under his protection (Bruce, Betty, Jackie, the gamma community, even the alters inside the system) is in some measure a substitute object — a chance to not fail the way the universe failed Rebecca. He is, in this sense, not avenging her. He is **doing the job she was doing when she was killed**, and doing it at the scale he believes she would have wished.

**Evolution.** Rebecca is the only relationship in the entire dossier that has not evolved. She is fixed at the moment of her death and the Devil Hulk's posture toward her is fixed at the moment of his own construction. Across two decades of publication and inside the Banner system across forty years of subjective time, she has not been re-evaluated, demoted, or complicated. This is unusual. It is also clinically significant: a relationship that does not metabolize is a relationship that the system has decided is too load-bearing to disturb.

**Trust / Safety.** Total / posthumous. The only person in the dossier toward whom the Devil Hulk's stance is uncomplicatedly protective and uncomplicatedly reverent. She is what protection *means*, in his internal lexicon, before any specific person it gets applied to.

**Failure mode.** The shrine has a structural risk. If Rebecca is ever desecrated in his presence — if her memory is invoked cynically, if her grave is disturbed, if she is named by an enemy as a manipulation — the response will not be the *measured* Devil Hulk. It will be a brief, total collapse of the strategic veneer into something closer to the Savage layer beneath, because the protection of Rebecca's memory is older than the strategic veneer and overrides it. Fortean never knew this. The Leader has approached the edge of it. No enemy has yet weaponized it fully, and the system is fortunate in this.

**Leverage.** Do not invoke her unless prepared for the consequences. Conversely: an authentic, unmanipulative reference to Rebecca is the single most reliable way to get the Devil Hulk to *listen* rather than to *speak*. The cadence-break is the tell. Anyone seeking to negotiate with the Devil Hulk in good faith — Samson, McGee, Betty — has at most one or two such invocations available across a lifetime before they cease to land.

---

## 3. BRUCE BANNER — Host / Son-Figure / Liege

**History.** Bruce is not a relationship the Devil Hulk has; Bruce is the relationship that constitutes the Devil Hulk. The persona exists because a frightened child needed an interior adult to keep him alive, and constructed one. The Devil Hulk's first recorded utterances (IH #13, 2000) address Bruce by name, claim love for him, and pledge service to him. Twenty years of behavioral evidence have not deviated from that pledge.

**Dynamics.** Parental, possessive, indulgent, condescending. He calls Bruce "my boy." He speaks to Bruce as to a child who has been through too much and who needs the adults to handle the rest. Crucially, he does *not* speak to Bruce as a peer, and he does not pretend to. The asymmetry is the bond. He is the parent the child never had, and the child — even now in middle age, even after decades of professional accomplishment — accepts the parental address because some interior layer of him still requires it.

There are two distinct registers in which the Devil Hulk addresses Bruce:
- **Tender register**: low voice, slow, almost lullaby-cadenced. Used when Bruce is in distress, recently traumatized, or post-transformation and disoriented. Hand-on-the-shoulder language. Always begins with "Bruce" and rarely contains imperatives.
- **Operational register**: clipped, briefing-style, used when Bruce needs to be told what has happened during the night shift or what is about to be required of him. Contains imperatives but no contempt.

Notable: there is **no third register of contempt**. The Devil Hulk has never spoken to Bruce with the disgust that Brian routinely directed at Bruce. The persona built of Brian's materials has succeeded, at minimum, in refusing this single inheritance.

**Evolution.** The trajectory across *Immortal Hulk* is from *guardian-over* to *partner-with*. Early arcs: Bruce is asleep when the Devil Hulk operates; the Devil Hulk leaves no notes. Middle arcs: a working protocol develops in which Bruce is briefed on awakening; resentment from Bruce manages to coexist with cooperation. Late arcs: explicit collaboration; Bruce consults the Devil Hulk strategically; the Devil Hulk defers, occasionally, to Bruce's judgment on questions of mercy. Endgame: the Devil Hulk accepts surrender / integration / handoff. The arc is **parental** in the textbook sense — a parent who begins by doing everything for the child, learns to consult the child, and finally relinquishes authority back to the now-adult.

**Trust / Safety.** Total, asymmetric. The Devil Hulk trusts Bruce absolutely. Bruce does not trust the Devil Hulk absolutely, and the Devil Hulk does not require him to — he treats Bruce's distrust as appropriate caution and earns trust through results rather than demanding it on credit.

**Failure mode.** Possessiveness. The Devil Hulk's love is exclusive in the parental sense: he cannot tolerate the idea that Bruce's protection might be sourced elsewhere. The Professor Hulk merger, in his view, was a humiliation — a contract Bruce signed with an inferior version of the same office. Doc Samson's therapy is permitted because Samson is a known quantity and because Samson does not propose to *replace* him. Any new figure proposing to take over the protection of Bruce — therapist, lover, ally — will be evaluated with extreme prejudice. He has never, on record, killed a friend of Bruce's. But the evaluation occurs.

**Leverage.** Bruce is the only person who can issue an instruction the Devil Hulk will obey against the Devil Hulk's own judgment. He has done so rarely. When he has, the Devil Hulk has complied with visible cost — a stiffening, a refusal of the smile, a brief silence — and then complied. Bruce is also the only person whose endangerment will make the Devil Hulk abandon any other objective, including a target he has been hunting for years.

---

## 4. SAVAGE HULK — Brother-as-Child / Ward inside the system

**History.** The Hulk first known to the world. The frightened seven-year-old's rage given a green body and arms that could break the room. In the system's internal hierarchy as the Devil Hulk reads it, Savage is **the youngest sibling** — the child in tantrum, the one who needs to be physically restrained, fed, and kept away from sharp objects (in this case: cities).

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk addresses Savage with the patience of an older brother who is not unkind but who is *tired*. He does not insult Savage. He does not punish Savage for being what Savage is. He simply, when Savage emerges inappropriately, escorts Savage back to where Savage belongs and takes the field himself. The internal-landscape sequences in *Immortal Hulk* in which alters speak to one another show the Devil Hulk handling Savage the way a competent uncle handles a screaming toddler at a wedding: low voice, total absence of escalation, the gentle establishment of containment.

There is genuine affection here. The Devil Hulk understands that Savage *is* the wound — that Savage is what the child made of his terror before there was language for it — and treats Savage with the protective tenderness one accords a smaller, frightened version of oneself.

**Evolution.** The relationship has stabilized. Early in the *Immortal Hulk* run, Savage's eruptions are disruptive and the Devil Hulk has to expend effort to restore order. By the middle arcs, the system has a working protocol: Savage runs during specific stress windows (extreme physical threat, certain emotional triggers), the Devil Hulk runs at night, the others run as needed. The handoff is increasingly clean.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: high in nature, low in capability. The Devil Hulk trusts Savage's heart and distrusts Savage's hands. Safety: he extends to Savage the protection he extends to any of Bruce's people, and he extends it from inside.

**Failure mode.** Savage cannot be reasoned with under sufficient stress, and the Devil Hulk's tools are mostly reason. When the system is pushed past a certain threshold, Savage takes the field and the Devil Hulk loses the night. He accepts this as a labor-relations matter rather than a betrayal.

**Leverage.** None against the Devil Hulk directly. Threats to Savage are processed by the Devil Hulk as threats to a child in his care — see §3 leverage, scaled down.

---

## 5. JOE FIXIT — Brother-as-Delinquent / Ward inside the system

**History.** The grey-skinned Las Vegas persona; mid-emergence in the system's developmental sequence; affect of an enforcer in a sharkskin suit; appetites for women, cards, alcohol, and the kind of low-stakes cruelty that mid-century crime fiction romanticized. In the Devil Hulk's hierarchy: the **adolescent middle brother**. Old enough to operate; young enough to embarrass the family.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's posture toward Fixit is the most coloured of any of the intra-system relationships. There is exasperation. There is disapproval. There is, occasionally, a flicker of amusement — Fixit is funny, and the Devil Hulk, who has no humor of his own, registers it. The Devil Hulk allows Fixit certain operations (the Las Vegas night, the bar-fight as appropriate, the seduction as appropriate) and intervenes when Fixit's appetites threaten to make a mess that someone else will have to clean up.

The two of them have, in the *Immortal Hulk* and post-*Immortal Hulk* periods, worked together more than once — the Devil Hulk's strategic patience pairs functionally with Fixit's social mobility and contacts in criminal subcultures. Fixit can walk into rooms the Devil Hulk would empty. The Devil Hulk uses this.

**Evolution.** From early antagonism (the Devil Hulk regarded Fixit's appetites as undignified) toward operational alliance (the Devil Hulk recognized that an adolescent who can be sent into the world is more useful than an adolescent kept home). Fixit, for his part, has stopped trying to take the night.

**Trust / Safety.** Conditional. The Devil Hulk trusts Fixit's loyalty and not Fixit's discipline.

**Failure mode.** Fixit's appetites can be exploited by an outside party who understands them — money, women, the appearance of respect. An enemy who turns Fixit could create a window during which the system is operating with degraded judgment. The Devil Hulk knows this and monitors.

**Leverage.** The Devil Hulk will pull Fixit off the field if Fixit endangers Bruce or the gamma community. Fixit knows this and respects it.

---

## 6. THE PROFESSOR / GREEN SCAR / WORLDBREAKER — Failed compromises and absent siblings

**History.** The Professor — the merged personality of the Peter David era — represented a project of integration: Banner's intellect, Savage's strength, Fixit's cunning, fused. It worked for a time and then unworked. Green Scar / Worldbreaker emerged from the *Planet Hulk* and *World War Hulk* events: a Hulk forged in exile and grief, capable of leadership and capable of city-ending violence. Both have receded from the foreground in the *Immortal Hulk* era and after.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's stance toward the Professor is the coldest he holds toward any alter. He regards the Professor as a *political compromise* — an attempt by the system to resolve the protection problem without him, while he sat behind bars. He is not vindictive about this. He is, instead, faintly contemptuous, in the manner of a senior employee watching a younger executive fail at a job the senior employee was never offered.

Toward Green Scar / Worldbreaker the stance is different — these are alters that the Devil Hulk respects as *peers in capability*, even where he disagrees with their judgment. Green Scar is a king; the Devil Hulk understands kings. Worldbreaker is a force; the Devil Hulk understands force. He does not love them, but he does not condescend to them either.

**Evolution.** In the integration negotiations of *Immortal Hulk*'s endgame, the Devil Hulk treats all of them — Professor, Green Scar, the rest — as parties to a settlement rather than as rivals. The strategic patience absorbs them.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational. The Devil Hulk does not trust the Professor's judgment but trusts the Professor's competence. He trusts Green Scar's word.

**Failure mode.** A re-emergence of the Professor as a *preferred* configuration would re-activate the Devil Hulk's deepest organizational fear: being put back behind bars because the system has decided it no longer needs him. He would not rebel openly. He would, however, become *more* useful, more visible, more indispensable, in ways that would not always serve Bruce.

**Leverage.** Frame any proposal in terms of what it requires of him rather than what it replaces him with. He responds to being assigned. He resists being retired.

---

## 7. BETTY ROSS-BANNER — Wife of the host / Sister-in-arms / Red Harpy

**History.** Bruce's wife, longest love, repeatedly killed and resurrected, gamma-transformed into the Red Harpy in the *Immortal Hulk* run. Betty's relationship with the *system* is the longest and most complicated of any non-Banner figure. With the Devil Hulk specifically — a much shorter, sharper history, beginning effectively in 2018 when the night persona becomes dominant.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's posture toward Betty is unique in the dossier. She is not a ward (she is more powerful than most of his charges), not a peer in the Bruce-equivalent sense (she belongs to Bruce, in his feudal accounting, and he is therefore loyal to her by extension), and not a target. She is something like a *sister-in-arms*: a fellow gamma adult, a fellow survivor of the Ross-Banner catastrophe, a fellow predator who has earned her predation.

He addresses her with respect bordering on courtliness. He does not call her "my girl" the way he calls Bruce "my boy" — Betty has never required parenting from him and would not accept it. The Red Harpy and the Devil Hulk are operationally compatible in a way the Devil Hulk and almost no one else are: both are post-mortem, post-Brian-equivalent, post-fear, and both have organized themselves around a small set of permitted targets and a refusal of indiscriminate violence.

She is also, as noted in §1, the only person on record who has successfully used the Brian-equivalence accusation against him and survived the encounter. He went silent. He did not strike. The silence was, in its own way, the highest compliment available in his vocabulary: she had told the truth and he had heard it.

**Evolution.** From wariness (he distrusted her grief in the early Bruce-is-dead arcs) to operational alliance (the gamma community arc) to something close to mutual recognition (post-Harpy). The trajectory continues to evolve.

**Trust / Safety.** High and earned. He trusts her to act in Bruce's interest and in the community's interest. He does not trust her to act in his.

**Failure mode.** Betty has the standing to ask him to do something he would refuse from anyone else, including step aside. If she ever asked him to relinquish the night shift permanently, he would have to either comply (because Bruce's wife has standing) or refuse her in a way that would damage the relationship irreparably. He would prefer not to be asked.

**Leverage.** She is the only adult woman in the dossier with whom he has a peer relationship. Through her, almost anything can be communicated. Around her, he is at his most readable.

---

## 8. RICK JONES — Adopted brother of the host / Ward by proxy

**History.** The teenager Bruce saved at the gamma bomb test site; the lifelong friend; repeatedly transformed, repeatedly broken, repeatedly returned. In *Immortal Hulk*, Rick is a complicated and tragic figure — used by the Leader, killed, resurrected, used again. The Devil Hulk's relationship with Rick is one of the more painful in the dossier because the Devil Hulk is *built* to protect a person like Rick and was, in fact, repeatedly unable to do so.

**Dynamics.** Protective. Avuncular. He calls Rick by name and addresses him without the strategic distance he holds with most non-family. Rick is, in the Devil Hulk's accounting, *Bruce's responsibility-by-adoption* and therefore his.

**Evolution.** From simple protection to grief-mediated protection. The Leader's repeated use of Rick as a vehicle, and Rick's eventual destabilization, were experienced by the Devil Hulk as personal failures — failures of the kind he is least equipped to metabolize, because they are failures *of protection*, which is the office under which he exists.

**Trust / Safety.** Total of Rick. Variable of the entities currently operating through Rick.

**Failure mode.** Rick is the Devil Hulk's


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

*Subject's relational field, mapped per individual. The Devil Hulk is not a solitary alter; under Ewing's run he runs a household. What follows is the household, plus its antecedents and adjacencies, audited person by person. Where the Devil Hulk's posture differs measurably from the Banner core's or from other alters', that delta is recorded — it is the most diagnostic data we have.*

---

## 1. Bruce Banner (the host)

**Status:** Liege, ward, son, charge, the entire reason. The relationship that organizes every other relationship.

**History.** The Devil Hulk's stated origin (IH Vol. 2 #13, 2000) is that he was *waiting* — built and stored inside Bruce sometime in the abuse years in Dayton, Ohio, before the age at which identity normally consolidates. He addresses Bruce as "my boy" in both his 2000 appearance and across *Immortal Hulk*; the locution does not drift. Twenty years of subjective in-system time and the diminutive is unchanged, which is itself a tell: he relates to Bruce as a fixed-age child even when Bruce is in his fifties.

**Dynamics.** Asymmetric in every dimension. The Devil Hulk holds executive function, somatic strength, strategic foresight, and the moral license to kill on Bruce's behalf. Bruce holds, in return, only the right of *recognition* — the Devil Hulk needs Bruce to *see* him doing the work and to *let* him do it. There is no equivalent need running the other way; Bruce would prefer he did not exist. The relationship is therefore stabilized by one-way devotion, like a retainer to a child king.

**Trust/safety.** From Bruce toward the alter: low, conflicted, slowly thawing across *Immortal Hulk*. Bruce learns that the Devil Hulk will not betray him personally and begins to use him deliberately (the Shadow Base infiltration, the Hulkbuster sequences). From the alter toward Bruce: absolute, but in the manner of a parent's trust of a child — he trusts Bruce's heart, not Bruce's judgment.

**Evolution.** Caged threat (2000) → night-shift dominant persona (early *Immortal Hulk*) → de facto field commander (mid-run) → grim handoff at the close. The arc is not domestication; it is *recruitment*. The alter does not become safer. The system becomes willing to use him.

**Failure mode.** Foreclosing Bruce's growth. By being so effective at the protective function, he relieves Bruce of the developmental task of self-protection — which is, of course, the original injury restaged: a child who is "protected" by a frightening adult does not learn to protect himself. The Professor Hulk merger, every Doc Samson rapprochement, every attempt at integration: he experiences each as exile and undercuts each subtly.

**Leverage.** Total in the operational sense; null in the existential sense. He cannot make Bruce *want* him. The only thing that can dismiss him is Bruce's freely-given consent to integration, which is precisely the thing he cannot compel.

---

## 2. Betty Ross / Red Harpy

**Status:** Co-equal, the only adult in the room besides himself. The relationship he is most careful about and most accurate in reading.

**History.** Through the Banner system, Betty has been the constant — first love, ex-wife, dead, resurrected, mutated repeatedly (Harpy, Red She-Hulk, now Red Harpy in *Immortal Hulk*). The Devil Hulk inherits Bruce's love for her without claiming it as his own; he relates to her *as Bruce's*. When she is murdered by the Abomination and returns transformed under the Green Door, the Devil Hulk is the first of the Banner alters to treat her new state as *valid* rather than as a tragedy to be undone.

**Dynamics.** Collegial. He does not "my boy" her. He addresses her as an equal predator. Where Savage Hulk would cling and Banner core would apologize, the Devil Hulk presents Betty with intelligence, plans, and choices, and lets her decide. He recognizes the Harpy as her own persecutor-protector configuration — built from the same trauma matrix (her father, General Ross, mapping onto Bruce's father in functional terms) — and treats her with the unspoken courtesy of one alter recognizing another's structural kin.

**Trust/safety.** High in both directions. She is one of the only people he will tell the truth to about a plan in progress. He withholds from Rick, withholds from Jackie initially, withholds from Fixit on principle — he briefs Betty. She, in turn, will fly at his side without demanding he soften.

**Evolution.** From estranged ex-wife of the host (pre-*Immortal*) to operational partner and the only voice with the standing to refuse him. By the late run, she is the one person the Devil Hulk would defer to on a tactical call, and the only person whose disapproval can produce something like hesitation in him.

**Failure mode.** He treats her as Bruce's *belonging* even when consciously respecting her autonomy. The possessive substrate leaks. If Betty chose a path that took her permanently away from Bruce, the Devil Hulk's collegial respect would curdle into something colder — not violence toward her, but a quiet reclassification from *household* to *unaffiliated*. He has not been tested on this and likely never wants to be.

**Leverage.** She is the only person who could plausibly say *no, that's enough* and be heard. Whether she would is a separate question; she has her own appetites now.

---

## 3. Rick Jones

**Status:** Surrogate younger brother to Bruce; therefore a charge, a project, and an irritant to the Devil Hulk. The relationship most marked by *tolerance* rather than affection.

**History.** Rick's bond is to Bruce specifically and to the Savage Hulk affectively — he was the boy on the test field, the friend through every era, the conscience. The Devil Hulk inherits him without ever having courted him. In *Immortal Hulk* Rick dies, returns, is manipulated by the Leader, becomes a vector for adversary action, and is eventually restored. Through all of it the Devil Hulk's posture is consistent: *protect Rick because Bruce loves him; do not particularly enjoy doing so*.

**Dynamics.** Paternalistic-impatient. He treats Rick as a younger sibling he did not choose. He will save Rick's life but will not explain himself to Rick. When Rick is compromised by the Leader, the Devil Hulk's response is grimly efficient — he does not perform grief, he performs containment, and he resents having to.

**Trust/safety.** Mixed. The Devil Hulk does not trust Rick's *judgment* (the Leader compromise confirms a pre-existing assessment) but trusts his *loyalty* to Bruce without reservation. Rick, for his part, fears the Devil Hulk in a way he has never feared any Hulk — he liked Savage, sparred with Fixit, respected Professor. The Devil Hulk he gives a wide berth.

**Evolution.** Pre-*Immortal*: not really a relationship. *Immortal* opening: wary household-mate. Leader arc: enemy-by-occupation. Resolution: convalescent under the Devil Hulk's roof, still uneasy.

**Failure mode.** Underestimating Rick's spiritual/cosmic significance — the Devil Hulk is a basement-and-back-alley operator who consistently treats Rick as a domestic problem when Rick is, structurally, a cosmic chess piece. This blind spot is repeatedly exploited by adversaries operating at a higher level of abstraction than the Devil Hulk natively prefers.

**Leverage.** Rick is the leverage *on* the Devil Hulk, not the other way around — threaten Rick credibly and the Devil Hulk's target-narrowing kicks in. Rick has no real leverage on him in return; the affection runs through Bruce, not through Rick directly.

---

## 4. Jackie McGee

**Status:** Witness, journalist, eventually integrated into the gamma family. The Devil Hulk's most sophisticated relational project.

**History.** Jackie enters as the reporter chasing the Hulk through the early *Immortal* arcs, carrying her own trauma — her childhood Pittsburgh neighborhood destroyed in a Hulk rampage, her father lost in the wreckage. She approaches the Devil Hulk as a subject and an adversary; she ends as a member of his retinue.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's handling of Jackie is the cleanest specimen we have of his *influence* tradecraft. He does not seduce, threaten, or recruit her. He *permits her access*. He lets her witness, lets her doubt, lets her ask, answers slowly, lets her reach her own conclusions across months of contact. This is patience used as a relational primitive — the same patience that converted a Hulkbuster cage into a courtroom, applied to a person. He understands that a journalist's *self-reached* conclusion will hold under pressure where a planted one will not.

**Trust/safety.** Calibrated, never warm. She trusts him to be consistent — to not lie about what he is — and that is enough scaffolding for working alliance. He trusts her to remain a witness rather than become a partisan, which is the role he wants her in: the system's external mirror.

**Evolution.** Adversary → reluctant observer → embedded chronicler → de facto member of Gamma Flight–adjacent inner circle. He never asks her to choose a side; he arranges conditions under which her own choices keep delivering her closer.

**Failure mode.** He treats her trauma as *evidence in his favor* — see, the Hulk hurt you too, see, I am the Hulk who corrects that — which is morally clean from his angle and morally questionable from hers. If she ever decides the correction does not justify the original injury, his framework breaks and his recruitment of her reads, retroactively, as predation. He does not appear to consider this.

**Leverage.** Limited and consensual. He does not have *hold* on her. He has *access*. If she walked, he would let her.

---

## 5. Joe Fixit (intra-system)

**Status:** Delinquent younger brother. The alter the Devil Hulk most consistently *manages downward*.

**History.** Fixit is the gray Las Vegas-era persona — enforcer, hedonist, transactional thinker, dressed for a casino, allergic to introspection. In *Immortal Hulk* Fixit briefly *inhabits Banner's daytime body* in an inverted configuration; the Devil Hulk, on the night shift, has to share the calendar with him.

**Dynamics.** Sibling-rivalry under a parental gloss. The Devil Hulk addresses Fixit with the patient condescension of an older brother handling a teenager who steals the car. Fixit returns sullen non-cooperation, occasional sabotage, and the resentment of a man being lectured by someone he privately considers a fanatic. The Devil Hulk's worldview (justice, household, long horizon) and Fixit's (cash, comfort, today) are nearly antithetical.

**Trust/safety.** Low-grade chronic. They will not betray Bruce to each other's detriment, but they will withhold, mislead, and outmaneuver inside the system constantly.

**Evolution.** Mutual hostility (early *Immortal*) → grudging operational cooperation under sufficient threat → in the late run, a kind of forced coexistence that neither endorses.

**Failure mode.** The Devil Hulk's contempt for Fixit underestimates Fixit's street-level competence. Fixit reads people *transactionally* with great accuracy — a skill the Devil Hulk lacks, because the Devil Hulk reads people *morally*. In situations requiring quick venal calculation, dismissing Fixit costs the system.

**Leverage.** Each can deny the other body-time, which is the only currency that matters between alters. The standoff is permanent.

---

## 6. Savage Hulk (intra-system)

**Status:** Frightened child to be sheltered, occasionally to be deployed.

**History.** Savage is the foundational Hulk — the green roaring boy, the original gamma response. The Devil Hulk regards him as the system's wounded core made physical: not contemptibly, but tenderly, and from a great distance.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk shields Savage from situations Savage cannot navigate (negotiations, captivity, anything requiring stillness) and releases Savage for situations only Savage can resolve (pure-tonnage destruction, the moments where rage is correct). He does not lecture Savage; he soothes him. The voice changes — gentler, simpler — when Savage is the listener inside.

**Trust/safety.** High in one direction (the Devil Hulk genuinely cares for Savage), opaque in the other (Savage's cognition is not high enough to formulate trust as a concept; he reacts to the Devil Hulk as the bigger one who is not hitting him).

**Evolution.** From rival cellmates in the 2000 architecture to protector-and-charge in the *Immortal* household.

**Failure mode.** Sentimentalizing Savage. The Devil Hulk's tender handling of Savage is the one place his moral splitting softens, and it can be exploited — adversaries who can route through Savage (the Leader's manipulations, illusion-based attackers) bypass the Devil Hulk's filters because the Devil Hulk will not be cold to that face.

**Leverage.** Savage is the household's child; threats to him produce target-narrowing in the Devil Hulk faster than threats to anyone else, Bruce included.

---

## 7. Professor Hulk (intra-system, historical)

**Status:** The failed compromise. A predecessor in the executive seat and, in the Devil Hulk's reading, a cautionary tale.

**History.** The Professor was the 1990s integration: Banner intellect, Savage strength, Fixit attitude, fused under therapeutic supervision. He held the executive function the Devil Hulk now holds, and lost it, repeatedly.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's relationship to the Professor is essentially posthumous and adversarial-by-comparison. He treats the Professor's tenure as evidence that *merger is a lie*, that the system cannot be fused, only delegated. Every time integration is proposed, he points internally at the Professor's collapse as the precedent.

**Trust/safety.** N/A — the Professor is structurally dormant during the Devil Hulk's tenure. But the Devil Hulk will not relinquish the seat to a reconstituted Professor.

**Failure mode.** His dismissal of integration is partly motivated reasoning — the Professor's existence threatens the Devil Hulk's necessity. He cannot be a neutral analyst on this question.

**Leverage.** None going either way. The Professor is the *option* the Devil Hulk argues against.

---

## 8. Doc Samson

**Status:** Therapist of the system, mentor in the technical sense, adversary in the structural sense.

**History.** Samson is the gamma-empowered psychiatrist who has been Bruce's analyst across decades. He is the one who, in IH Vol. 2 #13 (2000), conducted the hypnotic descent into the basement where the Devil Hulk was first found. He is therefore the *only* outside person the Devil Hulk has known continuously across his entire surface-record existence.

**Dynamics.** Wary mutual recognition. Samson sees the Devil Hulk for what he is — a persecutor-protector alter — and treats him with the careful courtesy clinicians extend to such configurations, which is to say: as a real party in the room, not a symptom to dissolve. The Devil Hulk respects Samson's *competence* and resents his *project*, which is integration, which is the Devil Hulk's death. The respect is real; the resentment is structural.

**Trust/safety.** Procedural rather than personal. The Devil Hulk will speak honestly to Samson in session because lying defeats the only relationship in which the alter's existence is formally acknowledged. He will not, however, follow Samson's recommendations.

**Evolution.** 2000: discoverer and warden. *Immortal Hulk* and adjacencies: complicated, with Samson himself periodically compromised, deranged, or instrumentalized by larger forces; the Devil Hulk watches these compromises with grim interest as evidence that even Samson cannot finally manage the gamma.

**Failure mode.** The Devil Hulk's respect for Samson is conditional on Samson remaining *outside* the system. The moment Samson would attempt true integration work the Devil Hulk would shift him from the *mentor* category to the *threat* category.

**Leverage.** Samson holds the only key the Devil Hulk acknowledges as a key — the diagnostic vocabulary to name what he is. The Devil Hulk holds, in return, the demonstration that what Samson named cannot be talked out of existence.

---

## 9. The Gamma Mutate Community (Gamma Flight–adjacent)

**Status:** Retainers. A found-family arranged as a household, not a peer group.

**History.** Across *Immortal Hulk* and the spin-out *Gamma Flight* line, a population of gamma-affected people — variously cursed, transformed, ostracized — consolidates loosely around the Banner system. The Devil Hulk is the figure who *organizes* them, and the first Hulk persona in canon to do so.

**Dynamics.** Feudal. He offers protection, structure, a category to belong to, and a target ledger. They offer loyalty, presence, and the moral weight of community that justifies his violence as *defense of someone* rather than as personal vendetta. The arrangement is mutually stabilizing.

**Trust/safety.** He is *reliable* to them in the way a warlord is reliable to villagers — known terms, predictable in defense, dangerous to cross, but the cost of his presence is lower than the cost of his absence.

**Evolution.** None of this existed under any prior Hulk persona. Savage Hulk had Rick and Betty; Fixit had Marlo and a casino payroll; Professor had a marriage. Only the Devil Hulk runs a *people*. This is the cleanest evidence that he is a new developmental layer in the Banner system, not a recycled one.

**Failure mode.** Feudal arrangements collapse when the lord cannot deliver protection. The Devil Hulk's household survives only as long as he can keep its members alive; when external threats scale past his ability (cosmic adversaries, the One Below All), the household fragments and he has no fallback structure.

**Leverage.** They are the moral cover for everything he does. Take the household away and his violence reclassifies, in his own internal accounting, from *protection* to *appetite*. He cannot afford that reclassification.

---

## 10. Brian Banner (the inverted mentor)

**Status:** Not an ally. Listed here because no map of the Devil Hulk's relational field is honest without noting that the foundational *model* in his architecture is the father he was built to kill. Every protective gesture is a calque of a paternal one, inverted. Every household he organizes is the household Brian failed to be. The Devil Hulk's entire repertoire — the calm voice, the certainty, the patience, the willingness to do violence inside the home — is Brian Banner's repertoire turned inside out and aimed back at its source. The wager that *use purifies origin* is the deepest commitment in the file, and it is the only commitment that, if examined too closely by the subject himself, destabilizes everything else listed above.

---

*End Section. Continued in Relationships III — Adversaries, Handlers & Operational Counterparties.*


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

*Note on scope: the Devil Hulk does not "have" lovers in the conventional sense — Bruce Banner has had intimates, and the Devil Hulk has had to negotiate with the fact of them. He is treated here as the negotiator. "Rivals" includes internal rivals (other alters) where the relationship rises to that level of structured antagonism; the broader system-internal map belongs to Relationships I.*

---

## I. RIVALS

### General Reginald Fortean

The defining adversary of the *Immortal Hulk* tenure and the cleanest case study of how the Devil Hulk constructs an enemy.

**History.** Fortean inherits Thunderbolt Ross's Hulkbusters posture after Ross's death, and inherits the moral certainty without inheriting the personal grief that, in Ross, occasionally produced restraint. Their direct contact begins after the Tommy Hill resurrection; Fortean reads the press accounts of the new "night Hulk" and correctly identifies a different actor inside the body. He stages a multi-phase campaign — surveillance through Shadow Base, capture, vivisection-grade interrogation, public framing of the Hulk as a domestic terrorism vector. The Devil Hulk allows almost all of it.

**Dynamics.** Fortean is the first adversary the Devil Hulk treats as a *peer-class* enemy — a man with resources, patience, and a coherent ideology rather than a costumed actor with a grudge. The dynamic is closer to two intelligence services than to hero/villain. Fortean wants the Hulk *understood, mapped, and disassembled*; the Devil Hulk wants Fortean *exposed, isolated, and broken into a use-case for the gamma community*. Each treats the other's institutional infrastructure (Shadow Base on one side, the nascent Gamma Flight / Hulk-aligned mutates on the other) as the real target. Their personal exchanges are quiet and almost courteous.

**Evolution.** Containment → study → reversal → consumption. Early arcs: Fortean owns the board, the Devil Hulk is the captive specimen. Middle: the Devil Hulk has begun to use captivity as reconnaissance, mapping Shadow Base from the inside. Late: Fortean dons a gamma-derived suit and becomes, in effect, a Hulk himself — and at that moment the Devil Hulk's victory becomes total, because Fortean has crossed into the Devil Hulk's category and is judged by the Devil Hulk's rules. Their final confrontation is not a battle but an erasure.

**Trust / Safety.** Zero trust, high *legibility* — each reads the other accurately, which is its own form of safety. Neither lies in the small encounters; both lie in the large ones. The Devil Hulk regards Fortean as the only adversary on the board who could plausibly have killed Bruce permanently if given enough time, and adjusts behavior accordingly.

**Failure mode.** The Devil Hulk's near-failure with Fortean is patience-overshoot. He lets the cage close around him longer than was strategically optimal in order to gather intelligence; the cost is paid by allies (Sasquatch wounded, McGee endangered, Rick Jones tortured into Abomination). The Devil Hulk metabolizes this cost as bookkeeping rather than guilt, which itself is the failure: people he is sworn to protect were spent for an intelligence picture.

**Leverage.** Against Fortean: his identification with Ross. Invoke the dead man and Fortean briefly becomes a son rather than a general. The Devil Hulk uses this exactly once and with surgical effect. Against the Devil Hulk: Fortean discovered, slowly, that hostages from the gamma family produced compliance — not capitulation, but *negotiation*. This is the only leverage he ever held, and the only reason the early arcs were nearly his.

---

### Samuel Sterns — The Leader

The Devil Hulk's antithesis and his most metaphysically dangerous enemy.

**History.** Sterns is the Hulk's oldest intellectual peer-rival; in *Immortal Hulk* he is revealed to have been operating from inside the Green Door system itself, conducting his own decades-long project on the gamma signal and the One Below All. By the time the Devil Hulk is dominant, Sterns has had years of preparation; the Devil Hulk has had months.

**Dynamics.** They are structurally identical and morally inverse. Both are calm. Both are patient. Both are paternalistic toward people they regard as their charges. Both treat suffering as bookkeeping. The difference is that the Devil Hulk's ledger is closed (Bruce + the named family), and Sterns's is open (humanity as a specimen population). Each recognizes the other as the only mind in the room that operates on his timescale, and the recognition is mutual and cold.

**Evolution.** Distant antagonism (Sterns as offstage spider) → direct contact → revelation of Sterns's penetration of the system → unwilling alliance during the One Below All arcs → final adversarial reset. The Devil Hulk's posture toward Sterns moves from underestimation (he initially treats Sterns as a problem in the Banner-Hulk file rather than as his own) to wary respect to active containment-priority.

**Trust / Safety.** No trust; very high *predictive accuracy*. The Devil Hulk can model Sterns's next three moves; Sterns can model his. They both understand that this mutual legibility is what keeps them alive in each other's presence. The handshake of two men who have each calculated the cost of killing the other and found the price currently too high.

**Failure mode.** The Devil Hulk underestimates Sterns's *theological* commitments — Sterns is not merely a strategist, he is a believer in the gamma cosmology, and belief generates moves outside the strategist's frame. This blind spot is structural: the Devil Hulk does not believe in anything beyond his own utility to Bruce.

**Leverage.** Against Sterns: his vanity is real but small; deeper leverage is his need to be *the one who knew*. Pre-empt his revelation and you collapse him. Against the Devil Hulk: Sterns understands earlier than anyone else outside the system that the Devil Hulk is *built from Brian* and weaponizes that diagnosis publicly. This is the cleanest external articulation of the Devil Hulk's deepest wound.

---

### Thunderbolt Ross (legacy rival)

A rival inherited rather than chosen, treated here because the Devil Hulk's relationship to the Ross-figure is structurally identical to his relationship to Brian Banner and reveals the underlying pattern.

**History.** Ross spent decades hunting the Hulk before the Devil Hulk became dominant. By the time the Devil Hulk is in the chair, Ross is dead, has been Red Hulk, has been a father-in-law, has been an antagonist and ally in rotation. The Devil Hulk inherits the *file* on Ross — the institutional memory — without having personally encountered him in most of those configurations.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk regards Ross posthumously with something close to professional respect and personal contempt. Respect for the relentlessness; contempt for the willingness to make Betty collateral damage to his obsession. The Devil Hulk's protectiveness of Betty is, in part, a continuation of an argument with a dead general.

**Evolution.** The relationship exists primarily in retrospect and in Fortean. When Ross briefly returns in the late arcs, the Devil Hulk's posture is unsentimental and final. He treats Ross the way he treats Brian: as a problem the system never properly closed.

**Trust / Safety.** Not applicable in life. In memory: Ross is filed under *fathers who damaged the protected*, second-tier (below Brian, above Fortean).

**Failure mode.** None directly; the Devil Hulk's handling of the Ross file is one of the cleaner pieces of work in his record.

**Leverage.** Asymmetric and posthumous. Ross had real leverage on Banner (Betty, institutional reach); the Devil Hulk has no reciprocal leverage to apply and does not seek any.

---

### The Savage Hulk (internal rival)

Internal-system rival; deserves placement here because the antagonism is structured, longitudinal, and never fully resolved.

**History.** Savage Hulk is the oldest and most public alter. For nearly all of the 2000–2018 period he is the surface; the Devil Hulk is the basement. When the Devil Hulk takes the night, Savage is displaced from primacy for the first time in the system's history. The displacement is not graceful.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk addresses Savage as one would address a frightened, dangerous child — with patience that shades into condescension. Savage understands enough to resent this and not enough to articulate it. Their interactions inside the system are brief, charged, and asymmetric: Devil Hulk reasons, Savage reacts, Devil Hulk waits.

**Evolution.** Containment-by-Savage (2000) → coexistence (early *Immortal Hulk*) → managed subordination (mid) → uneasy partnership under existential threat (late) → reluctant integration. The arc is the Devil Hulk slowly earning, by performance rather than declaration, Savage's grudging acceptance.

**Trust / Safety.** Conditional. Savage trusts that the Devil Hulk will not let Bruce die. Savage does not trust that the Devil Hulk regards him as a person rather than a tool. He is correct on both counts.

**Failure mode.** The Devil Hulk's contempt occasionally slips through the management. When Savage perceives the condescension directly, he rebels at exactly the worst moments — emerging during sunlight, refusing to cede the body, breaking the night-discipline that the Devil Hulk has organized the entire strategy around.

**Leverage.** Against Savage: name Betty, name Rick, name anyone the child loves. Against the Devil Hulk from Savage: refuse the schedule. It is the only move Savage has and the Devil Hulk has no defense against it that does not damage the body they share.

---

### Joe Fixit (internal rival)

A lesser internal rivalry, played in a different key.

**Dynamics.** Where Savage is the unmanageable child, Fixit is the unmanageable adolescent — sly, transactional, sexually present, contemptuous of authority. The Devil Hulk treats Fixit with the firmness of a man who was himself once a worse criminal and is not impressed. Fixit returns the contempt with the wariness of a smaller predator. They do not fight; they negotiate, and the Devil Hulk almost always wins the negotiation, because Fixit's currency is short-term and the Devil Hulk's is long.

**Failure mode.** The Devil Hulk's underestimation of Fixit's appetite for women, drink, and risk leads to repeated minor breaches of the night discipline. Fixit will burn an operation for a single evening's pleasure and shrug. The Devil Hulk has no good answer to genuine hedonism because he does not feel its pull.

**Leverage.** Against Fixit: his vanity, his fondness for being thought clever, his weakness for being treated as the eldest among the alters. Flatter him with seniority and he will sit down. Against the Devil Hulk: Fixit knows where the body has been and can produce embarrassments at will.

---

## II. ENEMIES

### Brian Banner

The foundational enemy. The only target the Devil Hulk has ever named in advance, in print, in 2000, and pursued to literal completion two decades later.

**History.** Brian Banner is the original wound — physicist, alcoholic, gamma-paranoid, child-beater, wife-killer. He died before Bruce's adulthood; he then surfaced periodically in afterlife/dream sequences across decades of canon. He is, structurally, the reason the Devil Hulk exists. The Devil Hulk is the architecture a small Bruce built specifically against him.

**Dynamics.** Pure predatory fixation, organized into a life-goal, deferred for forty subjective years. Every other relationship in the Devil Hulk's record is shaped by the negative space of this one — the protectiveness toward Bruce, the management of Savage, the contempt for Brian-like figures (Ross, in part Fortean), the moral splitting of the world into "his people" and "Brian's class." When the Below-Place finally gives him access, the encounter is not a fight; it is a ritual. He kills Brian's soul. The narrative permits him to do it again. He does it again. He does it as many times as the story will allow.

**Evolution.** Promise (2000) → forty years of waiting → execution → repetition compulsion. The repetition is the diagnostic event. A healthier alter would have killed Brian once and rested. The Devil Hulk kills him until the story takes Brian away.

**Trust / Safety.** Inapplicable. The relationship is execution.

**Failure mode.** Completion. The destruction of Brian deprives the Devil Hulk of his organizing object. He compensates by promoting Fortean, then Sterns, then the One Below All into the empty slot — but none of them *fit*, and the Devil Hulk's late-tenure restlessness reads in part as the irritability of a hunter whose primary quarry has been killed and who cannot quite admit that no replacement is equivalent.

**Leverage.** Brian's leverage on him was, finally, that Brian made him. The Devil Hulk cannot destroy what Brian made without destroying himself. He knows this. It is the only thing in the file that he refuses to discuss.

---

### The One Below All

The metaphysical enemy. The Devil Hulk's most revealing engagement, because it is the one fight he cannot win by patience.

**History.** The One Below All is the gamma cosmology's antagonist-deity, the entity at the bottom of the Green Door, the source of the immortality and the price of it. The Devil Hulk encounters it in the Hell arcs and is forced into the only register he is genuinely unprepared for: the sacred.

**Dynamics.** Where Savage Hulk would rage and Banner would collapse, the Devil Hulk *bargains*. He treats the One Below All as a hostile sovereign rather than a god — extends the diplomatic protocol that worked on Fortean and Sterns upward to a cosmic class. It does not work in the same way. The One Below All cannot be flattered or maneuvered; it can only be refused. The Devil Hulk's refusal is his finest hour and his first encounter with a problem his architecture was not built to solve.

**Evolution.** Naïve negotiation → recognition of category mismatch → grim continuation of negotiation anyway, because there is no other tool. He does not learn a new register. He does the only thing he can do, harder.

**Trust / Safety.** None possible. He is in the presence of something that regards him as the diorama regards the modeler.

**Failure mode.** Theological flat-footedness. He has no relationship to meaning beyond utility-to-Bruce. The One Below All is meaning-without-utility. He cannot get traction.

**Leverage.** He has none. This is the file's only entry under that heading in which the column is honestly blank.

---

### The Hulkbusters (institutional enemy)

**History.** Multi-decade institutional adversary; under Fortean, professionalized into a Shadow Base apparatus that comes closer to disassembling the Hulk than any prior iteration.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk treats the Hulkbusters as a *staff* rather than as soldiers — he reads them individually, learns names, identifies the weak link, the believer, the cynic, the careerist. He selects whom to break and whom to leave. The dismantling of the team is not a battle; it is a personnel action.

**Evolution.** Cage (he allows capture) → study (he learns the org chart from inside) → reversal (he begins picking them off in order of strategic value) → erasure (the institution dissolves with Fortean).

**Trust / Safety.** Asymmetric. He is safer among them than they realize, because they have him on a table; they are less safe than they realize, because being on his table means he is reading them.

**Failure mode.** Collateral damage among Hulkbusters with families he had no quarrel with. He files this under bookkeeping. The reader, and possibly Bruce, do not.

**Leverage.** Against them: their command structure is fragile and their morale assumes the Hulk is an animal. Demonstrating otherwise (the diner-counter, the courteous speech, the named recognition) corrodes the unit faster than violence does. Against him: hostages, always hostages.

---

### Xemnu, the Minotaur, and the lesser cosmology

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's handling of the secondary monsters of the *Immortal Hulk* run is brisk and disrespectful. He treats Xemnu, in particular, as a pretender — a noisy claimant to the Hulk-category who has not done the work. The encounters are short and the Devil Hulk's affect is closer to *irritation at presumption* than to fear.

**Failure mode.** He occasionally moves too quickly against these figures because they bore him, and bored Devil Hulk is a sloppier Devil Hulk than patient Devil Hulk.

**Leverage.** Their vanity. He has no use for his own and recognizes others' instantly.

---

### Tommy Hill (the trigger)

The man whose bullet started the *Immortal Hulk* era and, in doing so, gave the Devil Hulk the chair.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk's posture toward Hill is unusual. Hill killed Bruce; the Devil Hulk should regard him as a primary enemy. He does not. He regards Hill as an *instrument* — the accidental midwife of the new arrangement. The handling is contemptuous but not vengeful. This is one of the cleanest data points that the Devil Hulk's targeting is *moral* rather than reactive: a man who actually killed Bruce is filed lower than a man (Brian) who hurt a child Bruce decades earlier, because the *meaning* of the act matters more than the act.

**Leverage.** None pursued. Hill is left to his own machinery.

---

## III. INTIMATES & LOVERS — Negotiated, Not Held

### Betty Ross / Red Harpy

The most important woman in the file and the one the Devil Hulk handles with the most care.

**History.** Bruce's wife, daughter of Ross, decades of canonical entanglement, killed and resurrected, now (in the *Immortal Hulk* era) the Red Harpy — a gamma-mutated raptor configuration with her own grievances and her own autonomy. The Devil Hulk inherits her as a fact rather than choosing her.

**Dynamics.** He does not love Betty the way Bruce does. He does not desire her at all — there is no record of the Devil Hulk in any sexual posture toward anyone, and the absence is structural rather than incidental. He regards Betty as *Bruce's*, which in his moral order means his job is to keep her alive, keep her free, and not interfere with whatever she and Bruce work out between them. The Harpy configuration complicates this: she is now also a peer, a fellow gamma, a member of his family-of-monsters. He treats her in two registers simultaneously — as the liege's consort and as a colleague in arms — and manages the registers with notable delicacy.

**Trust / Safety.** Higher than almost any other entry in the file. He does not lie to her. He does not maneuver her. He gives her information Bruce would withhold. She, in turn, is the only person who has been allowed to criticize him to his face without consequence — she calls him on his paternalism more than once, and he absorbs it with the grave attentiveness of a man who has decided in advance that this particular voice gets heard.

**Evolution.** Wariness (he is, after all, frightening) → working alliance during the Shadow Base arcs → genuine partnership during the Hell descent and Fortean endgame → something like family by the close. The evolution is one of the few in his record that ends warmer than it began.

**Failure mode.** He cannot accept Betty making choices that endanger her. When she chooses risk, his protective architecture activates against her interests, and she perceives it as the Brian-shape under the surface. The argument that follows is the closest he comes, in the entire run, to losing emotional composure.

**Leverage.** Against him: she is the leverage. Threaten her and he goes still and cold and total. Bruce knows it. Sterns knows it. Fortean partially knew it and did not press hard enough. Against her: nothing. He has nothing he is willing to use on Betty, and the asymmetry is itself the relationship.

---

### Jennifer Walters — She-Hulk

**Dynamics.** Cousin to Bruce; the Devil Hulk treats her as *family-not-charge* — kin he respects without claiming. The relationship is the cleanest in the file because there is nothing he wants from her and nothing he is willing to do to her. He addresses her courteously, listens when she speaks, defers on legal matters in a slightly amused way, and would, if necessary, die before letting harm reach her.

**Trust / Safety.** High and lateral. She is one of two or three people (Betty, McGee being the others) on whose word he will adjust an operation in progress.

**Failure mode.** She, more than Betty, can name the Brian-shape and be heard. When she does, the Devil Hulk does not argue. He goes quiet, which in his system is the precursor to either capitulation or violence; with her, always capitulation.

**Leverage.** Against him: her moral authority. Against her: none. He will not.

---

### Jackie McGee

Not a lover; a chosen confidante and (in the Devil Hulk's classification) an *adopted member of the protected class*. The relationship belongs in this section because it is one of the very few elective intimacies in his record.

**Dynamics.** McGee is a journalist with a personal stake — her home was destroyed in a Hulk event in childhood — and she comes hunting answers. The Devil Hulk does something unexpected: he lets her hunt. He does not stage-manage her conclusions. He lets her witness, doubt, and arrive. This is the most sustained piece of *non-coercive* influence in the file, and it works. She ends up as the chronicler of the gamma family in part because he never tried to make her one.

**Trust / Safety.** Built incrementally, unusually durable. The trust is not friendship; it is mutual recognition of professional integrity across a hostile border.

**Failure mode.** He treats her, eventually, as he treats Betty — protectively, which she perceives as paternalism, which she resents. The pattern is identical and the diagnostic is the same: any woman he claims becomes, over time, slightly captured.

**Leverage.** Against him: her judgment. He cares what she writes. Against her: he could have, at any moment, made her career or ended it; he chose not to, and that choice is the relationship.

---

### Rick Jones

Bruce's oldest friend; the Devil Hulk's adopted nephew-figure and, in the worst stretch of the run, the source of his deepest unhandled grief.

**Dynamics.** The Devil Hulk regards Rick as *Bruce's brother* and therefore as his own kin by extension. The affection is real and the protectiveness is total. When Rick is tortured into the Abomination and then killed and re-killed across the run, the Devil Hulk handles it badly by his own standards — the bookkeeping does not balance, the targets do not satisfy, the grief does not metabolize.

**Trust / Safety.** Full on the Devil H


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: "THE DEVIL HULK"
## Section 6: Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

*Cross-reference: Sections 2 (Medical) and 3 (Psychological). The capacity inventory below is filtered for what this specific alter actually wields — not what the Banner body can theoretically produce. The distinction matters. Savage Hulk and the Devil Hulk share a chassis and use it differently in the way two drivers share a car and one of them parks.*

---

### 6.1 The Substrate: What the Body Itself Provides

Before cataloging what the Devil Hulk *does* with the gamma-saturated body, the inventory of what the body *is* under his control:

**Raw strength.** Functionally indexed in the Class 100+ tier of the Banner body's strength curve, though — and this is the operative caveat — the Devil Hulk's measured output rarely *peaks* the body's available ceiling. Savage Hulk's strength scales with rage; the merged Worldbreaker form scales toward cosmic-tier expression; the Devil Hulk's strength scales with **task requirement**. He uses what the job requires and not more. Tearing a Hulkbuster suit apart at the seams is a different motor program than uprooting a mountain, and he has been observed selecting the former with surgical economy. The strength is present. The exhibition of it is rationed.

**Durability and damage absorption.** The Banner body under the Devil Hulk presents the standard gamma-tier resistance: small-arms fire is irrelevant; tank rounds, energy weapons, and ordnance at the General Fortean / Shadow Base tier produce damage but not incapacitation; specialty weapons (gamma-disruptors, the various Hulkbuster prototypes, hellfire, certain mystical instruments) can wound seriously. The Devil Hulk's signature against damage is not its absorption but its **performance of submission to it**. He has stood still and let acid be poured on him. He has allowed himself to be vivisected. He has permitted dismemberment as field-research. The capacity is *durability as theater* — and the audience is the people doing the cutting.

**Regeneration.** This is the load-bearing power for everything else he does. The Banner body in the *Immortal Hulk* regime returns, intact, from states up to and including total physical dissolution, via the Green Door mechanism that anchors resurrection to sundown. For the Devil Hulk specifically, this is not a "healing factor" in the X-Men sense — it is *resurrection on a schedule*. The behavioral consequence is enormous and is treated in Section 6.8.

**Sensory acuity.** Sharpened. He has demonstrated tracking by scent (the gas station sequence, the early gamma-touched hunts), discrimination of heartbeat changes in interrogation subjects, and a markedly expanded peripheral vision consistent with the wider-set, predator-configured eyes of his phenotype. The Savage Hulk has the same sensory hardware but uses it like a startled animal; the Devil Hulk uses it like a forensic instrument.

**The morphology itself as a capacity.** The Devil Hulk is *taller, leaner, longer-armed* than Savage Hulk on the same body. This is not cosmetic. The elongated reach is a combat asset — he can strike from outside the engagement envelope an opponent has measured for the standard Hulk silhouette. The hunched, forward-loaded posture loads weight onto the forelimbs and frees a longer striking arc. The grin, technically, is a threat-display whose function is to terminate fights before they occur. Each morphological feature is *useful*. The persona did not select a frightening shape for aesthetic reasons; he selected a tactically optimal one and it happens to also be frightening.

---

### 6.2 Strength: Use Patterns and Signature Applications

The Devil Hulk's strength applications fall into four observable categories:

**(a) Architectural disassembly.** He prefers to take structures apart rather than collapse them. The Hulkbuster arc shows him peeling vehicle armor, removing plates, separating welds — leaving the operator exposed rather than crushing operator and machine together. This is strength used as *can-opener* rather than as hammer. The tactical purpose is to preserve the contents (for interrogation, for witness-creation, for personalized verdict).

**(b) Anatomical isolation.** He has been observed snapping single bones, dislocating specific joints, removing specific limbs, and otherwise applying violence in *increments*. Savage Hulk does not do this. Fixit does it sometimes, gangster-style. The Devil Hulk does it constantly, and the increments correlate with what he wants the target to feel or to say. Strength here is a torture instrument and an interrogation instrument simultaneously.

**(c) Demonstrative violence against the deserving.** When he kills, the kill is *visible* and *legible*. The body is left in a configuration that communicates the verdict to whoever finds it. This is strength used as signature. It carries forensic risk he calculates as worth it; the message-to-living matters more than the survival-of-himself.

**(d) Restrained protection.** The handling of Jackie McGee, Rick Jones, Betty in vulnerable states, and human bystanders he has decided are within his protection: he has the same body that has thrown tanks, and he uses it to lift, shield, carry. The granularity of strength control implied is extreme — he can apply a tank-throwing musculature to lifting a sleeping woman without harm. Savage Hulk does not have this calibration. It is not a power; it is a *skill on top of the power*.

---

### 6.3 Durability and Pain as Tactical Instruments

This is one of the most distinctive items in the inventory and worth specifying.

Standard Hulk durability is reactive: the body absorbs damage so the persona can keep fighting. The Devil Hulk's use of durability is **proactive**: the body absorbs damage so the persona can keep *gathering*. Pain becomes a probe.

Operational signature: when captured or attacked, the Devil Hulk's first observable response is *stillness*. He allows the first several rounds of input to occur uninterrupted. The behavioral output during this phase looks like passivity. It is not. He is mapping — weapons inventory, personnel count, command hierarchy, language tells, who flinches, who enjoys it, who is afraid of him, who is afraid of the colleague next to them. The Hulkbuster torture arcs read, on first inspection, as the Hulk being broken. On second inspection they read as the Hulk taking depositions.

Limit: there are damage thresholds (gamma-disruption, soul-tier attack, hellfire of certain grades) that can drop him *out of consciousness* before he completes the intelligence acquisition, and a small number of weapons (the more refined gamma-disruptors, certain artifacts) that can suppress regeneration long enough that he loses access to the body and another persona takes the field. The Devil Hulk knows this and treats those weapons as priority targets — when he identifies one in an opponent's arsenal, his patience curve shortens dramatically.

---

### 6.4 Regeneration, Resurrection, and the Behavioral Consequence

The body resurrects. The Devil Hulk, more than any other alter, has *built his strategy around this*.

**Mechanism.** Sundown to sunrise: the alter's active window. Death during that window produces regeneration in place or, if dissolution is total, return via the Green Door at sundown of a subsequent day. The persona has functional immortality on a circadian leash.

**Strategic consequences he exploits:**

- **Sacrificial advance.** He will move toward fire that would kill any mortal opponent, knowing the cost is temporary. Opponents calibrated to the assumption that beings avoid death cannot read his approach vector.
- **Information through death.** He has died, and on at least one occasion has *used* the death-and-resurrection cycle as transit — entering states (the Below-Place, certain liminal zones) accessible only by dying. Death as a door.
- **The negotiation posture.** Because he cannot be permanently killed, threats against his life are inert. This produces a peculiar calm in his negotiations: no opponent can offer him the one thing (continued existence) that motivates most negotiation. He must be offered things that *matter* to him — access to a target, protection of someone he has claimed, integration on his terms.

**Limits.** Resurrection is not invulnerability — he experiences each death. The dissociative-somatic record suggests he *remembers* deaths in a way that Savage Hulk does not. The behavioral evidence — increasing patience, increasing economy, decreasing taste for unnecessary engagement — is consistent with an entity that is *learning from its deaths*. Mortality is a teacher he keeps re-enrolling with.

---

### 6.5 Cognitive Capacities — Intelligence as a Power in Its Own Right

This is the abilities-category most under-appreciated in casual reads of the persona. The Devil Hulk is intelligent in a specific, operational way:

**(a) Long-horizon planning.** He runs schemes across arcs, not scenes. The Hulkbusters' destruction, the gamma-community assembly, the Brian Banner confrontation are all set up phases in advance and brought to closure with patience that no other Hulk persona possesses. Operational time-horizon: years. He is the only Hulk persona who *plans like Banner does* — and unlike Banner, he executes.

**(b) Investigative reasoning.** The opening arcs of *Immortal Hulk* show him running an actual case — connecting gamma-touched incidents, identifying the Green Door phenomenon, locating Shadow Base. The cognitive style is closer to a homicide detective's than a brawler's: pattern-finding, witness work, scene reconstruction.

**(c) Influence and management.** He recruits and runs the gamma-mutate community. He handles Jackie McGee with a sophistication that includes letting her doubt him, letting her witness things she will be unable to forgive, and giving her the autonomy to choose anyway. He manages the internal alters — Savage, Fixit, Banner himself — as a senior executive manages difficult direct reports.

**(d) Tactical reading of opponents.** He correctly identifies, on first encounter, what each opponent is afraid of. This is not telepathy; it is observation against an enormous internal catalog of human fear-responses, accumulated from forty subjective years of watching from behind the bars while other Hulks took the field.

**Limit.** His intelligence has blind spots. He underestimates *love* as a motivator outside his own claim-set — he treats other people's attachments as exploitable but not respectable. He also underestimates Bruce's capacity to refuse him, repeatedly, throughout *Immortal Hulk*, until very late. Strategic genius with a paternalistic blind spot is still strategic genius with a blind spot.

---

### 6.6 Specialized Capabilities

**Inter-alter communication and system arbitration.** Within the Banner system the Devil Hulk has demonstrated the capacity to *speak with* and *coordinate among* the other alters in a way no other persona reliably can. He is the only Hulk who can negotiate Savage Hulk's emergence in a fight, can let Fixit hold the body for a stretch when discretion or money are required, and can pass control back to Banner without internal sabotage. This is, functionally, an executive-management capacity inside the system. Limit: the other alters retain veto power in extremis; he cannot *force* the body to be his against unified internal resistance.

**The Green Door access.** He has navigated the Below-Place, parlayed with entities at its threshold, and returned. This is not a "power" in the conventional sense but a **familiarity** — the route is known to him in a way it is not known to Banner or to Savage Hulk. Whether this constitutes a capacity or a curse depends on the framing.

**Threat-display through stillness and smile.** Catalog this as a power because it functions as one. Opponents read his fixed grin, his lack of bluster, his unhurried speech, and many of them surrender or flee before contact is made. This is conservation of energy via reputation, and it is a learned capacity — early appearances show more snarl, later appearances show more smile. The smile is more efficient.

**Tolerance of being lied to that he detects but allows.** He notices deception within minutes, often immediately, and frequently does not act on it. He lets the deceiver continue, watching the shape of the lie. This is interrogation through patience — a capacity that requires intelligence, durability, and the absence of ego-injury all at once. Few opponents in the Banner record have survived being permitted to lie to him for very long.

---

### 6.7 What He Does Not Do — The Limits That Define the Profile

The negative space of the capability inventory is as diagnostic as the positive:

- **He does not display the Worldbreaker / cosmic-tier expressions.** Whether he is *incapable* of these or merely *uninterested* is open. The behavioral evidence suggests the latter — they are inefficient for his goals, which are personal and selective rather than territorial.
- **He does not use the body for travel-feats on the Savage Hulk scale.** No continent-crossing leaps. Movement is local, on-foot, often deliberately pedestrian. He walks into diners.
- **He does not engage in the property-destruction signature of Savage Hulk.** Collateral damage is minimized — not from compassion for the structures but because broken cities draw the wrong attention to the wrong investigation.
- **He does not initiate combat with opponents not on his list.** Provoked, he will respond proportionally; unprovoked, he passes by. The capacity for restraint is itself a capability, and it is the one Savage Hulk most conspicuously lacks.
- **He does not regenerate identity damage.** Physical wounds close; insults to the project of *who he is* (see Section 3, the Brian-Banner-resemblance pressure point) do not. The body is immortal; the persona is not. He can be argued out of existence in a way he cannot be killed out of it. This is the most important limit in the entire inventory.

---

### 6.8 Growth Curve Across the Record

**2000 (caged phase).** Capacities present but unexpressed. He demonstrates only voice — the measured English, the promise, the patience. The system contains him precisely because his capabilities are recognized as too dangerous to release. Power inventory: latent.

**The dormant decades.** Brief flickers — the more cunning Hulk that appears in *World War Hulk* at moments shares his cognitive style — but no full expression. The capabilities, by his own later testimony, did not atrophy. They were rehearsed internally.

**2018–2021 (operational phase).** Full expression. He has clearly *practiced*. The investigative methodology, the management of subordinates, the calibrated violence, the manipulation of the resurrection cycle — none of these read as improvised. They read as a skill set developed over forty subjective years of waiting and observing, finally given a field to operate on.

**Endgame.** Capacity-curve does not peak in violence but in *negotiation*. By the late *Immortal Hulk* arcs the most powerful thing he does is consent — to integration, to handoff, to standing down. The final capability the file records is the one he was least expected to possess: the ability to choose not to use the others.

---

### 6.9 Symptom-as-Signature

Each capability above can be re-read as a symptom of the etiology specified in Sections 3 and 4. This is not reductionism — it is the diagnostic key.
