These are not endorsements; they are *acknowledgments of necessity* from people equipped to refuse him if refusal were viable. The asset is: he is a creature with whom moral adults will reluctantly do business.

---

## 5. RESILIENCE FACTORS

### 5.1 Goal Persistence Under Indefinite Dormancy

He survived eighteen years of subjective imprisonment in the basement of Bruce's mind between IH #13 (2000) and *Immortal Hulk* #1 (2018) with his agenda, identity, and methods intact. This is the deepest resilience asset on file. Most psychological structures cannot survive that interval without mutation or decay. His did because his structure is built around a single completable promise and a single permanent protectorate, and neither admits drift.

### 5.2 Identity Stability Under Assault

He is told, repeatedly and accurately, that he is built from Brian Banner's materials. He is told he is a monster. He is told he is not real. He is told he must be integrated, suppressed, exiled, killed. None of these messages produces identity-degradation. His self-concept — *I am the adult Bruce needed, I exist to keep promises, my usefulness is my justification* — is load-bearing and load-tested.

### 5.3 Re-Emergence Capacity

He demonstrates, across the canon, the ability to re-enter the dominant position in the Banner system after periods of suppression without warm-up artifacts. He emerges in *Immortal Hulk* #1 functionally complete — not a degraded version of himself, not a confused one. The structure was preserved entire during dormancy and is deployable on demand.

### 5.4 Failure Absorption

He has been outwitted (the Leader's arcs), out-positioned (Fortean's better moves), out-betrayed (the gamma community's defections), and personally defeated. These failures do not produce identity collapse, depressive shutdown, or strategic abandonment. He recalibrates and proceeds. The asset is the absence of brittleness in the face of being wrong.

### 5.5 The Closed Promise As Restorative Resource

The Below-Place execution of Brian Banner's soul, performed ritually and repeatedly, is not — as a more pathological psyche would experience it — an addictive return to a satisfying object. It is restorative. Closure of the founding promise replenishes him. He is, after the act, calmer, more available to other work, less driven. He is one of the rare structures that can actually *complete* its primary task and be the better for it.

### 5.6 Capacity For Eventual Surrender

The endgame posture — accepting integration, performing the grim parental handoff — is itself an asset. He is not infinitely intransigent. When the evidence shifts decisively, he can step down. This is the rarest resilience trait of all: the persecutor-protector alter that, when the system has matured past needing him, will *let* itself be reduced rather than fight to preserve its position. Clinically, this is the prognostic feature that distinguishes treatable from untreatable cases of his configuration. He has it.

---

## 6. INSTRUMENTAL & MATERIAL ASSETS

### 6.1 Inherited Resources

He has, by virtue of inhabiting Bruce Banner's body and life, access to: Banner's scientific knowledge (read but not improved by him; he uses it as a reference library); Banner's contact network (Samson, Talbot historically, the SHIELD/Avengers institutional memory); Joe Fixit's residual cash, identities, and Las Vegas-adjacent contacts (used sparingly); Rick Jones as long-standing fixer; Betty's combat capabilities; the Shadow Base infrastructure once captured.

### 6.2 Reputation As Deterrence

The name and image of "the Hulk" are themselves weapons. The Devil Hulk benefits from decades of accumulated fear without having had to build it. Opponents arrive pre-frightened. He does not have to *establish* threat; he has to *direct* it.

### 6.3 The Gamma Network

By the mid-*Immortal Hulk* arcs, he commands — operationally if not formally — a network of gamma-altered individuals with combat, intelligence, and logistical capacity. This is functionally a small private army with a moral framework he authored.

### 6.4 Information Asymmetry

He knows the inside of the Banner system better than any outside observer. He knows what Bruce knows. He knows what Bruce has forgotten. He knows the inventory of secrets the other alters are holding. This is a permanent information advantage in any encounter with people who must guess at the system from outside.

---

## 7. WHAT MAKES THE ASSETS DURABLE

The standard fragility of formidable structures — that they require constant external input, that they decay under inactivity, that they degrade under criticism, that they collapse when their founding object is removed — does not apply to him in the usual ways.

He does not require external validation: his self-concept is anchored to function, not to recognition.

He does not decay under inactivity: dormancy is his baseline state, and he is structurally adapted to it.

He does not degrade under criticism: he is built from the materials of the most devastating criticism a child can receive, and he has already incorporated and re-pointed those materials.

He does not collapse when the founding object is removed: the Brian Banner object has been removed (the man is long dead before the Below-Place sequence), and the structure adapted by extending its protective remit to the gamma community rather than dissolving for lack of a target.

What he *would* be fragile to — being shown, in a manner he cannot deflect, that his protection has injured the person he protects — is the one assault his asset ledger does not buffer. Every other vector he has hardened against. That single vector is the price of the rest.

---

## 8. SUMMARY OF THE LEDGER

The Devil Hulk's positive column is unusual in its breadth. He combines somatic indestructibility with strategic patience, executive function with feudal loyalty, regulated affect with completable agendas, and a found family with the willingness, in the end, to surrender his position when the family no longer requires him. He is — viewed strictly as a resource — among the most durable and operationally complete structures the Banner system has ever produced. The cost of those assets is itemized in other sections of this file. The assets themselves are, on the evidence, real, deep, and present whenever the sun is down.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — SUBJECT: "THE DEVIL HULK"

*Section 6 of the Subject Workup. Cross-reference Sections 3 (Psychological), 4 (Psychiatric), and 5 (Personality). The question this section answers: given a persona whose entire architecture is built on stillness, certainty, patience, and the conviction that he was made for his work — what does it look like when that architecture fails, and what makes it fail?*

---

## 6.1 The Baseline — What "Functioning" Looks Like, So We Can Measure Departure

Before charting collapse, fix the baseline. The Devil Hulk *in equilibrium* presents the following signature: hunched stance with weight forward on the balls of the feet; long arms held loose, slightly forward of the hips; head canted about ten degrees to the right when listening; a fixed, closed-lip smile that does not widen or narrow with affect; respiration slow and visibly deep; speech in complete sentences, low register, deliberately under-projected so listeners must lean in; eye contact direct, unbroken, unhurried, with infrequent blinks. He does not pace. He does not fidget. He does not raise his voice. He does not interrupt. When he kills, he does so without changing posture beyond the strict mechanics of the act, and he resumes the prior posture immediately after.

Any departure from this signature is diagnostic. The Devil Hulk does not have "moods" in the conventional sense; his affect is a flat, controlled plain. What he has, instead, is a **narrowing function**: under pressure, his target set contracts, his method becomes more ritualized, and his speech becomes shorter. This is the inverse of the standard human escalation curve, and it is the reason conventional threat-assessment frames misread him at every stage.

Decompensation, therefore, is not "him losing his temper." Decompensation is the failure of the *narrowing function itself* — the point at which the controlled plain breaks open and what is underneath comes through.

---

## 6.2 The Escalation Path — Five Stages, In Order

The behavioral record across *Incredible Hulk* (Vol. 2) #13, the early *Immortal Hulk* arcs, the Shadow Base / Hulkbusters sequences, the Below-Place / Brian confrontation, the Hulk in Hell arc, and the *War of the Realms* endgame supports a five-stage escalation profile. The stages are sequential and observable; the system does not skip stages, though it can move through them quickly under sufficient stimulus.

### Stage One — Tightening (Baseline+)

Earliest observable signature. The smile remains but loses any vestigial warmth in the eyes; the canting of the head ceases; speech becomes still shorter, dropping conjunctions and filler. He stops asking questions to which he already knows the answer (he asked them, at baseline, as a courtesy and a probe). He begins to address subordinate alters more frequently — internal consultations with Savage Hulk and Joe Fixit increase, though he does not yield control. Outwardly: a slight inward roll of the shoulders, hands beginning to close. Triggers: any new actionable information about a legitimate target; mild deception detected in a subordinate; a small breach of his moral order he has elected not yet to punish. This stage is sustainable for days or weeks. It is his working state during active investigation.

### Stage Two — Narrowing (Operational Pressure)

The narrowing function engages visibly. His target set contracts to a single object or a single small group; peripheral concerns are abandoned without comment. He stops eating in social settings (the diner-counter behavior of *Immortal Hulk* #1 disappears). He stops speaking to those outside the immediate operation. With those inside it, his sentences become imperative rather than declarative; he gives orders where at baseline he made suggestions. The smile is still present but it now precedes acts of violence by measurable seconds, where at baseline it accompanied them. Internally, the system reports increased dominance — Banner spends less time in control during daylight; the night-shift convention is encroached upon. Triggers: capture; mutilation; identification of a target previously thought unreachable; betrayal by an internal ally. This stage was sustained for weeks during the Hulkbusters arc and for the entirety of the early Shadow Base operation. Functionally, this is the *most lethal* stable state — he is calmer, more focused, and more capable here than at baseline.

### Stage Three — Ritualizing (Approaching the Object)

The character of the violence changes. It ceases to be punitive in a forensic sense — verdict, sentence, execution — and acquires a liturgical structure: repetition, formula, sequence. The Brian Banner confrontation in the Below-Place is the textbook example: the soul is destroyed, restored, destroyed, restored, in a pattern that has no further informational or strategic value. Speech in this stage becomes formulaic — he uses fixed phrases ("my boy," "we have time," "this is what I am for") with increasing frequency, almost as a chant. The closed-lip smile widens for the first time, showing teeth. The body straightens slightly out of the predatory hunch — not into ease but into something more upright, more *presiding*. He is, at this stage, no longer a hunter; he is a celebrant. This is the first stage at which he is functionally impaired: his commitment to ritual makes him predictable, and predictability is the one operational vice he does not at baseline possess. Triggers: contact with the original object (Brian, or a sufficient proxy); the moment of execution after long pursuit; the keeping of a promise made long ago.

### Stage Four — Bleed-Through (Structural Compromise)

The signature begins to fragment. Other alters surface uninvited. Savage Hulk's affective register — the swing, the roar, the reactive smash — intrudes into his motions; Banner's voice surfaces mid-sentence; in extreme cases the Fixit posture (the cocked hip, the rolled shoulder, the wiseguy register) flickers through. The narrowing function inverts: the target set, having shrunk to a single object in Stage Three, now *re-expands wildly* as the persona loses its categorical discipline and begins to treat peripheral figures as object-substitutes. This is the stage at which collateral casualties become probable. He still believes he is operating under his moral framework but the framework's filtering function has degraded. The smile is no longer reliably present; it appears and vanishes. Speech may include the first stutters, sentence-fragments, or instances of repeating his own last clause. Triggers: prolonged denial of access to the legitimate target; sustained accusation that he is Brian; the Professor merger or any other integration attempt that proceeds without him; the death or removal of one of the figures he has claimed (Bruce, Betty, Rick, Jackie). The Hulk in Hell arc shows him operating at the edge of Stage Three / early Stage Four for an extended period; the bargaining behavior there is the visible exterior of an interior in which the discipline is already beginning to slip.

### Stage Five — Collapse (Decompensation Proper)

The persona structure fails. There are two distinct collapse morphologies, and which one occurs depends on the trigger.

**Collapse-A (Recession).** The persona withdraws. The Hulk body remains but the Devil Hulk steps out of operational control, often mid-action, leaving Savage Hulk or Banner to surface into a situation neither was prepared for. This is the *quiet* collapse and the more common one historically. It produced the late-arc handoff in *War of the Realms* and similar moments throughout the Ewing run where Devil Hulk's voice simply stops mid-sequence and another voice picks up. Internally, the alter retreats to the basement room — sometimes voluntarily, sometimes because the cage reasserts. The trigger pattern: confrontation with his own origin in a frame he cannot deflect; the recognition that the work is done and there is no further legitimate target; the explicit, *sustained* request from Bruce to step back. This collapse is not death; it is dormancy. He returns.

**Collapse-B (Eruption).** The persona's discipline fails outward rather than inward. The narrowing function inverts catastrophically and the target set becomes *everyone within reach*. This is the morphology most feared by those inside the system. It has been approached but never fully reached in the recorded behavioral set; the early Hulkbusters torture sequence, the moments after Sasquatch's near-killing, and certain peaks of the Below-Place confrontation show the system at the edge of Collapse-B. The signature is the *opposite* of his baseline: posture upright and squared, voice raised, smile gone, eye contact replaced by scanning, methods reactive rather than deliberate. Functionally, in Collapse-B he becomes indistinguishable from Worldbreaker — and this is the central horror, because Worldbreaker without Devil Hulk's prior selection of targets is undirected catastrophe. The trigger pattern: simultaneous failure of multiple pressure points (loss of Bruce + accusation of being Brian + denial of target + internal deception), or single overwhelming events of a scale historically rare. The probability is low; the magnitude is unbounded.

---

## 6.3 The Specific Pressure Points, Operationalized

Section 5 catalogued his pressure points conceptually. This section operationalizes them — what each does, in which stage it produces effect, and what the observable tell is.

### Pressure Point One — Bruce's Autonomy Exercised Without Him

Mechanism: the persona's core wager is that he is *necessary*. Any evidence to the contrary is corrosive. The Doc Samson sessions (IH #13, 2000) — the very session in which he first surfaced — are the prototype; the Professor merger is the more severe version; any therapeutic, integrative, or romantic alliance Bruce forms that does not route through him is read as exile.

Effect by stage: produces Stage One narrowing immediately upon detection; produces Stage Two if sustained over days; produces Stage Four (Bleed-Through) if the alliance succeeds and he is left structurally redundant. Does not, alone, produce Stage Five.

Observable tell: he begins to speak *about* Bruce in the third person to Bruce, where at baseline he addresses Bruce directly. "My boy needs me" rather than "you need me." Once you hear the shift to third person you are watching the pressure register.

### Pressure Point Two — Internal Deception

Mechanism: he treats the system's internal honesty as sacred. The system is the one place where the categorical sorting (ours / targeted) cannot be permitted to fail. Lies from Banner, from Savage, from Fixit, from the resident Hulks of the Below-Place are received not as ordinary deception but as *category-violation*.

Effect by stage: produces immediate Stage Two narrowing directed at the deceiving alter; in severe cases produces internal punishment (the dominant persona refuses to yield control during the deceiving alter's customary window). Does not produce eruption; produces an *internal* version of Stage Three ritualizing — repetitive interior confrontation, replayed over nights, until satisfaction.

Observable tell: external behavior becomes courtly to the point of caricature with everyone *except* the deceiving alter, who is addressed with surgical and humiliating brevity.

### Pressure Point Three — Denial of Access to a Legitimate Target

Mechanism: Brian Banner's death deprived him of the *original* object for years. The Below-Place restored it, and the response was Stage Three ritualizing for an extended period. The general principle: when the legitimate target is unreachable, the system manufactures one from the available pool. This is the most dangerous pressure point because its failure mode is *substitution* — and the moral framework that filters targets becomes elastic in proportion to the duration of denial.

Effect by stage: produces sustained Stage Two over weeks; produces Stage Three on contact with substitute; produces Stage Four if the substitute proves inadequate (i.e., the killing does not produce the closure the original would have); produces Stage Five Eruption if the substitute pool is large and contiguous (a battlefield, a city, the Hulkbuster headquarters).

Observable tell: the moral framework's brittle edge appears in *justifications* — at baseline, he does not justify his selections; under denial-of-target pressure, he begins to explain them, to himself and to others, with increasing frequency. When the Devil Hulk starts arguing his case rather than rendering verdicts, the system is already in trouble.

### Pressure Point Four — The Brian Accusation

The deepest wound and the cleanest. Mechanism: the persona is built from Brian Banner's materials — his cold, his control, his terror-as-instrument — and the entire project of the Devil Hulk is the wager that *purpose purifies origin*. To force him to look at the resemblance is to attack the wager directly. He cannot refute it; he can only refuse to dwell on it.

Effect by stage: skips intermediate stages. A single, well-placed, *believed* invocation of the resemblance produces Stage Four Bleed-Through almost immediately. Sustained or institutional invocation (a therapeutic protocol, a sequence of confrontations, an internal alter making the accusation persistently) is the most reliable known path to Stage Five Collapse-A (Recession) — he steps back, withdraws to the basement, and the cage reasserts. The accusation is functionally a *return-to-prison* command.

Observable tell: the smile vanishes. It is the only stimulus that has been recorded to remove the smile *without* eruption following. He goes very still, then very quiet, then very absent.

### Pressure Point Five — Loss of a Claimed Figure

Mechanism: the figures he has claimed (Bruce above all; Betty, Rick, Jackie, the gamma community below) are the substantive content of the protective role that justifies his existence. Their loss is not grief in the ordinary sense — he does not mourn — but it is *role-failure*, which is structurally worse for him.

Effect by stage: produces Stage Two immediately, Stage Three on identification of the responsible party, Stage Four if the responsible party is unreachable or absent. The loss of Bruce specifically — total, irrecoverable, not the nightly recession but the *end* of the host — has not been recorded in this configuration and represents the single most dangerous unknown. Best inference from the behavioral set: Collapse-B Eruption of historically unprecedented scale, given that role-failure plus loss of the central claimed figure plus the implicit invalidation of his entire purpose would collapse all five pressure points simultaneously.

Observable tell: posture and routine remain at baseline for an unsettling interval — hours to a day — after which the system reorganizes catastrophically. The delay is itself a warning sign; in normal humans, grief presents immediately, and the *absence* of immediate response indicates the system is computing rather than feeling.

---

## 6.4 The Decompensation Pattern — Internal Dynamics

What happens *inside* the system as the persona slides through the stages.

The Banner system in the Devil Hulk's operational era functions as a hierarchical executive cabinet, with the Devil Hulk holding the night shift and a kind of standing presidency over operations. Decompensation is the failure of that cabinet structure. The pattern, observable across the Ewing record:

**At Stages One and Two**, the cabinet remains intact. The Devil Hulk consults Joe Fixit on questions of street-level information and human deception; consults Savage Hulk for raw physical assessment; consults Banner for technical knowledge and historical context. The consultations are silent to outside observers but produce visible micro-pauses — half-second hesitations before speaking, slight unfocusing of the eyes — that an experienced observer can read.

**At Stage Three**, consultations cease. The persona acts unilaterally. The other alters become passive witnesses to the ritual; Banner, in particular, is *forced to watch* in a manner that the Devil Hulk explicitly frames as gift-giving but which Banner experiences as additional trauma. The internal cabinet has collapsed into a presidency; the presidency has collapsed into a high priesthood.

**At Stage Four**, the alters reassert chaotically. The Bleed-Through is not orderly succession but *intrusion*. Savage Hulk's affect surfaces because Savage Hulk is *fighting back* against having been silenced; Banner's voice surfaces because Banner has begun to seize windows of opportunity; Fixit's posture surfaces because Fixit, the system's actor, can mimic any of the others when given an opening. The Devil Hulk in Stage Four is no longer the executive; he is one voice among several, and the body's behavior reflects that contention.

**At Stage Five Collapse-A**, the cabinet structure reasserts itself by the Devil Hulk *withdrawing*. Order is restored at the cost of his operational presence. The system breathes again. This is, paradoxically, the system's *self-healing* mechanism — the Devil Hulk's deepest loyalty to Bruce expresses itself, at the limit, as retreat.

**At Stage Five Collapse-B**, the cabinet does not reassert. The body operates without executive selection of any kind. Worldbreaker capacity expresses without Worldbreaker context — that is, without the cosmic narrative framing that gave Worldbreaker meaning. The result is undifferentiated catastrophe operating on the Devil Hulk's residual targeting heuristics, which without his discipline degrade to "anyone who reads as a threat to anyone he ever claimed." The radius of this collapse, if sustained, is not estimable from the recorded data; the upper bound is what gamma physiology can deliver, which is large.

---

## 6.5 What Recovery Looks Like

Recovery from Stages One through Three is essentially automatic once the precipitating stimulus is removed; the persona returns to baseline within hours to days. Recovery from Stage Four is slower and requires what the *Immortal Hulk* record shows: explicit re-acknowledgment by Bruce of the Devil Hulk's role and necessity. This is the persona's only known *re-stabilizer*: confirmation, from the host, that he is still wanted. Recovery from Stage Five Collapse-A occurs spontaneously over weeks to months as the cage in the basement room ceases to feel like exile and begins to feel like a workshop again — the persona uses the recession as preparation, and re-emerges sharper. Recovery from Stage Five Collapse-B has not been observed and may not be possible without total system reorganization (death-and-resurrection through the Green Door, which is itself how the Ewing-era system originally came into being).

---

## 6.6 Conditions That Produce Failure — A Summary Matrix

The conditions sufficient to produce decompensation, ordered from most to least likely on the available record:

1. **Sustained accusation of resemblance to Brian Banner.** Reliable producer of Collapse-A. The system's only reliable "off-switch."
2. **Concurrent denial of legitimate target and presence of a substitute pool.** Producer of Stage Three ritualizing, Stage Four bleed-through, and at the limit Stage Five Eruption. The Hulkbuster headquarters in the early Ewing arcs sat near this configuration; restraint was the persona's choice, not the situation's.
3. **Successful integration attempt that excludes him.** Producer of slow-burn Stage Four; eventual Collapse-A as the persona accepts redundancy. The closest historical analogue is the Professor Hulk era's effect on the *concept* of the Devil Hulk before the Ewing era.
4. **Loss of Bruce.** Producer, by inference, of Collapse-B at unprecedented scale. Untested.
5. **Demonstrated internal deception by an alter the system has trusted.** Producer of focused Stage Two with internal Stage Three ritualizing. Contained; survivable for the system.
6. **Capture and torture by an external actor.** Counter-intuitively, the *least* destabilizing condition on the list. Maximum external stress produces maximum internal stillness. This is the persona at his most effective, not his most fragile.

---

## 6.7 Final Note on Decompensation Architecture

The Devil Hulk's failure modes are the inverse of the failure modes of every other Hulk persona. Savage Hulk fails by escalating into rage; Joe Fixit fails by escalating into appetite; Banner fails by escalating into terror and collapse; Professor Hulk fails by the dissolution of the compromise that constitutes him; Green Scar fails by becoming Worldbreaker. The Devil Hulk fails — when he fails — by *succeeding too completely*: by narrowing past the point where the moral filter can still operate, by ritualizing past the point of strategic flexibility, by becoming so fully what he was made to be that he forecloses any other role the system might need him to play.

The cage in the basement room in IH #13 (2000) was, in this light, not only the system's defense against him. It was the system's defense for him — the boundary that kept the persona from completing itself, from arriving fully at its own definition. The Ewing-era release of the persona from that cage was operationally necessary and personally fulfilling for the alter; it was also the first time in his existence he was exposed to the conditions under which he could fail. He has not yet failed comprehensively. The conditions for comprehensive failure are knowable, are listed above, and are — for any actor with the time and the leverage to assemble them — assemblable.

That is the dossier's most important sentence. He can be broken. The conditions are specific, are documented, and are reproducible. Whether breaking him is desirable is a separate question; this section addresses only how.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT — SUBJECT: "THE DEVIL HULK"

*Section 11 of the working file. Predictive, not retrospective. Probabilities here are analyst's estimates derived from the longitudinal behavioral record in §1 and the structural reads in §3–5. Treat as working hypotheses to be falsified against future canon, not as findings.*

---

## 11.1 The Shape of the Curve So Far

Before forecasting forward, the existing arc must be named cleanly, because the trajectory is not linear and any straight-line extrapolation will mislead.

The Devil Hulk has moved through three discrete states across his published existence:

1. **CAGED (2000–2017).** Sealed behind iron bars in the basement of Bruce's inner architecture. Verbal output minimal. Function: worst-case reserve. Activity level: near zero. He is the *threat the other Hulks define themselves against*. The system's relative health during this period is *measured by his confinement*.
2. **EXECUTIVE (2018–2021).** Released by the trauma of Bruce's death-and-resurrection. Becomes the dominant nighttime persona. Runs the Banner system as a managed enterprise. Builds and leads the gamma-mutate community. Closes the Brian Banner account. Bargains with cosmological evil. Accepts negotiated handoff at the endgame.
3. **POST-HANDOFF / DORMANT-INTEGRATED (2021–present).** Withdrawn from the front. Not destroyed, not exorcised — *retired in place*. The subsequent runs (Donny Cates' Hulk-as-spacecraft conceit, Phillip Kennedy Johnson's tenure, the Banner-as-Banner stretches) do not feature him because the system has, for now, moved its operations to a different floor of the building. He is downstairs again. The bars, however, are no longer locked.

The forward question is: **what happens the next time the system needs him, and what kind of room does he come out into?**

---

## 11.2 The Four Forward Vectors

The Devil Hulk's plausible futures cluster around four vectors, in declining order of probability. Each is described with its triggers, its likely behavioral signature, and its terminal state.

### 11.2.1 Vector A: Re-Emergence as Crisis-Executive (estimated ~45%)

The most probable future, because it is the one his structure was built for and the one canon has already rehearsed. Some external crisis — a re-incursion by the Leader; the reactivation of a successor Hulkbuster program under a non-Fortean general; the rise of a new gamma-touched antagonist; a metaphysical threat targeting Bruce specifically — exceeds the capacity of whichever Hulk currently holds the day. The Banner system, as it has done before under such pressure, will reach for the most competent available alter. He will come up the stairs.

The signature this time will differ from 2018–2021 in three specific ways:

- **Lower legitimacy threshold.** He no longer has to prove he is not the Brian-Banner-in-the-basement everyone feared. The gamma community remembers him as leadership. Jackie McGee — if she is still in play — will recognize him on sight and resume the role of chronicler. The startup costs of his executive function are gone.
- **Higher integration cost.** Precisely because he is more trusted, the other alters' resistance to him will be weaker, and the system risks letting him stay topside past the operational need. The 2018–2021 arc could end because the external threat ended. A repeat run risks a *standing* Devil Hulk regime.
- **Different opening move.** Last time he announced himself by punishing a gas-station robber as moral verdict. Next time the announcement will be quieter and more targeted — likely a single, surgical removal of a person he has *been waiting for* across the dormancy. He has had years of subjective time to build a list.

Terminal state of this vector: another negotiated handoff, but with a higher probability of failure than last time, because the system's reasons for asking him back will not be matched by equally strong reasons for asking him to leave.

### 11.2.2 Vector B: Drift into Standing Governance of the System (estimated ~25%)

The slow-motion catastrophe. No single crisis triggers him; rather, the post-2021 dormancy is interrupted by a series of smaller threats, each of which he handles, each of which marginally extends his time in the chair. The other alters defer — Savage Hulk because he was always frightened of him; Joe Fixit because Fixit respects competence and recognizes a senior operator; the Professor configuration because the Professor's own collapse history makes him reluctant to insist. Banner, exhausted, lets it happen.

This is the vector that produces the *paternal autocrat* endpoint — the Banner system functioning, externally, very well; internally, run by a single alter who has decided that his judgment is the system's judgment. The behavioral tells would be:

- Increasing daytime presence (the circadian binding loosens).
- The grin softens into a *smile* — the affect of a man comfortable in his office.
- The target set expands by category rather than by individual: not "this man hurt my boy" but "this class of person hurts boys like mine."
- The gamma community is rebuilt and run more efficiently than before, with clearer protocols, and with a quiet attrition of members who disagree.
- Bruce's voice in the system grows fainter — not suppressed, but *consulted less often*, in the manner of a founder kept on as figurehead.

Terminal state: a Hulk who is functionally indistinguishable from a benevolent strongman. Not a villain in any conventional sense. Genuinely protective. Genuinely effective. And the host's autonomy is gone.

### 11.2.3 Vector C: Genuine Integration (estimated ~20%)

The growth ending. Some combination of sustained therapeutic work (a Doc Samson redux done correctly, or a new clinician — Leonard Samson's death and resurrection notwithstanding, the *function* is what matters), the absence of a crisis that requires Devil Hulk specifically, and Bruce's own slow accumulation of the executive capacities he previously outsourced to him, results in the alter agreeing — not being forced — to fold his functions into the host.

What integration looks like for this specific alter, given his structure:

- He does not disappear; the *capacities* are retained. Bruce inherits patience, target-discipline, the ability to convert pain into intelligence, and the smile.
- The *paternal stance* is the hardest piece to dissolve. He has identified Bruce as a child for his entire existence. Integration requires him to recognize Bruce as an adult, which requires him to confront the implication that he himself was a *child's construct* — a hard demand for any alter, harder for one whose self-concept is built on being *the adult in the room*.
- The Brian Banner closure already accomplished in the Below-Place is a necessary precondition. Without that closure he cannot integrate, because his core mission is unfinished. With it, integration becomes thinkable.
- The likely pathway is *liturgical*: a long, ritualized internal scene in which he hands over his keys, names what he is, and consents to be carried inside Bruce rather than maintained as a separate room. He will require ceremony. He will not be talked out of himself in a single session.

Terminal state: a Bruce Banner who is, for the first time in his adult life, capable of being *both* dangerous and gentle in the same body without the danger requiring a separate occupant. The cost is that the Banner system loses its specialist; the gain is that Bruce stops being a tenant in his own life.

### 11.2.4 Vector D: Catastrophic Decompensation Into Brian Banner (estimated ~10%)

The worst case, and the one his entire defense structure is organized to prevent. The accusation identified in §5 as the cleanest wound — *you are Brian Banner* — is, sooner or later, going to be made by someone whose authority he cannot dismiss. Possible candidates: Betty, in a Red Harpy state where her own grievances against the Hulk system surface unfiltered; Jackie McGee, in print, in a way Bruce reads; a future child (Skaar; a hypothetical second child); or, most catastrophically, *himself*, in a moment of forced self-examination during a metaphysical event in which the Green Door is open and the One Below All or its successor agent shows him a mirror.

If the wound lands and the defense structure cracks, the cascade is fast:

- The wager that *use purifies origin* collapses.
- He cannot tolerate being the thing he was built to destroy.
- The patience and target-discipline that mark his function become indistinguishable from the cold control of the abuser.
- Without the moral framework he organized himself around, the apparatus remains and the steering goes. The result is not a more violent Hulk; it is a *quieter* one, executing the same competencies on a target set he is no longer sorting honestly.
- At extremis, he turns inward and attempts to destroy Bruce — not from hatred, but from the conviction that Bruce is better off without a protector who is Brian.

Terminal state: either the system's collapse and Bruce's death (true death, if the immortality mechanic is by then closed), or — the slightly less terrible variant — the other alters forcibly returning him to the basement and re-locking the bars, in which case the system regresses to the pre-2000 configuration but with the added scar tissue of having had to do it.

---

## 11.3 The Fork Points

The vectors above are not fated; they are selected by specific decision-points, most of which can be named in advance.

**Fork Point 1: The next external crisis large enough to require him.** This is the trigger event for Vectors A or B. If the crisis is *bounded* (a defined enemy, a defined operation, a defined end-state), Vector A. If the crisis is *diffuse* (an ongoing condition rather than an event — a chronic gamma-emergency, a long political conflict, a war of attrition), Vector B becomes far more likely, because diffuse crises do not have natural off-ramps.

**Fork Point 2: Whether Bruce undertakes sustained psychotherapeutic work between crises.** The single largest determinant of Vector C. The Devil Hulk cannot be integrated during operations; he can only be integrated during peace, and only by a clinician (or clinical surrogate — Samson, a successor, even a sufficiently disciplined Betty) who understands persecutor-protector configurations and is willing to *negotiate* rather than suppress. Suppression always fails with him; he was built in suppression.

**Fork Point 3: The status of the gamma community.** If it is intact and functional, he has somewhere to be that is not the chair at the top of the Banner system, which keeps Vector B at bay. If it is scattered, dead, or hostile to him, he will redirect his executive energy inward, accelerating Vector B.

**Fork Point 4: Whether Brian Banner stays dead.** The Below-Place arc closed the account, but in a universe with Green Doors, One Below Alls, and recurring resurrection mechanics, accounts re-open. If Brian returns in any form — as memory-construct, as cosmic echo, as something the One Below All wears — the Devil Hulk's mission re-activates and Vector A becomes near-certain, with elevated risk of Vector D depending on the form the resurrection takes.

**Fork Point 5: Bruce's own development of executive capacity.** The variable least often discussed but possibly the most important. The Devil Hulk's continued necessity is a function of Bruce's continued *insufficiency for his own protection*. Every increment of Bruce's own adulthood — every act of competent self-defense, of sustained relationship, of refusal to dissociate under stress — narrows the territory the Devil Hulk has to occupy. The integration ending is, in essence, the moment the territory shrinks to zero because Bruce has grown into it.

**Fork Point 6: The accusation.** Whether anyone with the standing to be heard names him as Brian. The clinical wisdom is that this naming, *done well*, is integrative and corresponds to Vector C; done badly — accusatorily, in public, under pressure — it corresponds to Vector D. There is no safe version of the conversation; there is only the difference between a clinician's version and an enemy's.

---

## 11.4 Open Questions the File Cannot Yet Answer

A surveillance dossier is honest about what it does not know. The following questions remain genuinely open and should be flagged for monitoring rather than guessed.

- **Is the circadian binding still operative?** The sundown-to-sunrise rule was a feature of the *Immortal Hulk* configuration. Post-handoff, it is unclear whether re-emergence would respect the old schedule or whether the alter would surface on demand. The first observed re-emergence is the diagnostic event.
- **Does he retain memory of the handoff?** If yes, his re-emergence will be marked by *continuity* — picking up where he left off, with the same agenda items. If no, the system has effectively reset him to a pre-Ewing state, and his behavior may regress toward the caged-promise posture of IH #13 (2000), with all the early-arc unpredictability that implied.
- **How does he relate to alters that did not exist during his executive period?** Any Hulk persona that has emerged since 2021 — and the post-Ewing runs have introduced new configurations — has no prior relationship with him. His default with unknown alters is *firmness*, but firmness directed at a stranger of unknown capacity is a recipe for internal conflict.
- **What is his stance on his own mortality now that the immortality mechanic has been modulated?** The Green Door's status post-Ewing is canonically ambiguous. If he can now die properly, his behavior should become *more* cautious — but his structure is so committed to outcome that a finite-life Devil Hulk may also become *more* willing to spend himself in a single decisive action.
- **The Skaar variable.** A son exists. The Devil Hulk's paternal stance toward Bruce has never been tested against an actual child Bruce is responsible for. The first time he is present in the body when Skaar is in danger will produce data that nothing in the existing file predicts.
- **Whether the system will tolerate a clinician.** Bruce's history with therapists is mixed-to-poor. The Devil Hulk's history with Doc Samson specifically is one of contempt within respect — he allowed Samson to see him, in IH #13, but on his terms. Whether he would tolerate a *new* clinician is unknown and is the rate-limiting step on Vector C.

---

## 11.5 What Pushes Him Toward Growth

Concretely, the conditions that bend his trajectory toward Vector C:

- A long peacetime in which no external crisis demands his executive function, so that his continued presence in the chair must justify itself on grounds other than necessity.
- A clinician or clinical surrogate who approaches him as a *negotiating party* rather than a symptom, who acknowledges his protective function as legitimate before asking him to surrender it, and who is willing to conduct the work in his idiom (formal, paternal, ceremonial) rather than the host's.
- Bruce's own visible accumulation of adult competencies — therapeutic, relational, occupational — that make the *child-to-be-protected* framing harder for the alter to sustain without self-deception.
- The maintenance of the gamma community as an independent entity, so that his protective drive has a legitimate outlet that is not the Banner system itself.
- A confrontation with the Brian-resemblance accusation that is delivered in private, by someone who loves him (most plausibly Betty), in a form that names the resemblance *and* the difference. He can survive being told he was built from Brian's materials if he is told in the same breath that what he built was not Brian.
- Permission to remain *available* after integration — the assurance that folding into Bruce does not mean ceasing to exist, only ceasing to be separate. He will not consent to annihilation. He may consent to becoming part of a larger thing he still recognizes as protective.

## 11.6 What Pushes Him Toward Catastrophe

The mirror list:

- A sustained, diffuse, low-grade external crisis with no natural end, which keeps him in the chair past the point at which leaving would be possible.
- Suppression-based clinical work, or any attempt to *remove* him without negotiation. Every prior attempt to suppress him has strengthened him.
- The collapse or hostile capture of the gamma community, which would force his protective drive back into the Banner system as its only outlet.
- The return of Brian Banner in any form, especially a form that requires re-killing rather than mourning.
- Bruce's regression — a relapse into the suicidality of the pre-*Immortal Hulk* state, or into a passive-helpless posture, which the alter will read as confirmation that the child still requires the bodyguard.
- A public, hostile naming of the Brian-resemblance, especially by an enemy who has done their homework. The Leader is the canonically obvious candidate; he has the analytic capacity and the malice to deliver the wound in its most damaging form.
- A theological event in which the One Below All or its successor shows him a true image of himself. Cosmological mirrors are the failure mode his defense structure cannot survive, because they bypass the moral framework he uses to sort the world and present him only with origin.

---

## 11.7 The Analyst's Best Single-Sentence Forecast

In the absence of either sustained peace or sustained therapy, and given that the Marvel publishing apparatus reliably generates the crises his structure was built for, the most probable medium-horizon outcome is **Vector A with creeping leakage into Vector B** — a re-emergence as crisis executive that is meant to be temporary and that, absent active counter-pressure from Bruce, Betty, or a clinician, gradually becomes the system's default operating mode, with Vector C remaining available as long as the gamma community is intact and Brian Banner stays buried, and Vector D held at bay only by the fact that the people best positioned to land the wound — Betty, Jackie, Bruce — also love him enough not to want to.

He is, in other words, exactly where his structure predicted he would be at this stage: downstairs, patient, listening for the footsteps that mean it is time to come back up. The file's recommendation is not that those footsteps be prevented — they cannot be, and his coming back up has, on the record, saved lives — but that someone be ready, when he does, to begin the conversation that ends with him agreeing to stay.

## Relationship Graph
### [[Robert Bruce Banner, PhD (Hulk)]]
- Fused, possessive, parental: 'my Bruce'
- Self-appointed sole competent protector; contemptuous of Banner's attempts at control
- Failure mode: if Banner successfully revokes consent or attempts forced integration, the Devil will sabotage the relationships and bodies Banner values to reassert primacy

### [[Brian Banner]]
- Originating template — the silhouette he wears
- Direct invocation of the name destabilizes him briefly
- Failure mode: every predator-class target is, perceptually, Brian wearing a different face; this guarantees both his effectiveness and his potential for category error

### [[Elizabeth "Betty" Ross (Betty Ross (Harpy / Red She-Hulk))]]
- Respected via Banner's longing and via her own remaking by violence (Red Harpy)
- Treated as peer-class rather than dependent-class
- Failure mode: if she is positioned as a threat to Banner's autonomy, respect converts to confrontation

### [[Jennifer Susan Walters (She-Hulk)]]
- Tolerated as Banner-adjacent kin; conditional protection
- Failure mode: if she sides decisively with institutional authority against Banner, she is recategorized

### [[Richard Milhouse Jones (Rick Jones)]]
- Tolerated; trust proportional to Rick's coherence
- Failure mode: Rick's instability and history of compromise (A-Bomb, possession arcs) makes him a recurring source of perceived betrayal

### Savage Hulk
- Contemptible younger sibling; the dysregulated child the Devil grew past
- Failure mode: actively suppresses; refuses integration that preserves Savage's voice

### Joe Fixit
- Contemptible; the hustler, the appetite alter
- Failure mode: views Fixit's hedonism as a security leak

### The Professor
- The rival adult alter; the integration-attempt the Devil eventually allowed
- Failure mode: tolerated only when the Devil authors the terms

### General Fortean
- Predator-class adversary; institutional cruelty incarnate
- Failure mode for Fortean-types: the Devil will accept capture and vivisection to reach the chain of command

### Dario Agger
- Predator-class adversary; corporate-paternal cruelty
- Failure mode: the Devil will accept being branded a monster on global media to complete the case

### The One Below All
- Cosmological substrate; accepted without flinching
- Failure mode: if the targeting code fractures, the Below-Place authorization makes him indiscriminate
